# Heat Trophy: gcb-trigger-migration-tier3

**Firemark:** ₣Ai
**Created:** 260222
**Retired:** 260303
**Status:** retired

## Paddock

# Paddock: gcb-trigger-migration-tier2

## Context

Migrate the Recipe Bottle build pipeline from ad-hoc `builds.create` API calls
to Cloud Build trigger-based builds. This is Tier 2 of the RBSCB Cloud Build
Roadmap, selected as MVP-required for SLSA v1.0 provenance.

### The Rubric Concept

A **Rubric** (`rbtgr_rubric`) is the composite per-vessel build definition comprising:
- **Rubric JSON** (`rbtgr_build_json`) — committed `cloudbuild.json` per vessel,
  generated from step scripts + regime pins by the stitch function
- **Rubric Trigger** (`rbtgr_vessel_trigger`) — per-vessel Cloud Build trigger resource in GCP
- **Rubric Repo** (`rbtgr_rubric_repo`) — single shared repo with per-vessel directories (what Cloud Build sees)
- **Rubric Provenance** (`rbtgr_provenance`) — SLSA v1.0 attestation auto-generated by Google
  for trigger-invoked builds

The rubric lifecycle has one user-facing operation:
- **Inscribe** (`rbtgo_rubric_inscribe`) — batch-all-vessels lifecycle command: refresh pins,
  generate all JSONs, copy all build contexts, verify committed in main repo, sync all to
  rubric repo (one clone/commit/push), ensure all triggers exist

And one existing operation adapted:
- **Dispatch** (`rbtgo_trigger_build`, revised) — execute triggers.run with zero custom
  substitution overrides; all values baked into committed JSON

There is no separate assay or enshrine operation. Inscribe handles pin refresh,
generation, verification, and trigger creation internally.

Developer Connect provides the bridge from GitHub to GCB:
- **Source Connection** (`rbtgi_source_connection`) — the Developer Connect connection
- **Source Link** (`rbtgi_source_link`) — the git repository link binding

### Key Design Decisions

- **Single rubric repo with per-vessel directories** — one shared repo (pre-created by user
  on any git hosting service) containing per-vessel directories, each with cloudbuild.json +
  Dockerfile + build context. Cloud Build sees ONLY the rubric repo via Developer Connect,
  never the main repo. This is a deliberate security boundary: the main repo (with all
  tooling, specs, regime files) is never exposed to Google. Rubric repo management is fully
  orchestrated git (inscribe handles clone/commit/push). Host-agnostic: works with GitHub,
  GitLab, Bitbucket, or any git service. PAT embedded in authenticated URL (`RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL`).
- **Zero custom substitution overrides** — all values baked into committed JSON at inscribe
  time (GAR coordinates, pins, platforms, vessel identity, inscribe timestamp in tag).
  Per-build uniqueness comes from Cloud Build built-in `$BUILD_ID`. Maximum SLSA purity.
- **Git-host-agnostic** (Developer Connect supports GitHub and GitLab; PAT-in-URL works with any host)
- **Per-vessel {rbtgr_build_json}** — master copy committed to main repo (user-reviewed),
  synced to rubric repo by inscribe
- **Inscribe timestamp in tags** — baked at inscribe time (e.g., `i20260223.143022`),
  `$BUILD_ID` prefix for per-build uniqueness. Multiple builds of same inscribed JSON
  produce distinct but related tags.
- **Pin staleness is a blocking gate** — inscribe verifies `RBRR_GCB_PINS_REFRESHED_AT`
  is less than 1 day old and dies if stale, directing the operator to refresh pins
  manually, commit, and re-run inscribe. Deliberate: inscribe never silently refreshes.
- **Separate inscribe and build commands** — inscribe updates the rubric; build dispatches.
  Build does NOT verify main repo git state (inscribe already synced rubric repo).
- **Modify existing functions, not recreate** — `zrbf_stitch_build_json()` is extended to
  emit complete trigger-compatible JSON (same inputs, fuller output). `rbf_build()` is simplified (remove
  tarball/GCS chain, add triggers.run). Step scripts (rbgjb/*.sh) are kept as source of
  truth for build logic, consumed at inscribe time.
- **Phased rollout** — rbev-busybox first, verify {rbtgr_provenance}, then migrate remaining vessels
- **Tier 1 log hygiene** folded into JSON authoring (audit during script inlining)
- **All API calls via curl/REST** — consistent with existing Foundry pattern, no gcloud/gh dependency
- **One {rbtgi_source_connection}** to the git host org; one source link to the rubric repo via Developer Connect
- **rb*-prefixed linked terms** with AXLA voicing annotations — not google-domain prefixes
  (legacy gcb_*/gar_*/gcs_*/giam_*/gcp_* cleanup deferred to ₣Aj)
- **OCI Layout Bridge pattern** survives unchanged (build/push/SBOM phase split)

### Decision Rationale

**Why GitHub (not GitLab, CSR, or SSM)?**
Evaluated four options. Cloud Source Repositories is End of Sale (June 2024) — unavailable
to new customers. Secure Source Manager requires 100-user minimum at $10/user = $1,000/month —
enterprise pricing, non-starter. GitLab was more automatable (PAT-only, no OAuth browser step)
but GitHub was chosen because the project already lives there. GitLab remains a viable
future migration if GitHub relationship deteriorates.

**Why a separate rubric repo (not main repo triggers)?**
SLSA provenance should record only the build material, not the entire project. Exposing the
main repo to Google Cloud Build is unnecessary — Cloud Build only needs the Dockerfile,
build context, and cloudbuild.json. The rubric repo provides a clean security boundary:
Google sees exactly what it needs, nothing more. The rubric repo commit hash in SLSA
provenance maps directly to the build material. Originally per-vessel mini-repos; revised
to a single rubric repo with per-vessel directories (session 4) to avoid broad PAT scopes
and enable git-host-agnostic operation.

**Why zero custom substitution overrides?**
For maximum SLSA purity. If the build is fully determined by the committed JSON at a
specific commit, the provenance chain is clean: commit → JSON → image. No runtime parameters
can influence the build. Per-build uniqueness uses Cloud Build's built-in `$BUILD_ID`
(the API resource key, guaranteed unique). The inscribe timestamp in the tag provides
human-readable context about which pin generation produced the JSON.

**Why GDC prefix for Developer Connect regime variables?**
Developer Connect is a Google service, not a GitHub concept. RBRR regime variables use
the GDC prefix (RBRR_GDC_*). The linked terms for the resources themselves use rbtgi_*
(RB-specific instances) with AXLA voicing annotations back to axig_* motifs.

**Why "Rubric"?**
The build definition per vessel needed a name. The metaphor chain is Vessel → Foundry → Ark.
A rubric is "the written instructions that tell the Foundry how to transform a vessel into
an ark." Inscribe is the natural verb for writing/updating a rubric.

### Session Decisions (2026-02-24)

**Spec-code mismatch: RBRR_GDC_REPO_LINK**
Spec correctly omits this (repo links are per-vessel, created by inscribe). Code still has it
in `rbrr.env`, `rbrr_regime.sh`, `rbgm_ManualProcedures.sh`. ₢AiAAR will remove from code.

**RBRR_GCB_TRIGGER_PATTERN demoted to RBGC constant**
No justification for per-installation configurability. Trigger naming is deterministic from
a constant prefix + vessel sigil. Demote to `RBGC_RUBRIC_TRIGGER_PREFIX` in `rbgc_Constants.sh`.
Remove `RBRR_GCB_TRIGGER_PATTERN` from `rbrr.env`, regime enrollment, and validation.

**rbgjb/*.sh: flat bash source material, consumed at inscribe time**
Step scripts stay as editable flat bash files — never deleted. Inscribe reads them, inlines
their content into JSON `args` arrays. All `_RBGY_*` values baked into the JSON
`substitutions` object at inscribe time. Zero dispatch-time substitution overrides.
Cloud Build resolves `_RBGY_*` from the committed JSON, not from triggers.run request.
Rationale: flat bash is easier for both humans and models to edit than config-embedded scripts.

**Bake main repo AND rubric repo metadata into JSON substitutions**
Inscribe captures at inscribe time and bakes into `substitutions` object:
- `_RBGY_GIT_COMMIT`, `_RBGY_GIT_BRANCH`, `_RBGY_GIT_REPO` — main repo (as today)
- `_RBGY_RUBRIC_REPO`, `_RBGY_RUBRIC_COMMIT` — rubric repo URL and HEAD after push
- `_RBGY_INSCRIBE_TIMESTAMP` — inscribe timestamp for tag construction
`rbgjb10-assemble-metadata.sh` picks these up unchanged; `build_info.json` extended with
rubric repo facts and inscribe timestamp.

**Dual-timestamp consecration tag format**
Format: `i{date}_{time}-b{date}_{time}-{suffix}`
Example: `i20260224_153022-b20260224_160530-image`
- Inscribe timestamp prefix (`iYYYYMMDD_HHMMSS`) — baked as `_RBGY_INSCRIBE_TIMESTAMP`
- Build timestamp (`bYYYYMMDD_HHMMSS`) — derived at build time by `rbgjb01`
- Hyphen delimits major concepts (inscribe, build, suffix); underscore within timestamps
- No dependency on undocumented BUILD_ID format
- Multiple builds of same inscribed JSON sort together by inscribe prefix
- `rbgjb01` modified to: `TAG_BASE="${_RBGY_INSCRIBE_TIMESTAMP}-b$(date -u +%Y%m%d_%H%M%S)"`
- Consecration = full tag base (both timestamps)

### Session Decisions (2026-02-24, session 2)

**gcloud is not available on the platform**
The `rbgm_gdc_establish()` guide was fundamentally wrong — it used gcloud commands throughout.
The platform does not have gcloud installed and it is not on the approved tools list. All GCP
operations must use curl/REST, consistent with the existing Foundry pattern.

**Most of Developer Connect setup is automatable**
API enablement, connection creation, and status polling are all REST API calls. The ONLY
human-interactive step is opening the OAuth authorization URI in a browser and clicking
Authorize on the GitHub app consent page. This is one-time per GitHub org.

**Developer Connect OAuth belongs at payor/depot level**
It's org-level infrastructure, like billing account setup. Connection creation moves into
`rbgp_depot_create()` (automated). OAuth completion moves into a new `rbgm_depot_initialize()`
(human-guided with orchestration).

**GitHub PAT needed for rubric operations — `RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT`**
Rubric mini-repo management requires GitHub PAT: create repos via REST API, git clone, push.
Cloud Build does NOT need the PAT (uses Developer Connect). The PAT is local-only.
Added as an optional field in the RBRA regime. Both Governor and Director populate it
(see session 3 decisions). Name: `RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT` (not `RBRA_GITHUB_PAT`).
**SUPERSEDED by session 4**: replaced by `RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL` (authenticated git URL).

**`rbgm_gdc_establish()` replaced by depot_create + depot_initialize**
The standalone manual guide is deleted. Its responsibilities split:
- Automated: API enablement + connection creation → `rbgp_depot_create()`
- Human-guided: PAT validation + OAuth browser step → `rbgm_depot_initialize()`

**`rbgm_depot_initialize()` must be idempotent**
Safe to re-run. Skips steps already complete (PAT already valid, connection already COMPLETE).

**Will delete and recreate depot for testing**
No history-adaptive steps. Test against a fresh depot created with the updated `rbgp_depot_create()`.

**₢AiAAN scope: remove builds.create path only**
Keep `rbgjb/*.sh` (inscribe source material). Only remove: builds.create submission functions,
GCS tarball chain, JSON build request assembly, tarball temp variables from kindle.

### Session Decisions (2026-02-24, session 3)

**RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT lives in both Governor and Director RBRA**
In multi-person orgs, Governor and Director may be different people on different machines.
Governor needs the PAT during depot setup (depot_initialize) and as a gate before creating
roles (create_retriever, create_director). Director needs the PAT for inscribe operations
(mini-repo management). These may be different PATs with different scopes. RBRA regime
already accepts PAT as optional in any RBRA file.

**depot_initialize sources Governor RBRA (not Director)**
Director SA doesn't exist at depot setup time — it's created later by create_director.
Fixed: depot_initialize now sources RBRR_GOVERNOR_RBRA_FILE. PAT is configured in
Governor RBRA before running depot_initialize.

**Two atomic rubric check routines, no wrapper**
`rbgu_check_rubric_pat(pat)` and `rbgu_check_devconnect(token, project, region, conn)`
live in rbgu_Utility.sh. Both are buc_die gates — succeed or die, no side effects.
Governor's create_retriever and create_director call both via `zrbgg_rubric_preflight()`.
Inscribe (future) calls only PAT check via Director RBRA. No standalone preflight command.

**rbgg_cli.sh BCG sourcing violation fixed**
Top-level sources moved into furnish (only buc_command.sh at top level per BCG pattern).
This fixed a pre-existing "rbrr multiply sourced" error that blocked all Governor commands.

### Session Decisions (2026-02-24, session 4)

**Single rubric repo replaces per-vessel mini-repos**
The per-vessel mini-repo model required GitHub PATs with "All repositories" or
"Administration: Read and write" permissions — overly broad for rubric needs. GitHub
fine-grained PATs cannot scope to "repos matching a pattern" or "repos not yet created."

New model: one pre-created rubric repo with per-vessel directories. The user creates the
repo manually on their preferred git hosting service. Inscribe writes per-vessel
directories (cloudbuild.json + Dockerfile + context), commits, and pushes.

**`RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL` replaces `RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT`**
The authenticated URL embeds the credential:
`https://x-access-token:<PAT>@github.com/org/rb-rubric.git`
This is host-agnostic — works identically for GitHub, GitLab, Bitbucket, Gitea, any git
host. No host-specific REST API calls needed. Inscribe does pure git operations
(clone, commit, push). PAT validation becomes `git ls-remote "${RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL}"`.

The PAT only needs Contents:write on a single pre-existing repo — minimal scope.

**What changes:**
- Drop `RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT` from RBRA regime enrollment and validation
- Add `RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL` (optional, 0-512 chars) to RBRA regime
- `rbtoe_check_rubric_pat` → replaced by `git ls-remote` validation on the URL
- `rbgm_depot_initialize` guide: simplified to "create a repo, create a PAT with
  Contents:write on that repo, provide the authenticated URL"
- `zrbgg_rubric_preflight()` updated to check URL reachability instead of PAT format
- Inscribe: clone URL, write per-vessel directory, commit, push (no repo creation API)
- Developer Connect source link: points to the single rubric repo (not per-vessel repos)

**What this enables (future):**
- Users can use GitLab, Bitbucket, or any git hosting service
- No host-specific API dependencies in the toolchain
- Single PAT with minimal scope (Contents:write on one repo)

**depot_create: region read from RBRR_GCP_REGION**
No longer an argument — the regime already has it. One less thing to type wrong.

**BUK improvements landed during live testing:**
- `buc_require`: reusable confirmation gate with `BURE_CONFIRM=skip` bypass
- `buc_bare`: unprefixed cyan text for typeable guidance
- `buc_next`: tabtarget hint resolving colophon to filename
- `burd_regime.sh` missing from `rbgp_cli.sh` and `rbgm_cli.sh` furnish (caused
  zburd_sentinel command-not-found after exec boundary)
- `rbra_regime.sh`: missing `:-` default on optional `RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT` check
- Payor tabtarget renames (rbw-pCD, rbw-pDD, rbw-pRG, rbw-pip) + zipper colophon updates

### Session Decisions (2026-02-24, session 5)

**JSON elected for Cloud Build config — no YAML, no backtracking**
The Cloud Build REST API (`projects.builds.create`, `projects.triggers.run`) is natively JSON.
YAML is an authoring convenience parsed into the same `Build` resource. Both formats work
equivalently with triggers, SLSA v1.0 provenance, and all Cloud Build features. No deprecation
signals through Feb 2026 release notes. The existing `zrbf_stitch_build_json()` already
generates JSON via jq — converting to YAML adds complexity with zero functional benefit.
Trade study RBSCJ-CloudBuildJson.adoc authored with full evidence chain.

Key sources:
- Build config file schema: "YAML or JSON syntax" (equivalent serializations of Build resource)
- REST API: JSON wire format; CLI converts any config to JSON for submission
- Trigger autodetect precedence: cloudbuild.yaml, cloudbuild.yml, cloudbuild.json, Dockerfile

**`rbtgr_build_yaml` renamed to `rbtgr_build_json`**
Linked term, attribute mapping, definition, display text, and all references across RBS0,
RBSRI updated. The term was "yaml" only because Google's docs default to YAML examples —
the project's actual generation path was always JSON via jq.

**Hand-authored `rbev-busybox/cloudbuild.yaml` deleted**
The prototype was created in ₢AiAAD to establish the target format. That purpose is served.
The stitch function is the source of truth — `cloudbuild.json` will be generated output, not
hand-crafted input. The inscribe flow (RBSRI) generates → operator reviews and commits →
inscribe on re-run verifies match. Converting one hand-authored prototype to another is wasted work.

**Duplicate RBSCB include in RBS0 fixed**
Lines 3089-3100 had the Cloud Build Roadmap included twice (once as a trade study subsection,
once as a standalone top-level section). The duplicate top-level section was replaced with
the new RBSCJ Cloud Build JSON trade study.

### Constraints

**Build context scope**: With rubric repo triggers, Cloud Build checks out only the rubric repo
(Dockerfile + build context + cloudbuild.json). The main repo is never exposed.

**Developer Connect setup**: One-time per GitHub org. Connection creation is automated in
`rbgp_depot_create()` (left in PENDING state). The human completes the GitHub OAuth
authorization via `rbgm_depot_initialize()` (open browser, click Authorize). Subsequent
trigger operations are fully automated via REST API.

**Rubric repo credential**: `RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL` is an authenticated git URL
(PAT embedded) in RBRA. Governor needs it at depot_initialize time and as a preflight
gate. Director needs it for inscribe. Cloud Build does NOT need it (uses Developer Connect).
Host-agnostic: works with any git hosting service.

**No gcloud dependency**: All GCP operations use curl/REST. The platform does not have
gcloud installed. All git operations use authenticated URLs (PAT-in-URL).

### What Dies

- `builds.create` API path and JSON build request composition
- GCS tarball upload chain (package, compose name, upload)
- `zrbf_compose_build_request_json()` and `zrbf_submit_build_json()`
- Runtime stitching from the build hot path (stitch is now at inscribe time, not build time)
- The `$$` dollar-escaping dance for Cloud Build substitutions
- Dispatch-time `_RBGY_*` substitution overrides (values now baked in committed JSON)
- Courier credential regime concept (replaced by RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL + Developer Connect)
- `RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT` — replaced by `RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL` (host-agnostic)
- `rbtoe_check_rubric_pat` — replaced by `git ls-remote` validation
- Per-vessel mini-repo creation and management
- `rbgm_gdc_establish()` standalone manual guide and `tt/rbw-gge.GdcEstablishment.sh`

### What Survives (modified)

- `zrbf_stitch_build_json()` → extended to emit complete trigger-compatible JSON (same inputs, fuller output)
- `rbf_build()` → simplified to trigger dispatch (remove tarball/GCS/JSON chain)
- `zrbf_wait_build_completion()` → polling logic unchanged
- `zrbf_load_vessel()` → unchanged
- `rbgjb/*.sh` step scripts — still the source of truth, consumed at inscribe time
- `rbrr_refresh_gcb_pins` → writes RBRR_GCB_PINS_REFRESHED_AT timestamp, called by inscribe (rate-limited) or standalone

### What's Born

- {rbtgr_rubric} — per-vessel build definition (cloudbuild.json + trigger + rubric repo directory + provenance)
- {rbtgr_rubric_repo} — single shared rubric repo with per-vessel directories (security boundary)
- {rbtgi_source_connection} — Developer Connect connection (OAuth GitHub App)
- {rbtgo_rubric_inscribe} — batch-all-vessels command (pin refresh → generate all → copy all contexts → verify committed → sync rubric repo → ensure triggers)
- Inscribe tabtarget + rubric repo management orchestration
- AXLA motifs: axig_developer_connect, axig_build_trigger, axig_repo_link, axig_build_config, axig_slsa_provenance
- `RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL` — optional RBRA field, authenticated git URL for rubric repo (host-agnostic)
- `rbgm_depot_initialize()` — human procedure: validate rubric repo URL, guide Developer Connect OAuth, verify
- Developer Connect connection creation step in `rbgp_depot_create()` (automated, PENDING state)

### Vessel Modes

Currently implementing conjure mode only. Repo structure designed to accommodate:
- **Conjure**: {rbtgr_build_json} + Dockerfile + context (build from scratch)
- **Mirror**: {rbtgr_build_json} + manifest (pull public, push to GAR) — future
- **Local push**: {rbtgr_build_json} + OCI tarball reference — future

## Build Requirements

This heat is primarily bash/GCP tooling (RBW). No Rust builds required for most paces.
BCG compliance is mandatory for all new bash code — enterprise-grade orchestration.

### Session Decisions (2026-02-25)

**Inscribe batches all vessels in one rubric repo commit.**
With a single rubric repo, there is no reason to inscribe per-vessel. Inscribe becomes:
refresh pins → generate all cloudbuild.json files → copy all build contexts (Dockerfile + context
per vessel directory) → one rubric repo clone/commit/push → ensure all triggers exist.
One command, one rubric repo commit, one main-repo commit to review. This eliminates the
per-vessel inscribe ceremony and the temporal gap between vessel updates.

**Pin staleness is a blocking gate in inscribe.**
Inscribe verifies `RBRR_GCB_PINS_REFRESHED_AT` is less than 1 day old (shortened
from 2 days). If stale, inscribe dies with guidance to run pin refresh manually,
commit, and re-run. Deliberate design: inscribe never silently refreshes — the
operator sees and commits pin updates explicitly. The standalone
`rbrr_refresh_gcb_pins` command remains callable for manual inspection.
`RBRR_GCB_PINS_REFRESHED_AT` survives as a staleness timestamp, written by pin
refresh on success.

**Build context explicitly copied to rubric repo.**
Each vessel's Dockerfile and build context directory are copied to the per-vessel directory
in the rubric repo at inscribe time. This makes the rubric repo commit a complete snapshot
of all build material. Clear step in the inscribe flow, not implicit.

**SLSA v1.0 does not require base image digest pinning.**
Verified against slsa.dev/spec/v1.0/requirements. SLSA v1.0 Build L1-L3 requires provenance
existence, builder-generated provenance, and hardened build platform. It does NOT require
hermetic builds, input pinning, or base image digest validation. Dockerfile base image pinning
is deferred to a separate future heat — a policy decision for vessel authors, not a trigger
migration prerequisite.

**Tier 3 (Private Pools) folded into this heat.**
Private Pool pricing is essentially identical to default pool pricing (~$0.003/vCPU-min,
1.0-1.13x ratio depending on region, as of Nov 2025 repricing). The stitch function is
already being modified for Tier 2, so adding conditional `options.pool.name` is minimal
incremental work. Two paces added: depot lifecycle (create/destroy pool) and build JSON
wiring (conditional pool reference, machine type expansion).

**RBSCB roadmap reconciliation deferred to end of heat.**
The roadmap document has accumulated contradictions between tier body text and decision log
entries. A reconciliation pace (₢AiAAd) will re-read the document fresh after all implementation
paces land and rewrite it as a coherent plan — eliminating the decision log in favor of
authoritative tier descriptions.

### Session Decisions (2026-03-01) — CB v2 Connection Research

**Developer Connect replaced by Cloud Build v2 connections — separate GitHub App.**
CB v2 connections use the "Google Cloud Build" GitHub App (github.com/apps/google-cloud-build),
which is entirely separate from the Developer Connect GitHub App. A new GitHub App installation
is required. The existing Developer Connect connection cannot be reused.

**CB v2 connection creation is fully programmatic (no browser OAuth consent).**
Unlike Developer Connect (which required a browser-based OAuth authorization flow), CB v2
connections can be created entirely via REST API when an existing GitHub App installation ID
and classic PAT are provided. Google's docs confirm: "When using an existing token and
installation ID to create a connection, no manual intervention using a web browser is required."
The one-time browser steps are: (1) install the Google Cloud Build GitHub App on the org,
(2) generate a classic PAT with `repo`, `read:user`, `read:org` scopes.

**CB v2 connection REST API:**
```
POST cloudbuild.googleapis.com/v2/projects/{p}/locations/{r}/connections?connectionId={id}
Body: {
  "githubConfig": {
    "authorizerCredential": {
      "oauthTokenSecretVersion": "projects/P/secrets/S/versions/1"
    },
    "appInstallationId": "INSTALLATION_ID"
  }
}
```
The PAT is stored in Secret Manager; the API references the secret version.
Returns a long-running operation. Connection goes through stages:
PENDING_CREATE_APP → PENDING_USER_OAUTH → PENDING_INSTALL_APP → COMPLETE.

**CB v2 repository creation REST API:**
```
POST cloudbuild.googleapis.com/v2/projects/{p}/locations/{r}/connections/{c}/repositories?repositoryId={id}
Body: { "remoteUri": "https://github.com/org/repo.git" }
```
The `remoteUri` is a plain HTTPS URL (no embedded credentials). Authentication is
handled by the parent connection's Secret Manager reference. CB v2 auto-creates a
GitHub webhook on the repository.

**IAM: `roles/cloudbuild.connectionAdmin` for connection CRUD.**
Grants `cloudbuild.connections.create/get/list/update/delete` and
`cloudbuild.repositories.create/get/list/delete`. This is a new role not
previously used in the depot lifecycle.

**Same Cloud Build service agent, needs Secret Manager access.**
The service agent `service-{PN}@gcp-sa-cloudbuild.iam.gserviceaccount.com` is the
same one already provisioned when Cloud Build API is enabled. During connection
setup, it needs `roles/secretmanager.admin` (can be scoped down to
`roles/secretmanager.secretAccessor` on the specific secret after COMPLETE).

**RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL coexists with CB v2 connection.**
Two separate credential paths:
- `RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL` (PAT-in-URL): used by inscribe for git clone/commit/push
  to the rubric repo. Local git operations only.
- CB v2 connection (PAT in Secret Manager + GitHub App): used by Cloud Build triggers
  for source checkout. The `remoteUri` on the CB v2 repository is the plain URL
  (no credentials). These can use the same PAT or different PATs.

**Fine-grained PATs NOT supported for CB v2 connections.**
Google Issue Tracker #343223837 confirms: fine-grained tokens cause
"the user token does not have access to installations". Classic PATs required
with `repo`, `read:user`, `read:org` scopes.

**Trigger repositoryEventConfig references CB v2 repository:**
```json
{
  "repositoryEventConfig": {
    "repository": "projects/P/locations/R/connections/C/repositories/REPO_ID",
    "push": { "branch": "^main$" }
  }
}
```

**Regime variable plan:**
- `RBRR_GDC_CONNECTION_NAME` → rename to `RBRR_CBV2_CONNECTION_NAME`
- `RBRR_GDC_REGION` → rename to `RBRR_CBV2_REGION` (or reuse `RBGD_GCB_REGION`
  since CB v2 region must match trigger region, which already equals GCB region)
- New: Secret Manager secret name for the GitHub PAT (used by CB v2 connection)
- New: GitHub App installation ID (used by CB v2 connection creation)
- Delete: all `developerconnect.googleapis.com` API references
- Delete: Developer Connect API enablement from depot_create

**What replaces what in depot_create:**
- Delete: `developerconnect.googleapis.com` API enable
- Delete: Developer Connect connection creation (POST .../connections)
- Add: `secretmanager.googleapis.com` API enable (if not already)
- Add: Store PAT in Secret Manager
- Add: Grant service agent Secret Manager access
- Add: CB v2 connection creation (POST cloudbuild.googleapis.com/v2/.../connections)
- Add: CB v2 repository creation (POST .../connections/{c}/repositories)

**What replaces what in depot_initialize:**
- Delete: Developer Connect OAuth browser flow (installAuthorizationUri)
- Delete: Console IAM grant for Developer Connect OAuth
- Simplify: CB v2 connection with existing App installation + PAT is fully programmatic
- The rubric repo URL validation (git ls-remote) survives unchanged
- The one-time browser step (install Google Cloud Build GitHub App) becomes part of
  a setup guide, not the depot_initialize flow

**What replaces what in inscribe (rbf_Foundry.sh):**
- Delete: Developer Connect source link (gitRepositoryLinks) creation/check
- Add: CB v2 repository check (already created by depot_create)
- Trigger creation body: use `repositoryEventConfig.repository` (CB v2 path)
  instead of Developer Connect source link reference

**Sources:**
- CB v2 connections API: https://cloud.google.com/build/docs/api/reference/rest/v2/projects.locations.connections
- CB v2 repositories API: https://cloud.google.com/build/docs/api/reference/rest/v2/projects.locations.connections.repositories
- Connect repo (2nd gen): https://cloud.google.com/build/docs/automating-builds/github/connect-repo-github?generation=2nd-gen
- IAM roles: https://cloud.google.com/build/docs/iam-roles-permissions
- Fine-grained PAT limitation: https://issuetracker.google.com/issues/343223837
- Google Cloud Build GitHub App: https://github.com/apps/google-cloud-build

### Session Decisions (2026-03-02) — CB v2 Architecture Decisions

**SUPERSEDES** portions of the CB v2 research section above. Where conflicts exist,
this section is authoritative.

**depot_initialize is dead.**
CB v2 connection creation is fully programmatic when GitHub App installation and PAT
are pre-existing. The Developer Connect OAuth browser flow was the sole reason
depot_initialize existed. With CB v2, all connection setup is automated in depot_create.
Delete: `rbgm_depot_initialize()`, spec RBSDN, tabtarget `rbw-gdi`, all "Next:
depot_initialize" guidance. The rubric repo URL validation (formerly in depot_initialize)
moves to depot_create.

**One classic PAT for everything.**
A single GitHub classic PAT (scopes: `repo`, `read:user`, `read:org`) serves both
Cloud Build triggers (via Secret Manager) and local inscribe git operations (fetched
at runtime). No fine-grained PAT option — CB v2 requires classic PATs.

**PAT lives only in Secret Manager — never on disk.**
The PAT enters the system once via stdin during depot_create, goes directly into
Secret Manager, and is never stored in regime files, RBRA files, or any persistent
local file. Inscribe fetches it from Secret Manager at runtime, constructs the
authenticated git URL in memory, uses it, discards it.

**RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL is dead.**
The old PAT-embedded URL in RBRA files is eliminated. No credentials in RBRA.
No credentials in regime. The PAT has exactly one home: Secret Manager.

**RBRR_RUBRIC_REPO_URL — new, plain URL, required regime variable.**
`RBRR_RUBRIC_REPO_URL=https://github.com/org/rb-rubric.git` — no credentials.
Infrastructure config identifying which repo is the rubric repo. Operator sets it
in rbrr.env before running depot_create. depot_create validates it (git ls-remote
using the PAT from stdin). Inscribe reads it to construct the authenticated URL
at runtime (combining with PAT fetched from Secret Manager).

**GitHub App installation ID is ephemeral — not stored in regime.**
The operator provides the installation ID via stdin to depot_create alongside the PAT.
It's baked into the CB v2 connection resource and never stored in regime or RBRA.
If the connection is destroyed and recreated, the operator provides it again.

**depot_create stdin input: PAT + installation ID.**
Two values via stdin (avoids shell history and `ps` visibility). depot_create:
1. Reads PAT and installation ID from stdin
2. Validates rubric repo URL from regime using PAT (git ls-remote)
3. Enables `secretmanager.googleapis.com` API
4. Creates Secret Manager secret, stores PAT
5. Grants Cloud Build service agent `secretAccessor` on the secret
6. Creates CB v2 connection (referencing secret version + installation ID)
7. Creates CB v2 repository (referencing `RBRR_RUBRIC_REPO_URL`)

If PAT is not provided, depot_create displays inline guide (GitHub-focused with
note that other git hosts work) and dies with "provide credentials via stdin and
re-run." Guide covers: install Google Cloud Build GitHub App, create classic PAT,
provide both values.

**RBRR_GDC_REGION is dead — redundant.**
CB v2 region must match trigger region, which already equals `RBGD_GCB_REGION`.
No separate regime variable needed. All CB v2 API calls use `RBGD_GCB_REGION`.

**Regime variable changes (complete):**
- `RBRR_GDC_CONNECTION_NAME` → `RBRR_CBV2_CONNECTION_NAME` (rename)
- `RBRR_GDC_REGION` → delete (use `RBGD_GCB_REGION`)
- `RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL` → delete (PAT-in-URL pattern eliminated)
- New: `RBRR_RUBRIC_REPO_URL` (plain URL, no credentials, in rbrr.env)

**Constants (new in rbgc_Constants.sh):**
- `RBGC_CBV2_PAT_SECRET_NAME` = `rb-github-pat` — Secret Manager secret name
  (internal to depot project, no cross-depot visibility)
- `RBGC_CBV2_REPOSITORY_ID` = `rubric` — CB v2 repository local identifier
  within the connection (one rubric repo per depot)

**Director SA gets Secret Manager access during create_director.**
`rbgg_create_director` grants `roles/secretmanager.secretAccessor` on the
PAT secret to the Director SA. This enables inscribe to fetch the PAT at runtime.

**depot_destroy deletes CB v2 resources.**
depot_destroy deletes: CB v2 repository, CB v2 connection, Secret Manager secret.
Tolerates 404 (already gone) for idempotency.

**Git host dependency is acknowledged but not abstracted.**
CB v2 connection config is host-specific (`githubConfig` vs `gitlabConfig`).
The code is GitHub-focused (the project uses GitHub). The inline guide in
depot_create references GitHub but notes other hosts are possible. A future
host migration would swap the connection config shape — the architecture
(Secret Manager + CB v2 connection + repository) is host-portable.

| 4 | ₢AiAAN | remove-builds-create-path | Delete builds.create code path from Foundry |
| 5 | ₢AiAA0 | e2e-verify-cbv2-provenance | Full e2e: destroy → create → inscribe → dispatch → provenance |

### Session Decisions (2026-03-03) — E2E Dispatch Findings

**Three blocking issues discovered during first E2E dispatch (demo1015 depot):**

1. **CB v2 service agent needs Secret Manager access for repository fetch.**
   Cloud Build's service agent (`service-{PN}@gcp-sa-cloudbuild.iam.gserviceaccount.com`)
   needs `secretmanager.secretAccessor` on the GitLab API token secret to authenticate
   when fetching commits from the rubric repo. `depot_create` already grants this, but
   `create_director` overwrote it (see #2). Symptom: `triggers.run` returns HTTP 400
   "Couldn't read commit".

2. **IAM read-modify-write race destroys bindings (secret AND GAR repo).**
   `create_director` reads IAM policies, adds its own binding, and writes back.
   If the read returns stale data (IAM eventual consistency — 200 but missing
   bindings set by `depot_create`), the write overwrites them. This is NOT a
   timing/retry issue — stale 200 is indistinguishable from fresh 200.
   Affected resources: Secret Manager (CB service agent `secretAccessor` lost)
   and GAR repository (Mason `writer` lost).
   **Fix (₢AiABD):** Every `setIamPolicy` writes the complete expected binding set.
   One path, one write, always correct.
   **Interim fix applied:** Silent vanilla-json fallbacks in `rbgp_Payor.sh` and
   `rbgg_Governor.sh` replaced with die-on-failure. This prevents the worst case
   (empty policy overwrite) but does not prevent stale-read overwrites.

3. **Push triggers fire on inscribe push — unintended 7-build burst.**
   Triggers configured with `push: { branch: "^main$" }` fire automatically when
   inscribe pushes to the rubric repo. All 7 vessel triggers fire simultaneously.
   **Fix (₢AiABC):** Remove push filter; triggers become manual-dispatch-only
   via `triggers.run`. Matches the zero-override design philosophy.

**Build step `dir` field was missing from stitched JSON.**
`zrbf_stitch_build_json` emitted steps without a `dir` field. When Cloud Build
checks out the rubric repo (per-vessel subdirectories), the working directory
defaults to `/workspace` (repo root). Dockerfile and build context are in
`{vessel}/` subdirectory. Fix: add `dir: $moniker` to every stitched step.
Regenerated all 7 `cloudbuild.json` files.

**Syft SBOM step fails on multi-platform OCI layout.**
`oci-dir:/workspace/oci-layout` contains a multi-platform index manifest
(`application/vnd.oci.image.index.v1+json`). Syft's `oci-dir:` transport
doesn't support index manifests (anchore/syft#1545). Steps 4-5 (build + push)
succeed; step 6 (SBOM) fails. Research in progress on alternatives:
local analysis with platform selection, registry-based analysis, or alternative
SBOM tools. May require changes to the OCI Layout Bridge pattern.

**E2E pace (₢AiAA0) scope revised.**
Original scope assumed a clean run from fresh depot. Actual experience revealed
infrastructure bugs that require code fixes before a clean run is possible.
The remaining E2E verification requires: fix push triggers (₢AiABC), fix IAM
assertions (₢AiABD), resolve Syft multi-platform issue, then re-run from
depot destroy. Reslated to reflect this dependency chain.

### Pace Plan Update (2026-03-03)

| Order | Coronet | Silks | Scope |
|-------|---------|-------|-------|
| next | ₢AiABC | fix-trigger-push-filter-removes-auto-fire | Remove push filter from triggers |
| next | ₢AiABD | fix-iam-policy-declarative-assertions | Complete policy construction in create_director |

### Session Decision: Unmatchable push filter for manual-dispatch-only triggers (2026-03-03)

Triggers were configured with `push: { branch: "^main$" }` in `repositoryEventConfig`.
When inscribe pushes to the rubric repo's main branch, all 7 vessel triggers fire
automatically. This is unintended — builds should only dispatch via explicit `triggers.run`
calls from `rbf_build`. Changed push filter to `^MANUAL-DISPATCH-ONLY$` (unmatchable
branch name) rather than removing `push` entirely, because `repositoryEventConfig`
requires a `push` or `pullRequest` filter (union field per API docs). The alternative
(`sourceToBuild` for true manual triggers) would change the trigger structure significantly
and require live API testing — deferred. The unmatchable pattern is self-documenting and
preserves the existing dispatch path unchanged.
| then | ₢AiAA0 | e2e-verify-cbv2-provenance | Full e2e re-run from depot destroy (depends on ₢AiABC + ₢AiABD + Syft resolution) |

### Session Decision: Complete-policy-write pattern for IAM (2026-03-03)

**Problem:** `create_director` does read-modify-write on IAM policies for secrets and GAR
repo, adding only its own bindings. If `getIamPolicy` returns stale data (IAM eventual
consistency returns 200 with missing bindings), the `setIamPolicy` overwrites bindings set
by `depot_create`. Affected: CB service agent `secretAccessor` on secret, Mason `writer`
on GAR repo.

**Fix:** Every `setIamPolicy` in `create_director` writes the complete expected binding set.
Two `rbgu_jq_add_member_to_role_capture` calls chained via intermediate temp file, then one
`setIamPolicy`. No conditional branches based on what the read returned — one path, always
correct.

**Secret IAM:** Director `secretAccessor` + CB service agent `secretAccessor`
(email derived from `z_project_number` already fetched in create_director).

**GAR repo IAM:** Director `repoAdmin` + Mason `writer` (email from `RBGD_MASON_EMAIL`).
Replaced `rbgi_add_repo_iam_role` with inline read-modify-write to chain both bindings
before the single set. Propagation retry preserved (inline, same exponential backoff pattern).

### Session Decision: Secret sanitization audit and stdin pipe (2026-03-03)

**Audit:** Comprehensive review of `rbgu_Utility.sh`, `rbf_Foundry.sh`, `rbgp_Payor.sh`,
`rbgg_Governor.sh` for secret leakage into transcripts and logs.

**Finding:** Bearer tokens, OAuth tokens, and PAT values do NOT appear in transcript files.
`curl -sS` (no verbose), `buc_log_args` never passed token values, OAuth token stays in
memory. The code already follows BCG discipline for in-memory secret handling.

**One violation found:** `rbgp_Payor.sh` `depot_create` wrote base64-encoded GitLab tokens
to temp files (`rbgp_secret_version_*.json`) for Secret Manager `addVersion` API calls.
These persist in `BURD_TEMP_DIR` (never auto-cleaned). Token is valid up to 30 days (GitLab
project access token lifetime).

**Fix:** BCG says "Secrets use `_capture` functions, never temp files." Applied the same
principle to HTTP request bodies: pipe secret payload via stdin using `jq | rbgu_http_json
... "-"`. `rbgu_http_json` already uses `-d @"${body_file}"` — passing `-` as body file
yields `-d @-` (curl stdin convention). Secret never touches filesystem. No changes to
`rbgu_http_json` needed.

**Specs (RBS0, RBSDC):** No changes needed — specs describe what data goes to the API,
not how the body is transmitted. The stdin pipe is an implementation improvement.

### Session Decision: Mason tokenCreator grant audit (2026-03-03)

**Audit of `roles/iam.serviceAccountTokenCreator` granted to CB service agent on Mason SA.**

**Finding: KEEP.** The grant is required by the OCI Layout Bridge pattern. Build steps
execute as Mason (via trigger `serviceAccount` field = actAs). Those steps need to
authenticate to GCP APIs (GAR docker login, crane push), which requires generating fresh
access tokens. The CB service agent's `tokenCreator` role enables this token generation.

**Two distinct impersonation relationships:**
- **Director → Mason**: `serviceAccountUser` (actAs) — Director submits builds that run as Mason
- **CB service agent → Mason**: `tokenCreator` — build steps running as Mason can mint tokens

RBSCIP-IamPropagation.adoc already preserves this grant with rationale. Updated RBSDC
NOTE to clearly explain the distinction between tokenCreator and serviceAccountUser.

## Paces

### spec-replace-impersonation-gate-with-connection-retry (₢AiAA-) [complete]

**[260303-1450] complete**

Rewrite RBSCIP and update RBSDC to replace the impersonation readiness gate
with Pattern B: connection-creation-as-probe with retry/backoff.

## Background

Two Cloud Build service accounts exist in every depot project:
- **Default build SA**: `{PN}@cloudbuild.gserviceaccount.com` — executes builds
- **Cloud Build Service Agent**: `service-{PN}@gcp-sa-cloudbuild.iam.gserviceaccount.com` — manages CB v2 connections, reads secrets for connection config

The impersonation readiness gate impersonated the wrong one (the default build
SA) and relied on a permission (generateAccessToken) that roles/owner does not
grant. Pattern B eliminates impersonation entirely.

## Rationale (record in RBSCIP rewrite and RBSDC design note)

The impersonation readiness gate (generateAccessToken + accessSecretVersion)
was designed to verify IAM propagation before creating the CB v2 connection.
Research (2026-03-03) revealed three problems:

1. **roles/owner does NOT grant iam.serviceAccounts.getAccessToken** —
   the explicit tokenCreator grant (deleted Step B per prior RBSCIP) was
   required, not optional. Persistent 403 on generateAccessToken.

2. **Wrong SA identity** — the code impersonated the default build SA
   ({PN}@cloudbuild.gserviceaccount.com) but CB v2 connections use the
   Cloud Build Service Agent (service-{PN}@gcp-sa-cloudbuild.iam.gserviceaccount.com).

3. **No non-impersonation alternative exists** — Policy Analyzer and
   testIamPermissions reflect policy intent, not enforcement state.
   Only actual access as the principal proves propagation.

Pattern B: let the connection creation LRO itself be the propagation test.
If the service agent can't read secrets, the LRO fails. Retry with backoff.
This eliminates generateAccessToken, accessSecretVersion, and any need for
tokenCreator grants for the readiness gate.

## File-by-file changes

### RBSCIP-IamPropagation.adoc — FULL REWRITE
The entire document (86 lines) is the rationale FOR the impersonation gate.
Rewrite to document Pattern B instead:
- Decision: replace impersonation gate with connection-creation retry
- Rationale: the three problems above + "connection LRO tests the actual
  operation, not a proxy"
- Preserve the Evidence table (IAM propagation docs, SA creation delays)
- Remove generateAccessToken/accessSecretVersion evidence rows
- Add evidence: CB v2 connection docs showing Service Agent reads secrets
- Preserve the Backoff Profile section (same profile applies to retry)
- Update What Dies / What Survives accordingly
- Add a "Superseded" note documenting the old gate approach and why it failed

### RBSDC-depot_create.adoc — UPDATE connection creation step
The spec already has NO impersonation gate step (it was code-only, never
spec'd as a step). Changes needed:
- Lines 215-246 (Create CB v2 GitLab Connection): add retry/backoff language
  and zombie cleanup between retries to the connection creation step
- Add a design note explaining why connection creation serves as the
  propagation gate (brief, pointing to RBSCIP for full rationale)
- DO NOT touch line 168-177 ("Enable Cloud Build service agent to impersonate
  Mason") — that is a different grant for build-time Mason impersonation,
  unrelated to the readiness gate. Audited separately in ₢AiABA.

### RBS0-SpecTop.adoc — VERIFY, likely no change
Grep found only one "impersonates" reference (line 1232, about Mason build-time
impersonation — unrelated). Verify no other references exist. If clean, no
changes needed — do not invent edits.

## Acceptance criteria

- RBSCIP fully rewritten to document Pattern B with rationale
- RBSCIP records why the old impersonation gate failed (the three problems)
- RBSDC connection creation step includes retry/backoff and zombie cleanup
- RBSDC Mason impersonation step (line 168-177) is untouched
- RBS0 verified clean (no impersonation gate references)
- No references to generateAccessToken or accessSecretVersion as a
  readiness gate in any spec (build-time references preserved)

### implement-connection-retry-gate (₢AiAA_) [complete]

**[260303-1502] complete**

Replace the impersonation readiness gate in depot_create with Pattern B:
connection-creation-as-probe with retry/backoff.

## Background: Two Cloud Build SAs

- **Default build SA**: `{PN}@cloudbuild.gserviceaccount.com` — executes builds
- **Cloud Build Service Agent**: `service-{PN}@gcp-sa-cloudbuild.iam.gserviceaccount.com` — manages CB v2 connections, reads secrets for connection config

The secret accessor grants (lines ~897-955) correctly target the Service Agent
(`service-` prefix). The connection creation LRO exercises the same SA reading
the same secrets — making it a direct propagation test.

## What to remove

Delete from rbgp_Payor.sh (rbgp_depot_create function):
- The `Impersonation readiness gate` buc_step block and everything in it:
  - CB SA email URL-encoding
  - Step C: generateAccessToken polling loop
  - Step D: accessSecretVersion polling loop
  - All z_gat_* and z_asv_* local variables
- Identify the block by the buc_step label, NOT by line numbers (they shift)

**DO NOT touch:**
- Line ~812: `rbgi_add_sa_iam_role ... roles/iam.serviceAccountTokenCreator`
  on Mason — this is build-time impersonation (CB impersonates Mason during
  builds), NOT the readiness gate. Audited separately in ₢AiABA.
- Secret accessor grants on the 3 secrets — these stay (they're what the
  connection creation will exercise)
- Connection admin grant — stays

## What to modify

Wrap the existing connection creation + poll in a retry loop:

### Pre-work: extract zombie cleanup
The existing zombie connection cleanup (find by `Check for zombie CB v2
connection` log message) currently runs once before the first create attempt.
Extract it into a local function or clearly-delimited block so it can be
called between retry attempts.

### Retry loop structure
1. Run zombie cleanup (delete any existing connection with same name)
2. Attempt connection creation (POST connections.create → LRO)
3. Poll LRO to completion (existing `rbgu_http_json_lro_ok` call)
4. On LRO success: poll installationState until COMPLETE (existing code)
5. On LRO failure (secret-access-related or other):
   - Log diagnostic: which step failed, HTTP code, error message
   - Backoff sleep (exponential: 3s initial, 2x multiplier, 20s cap)
   - Increment elapsed time, check against 420s deadline
   - Loop back to step 1
6. On deadline exceeded: die with diagnostic checklist

### Risk: LRO failure mode is unverified
We assume the LRO fails cleanly when the service agent can't read secrets.
This has NOT been observed directly. During implementation:
- On the FIRST attempt (when IAM hasn't propagated), observe and record
  the actual LRO error shape (done:true with error? stuck in pending?)
- If the failure mode is NOT clean (e.g., LRO hangs indefinitely instead
  of failing), we may need a timeout on the LRO poll itself as the trigger
  for retry. Document what we find.

## Files

- Tools/rbw/rbgp_Payor.sh — primary changes (remove gate, add retry loop)

## Acceptance criteria

- No generateAccessToken or accessSecretVersion calls in depot_create
- The `Impersonation readiness gate` buc_step block is fully deleted
- Mason tokenCreator grant (line ~812) is preserved untouched
- Connection creation retries on failure with exponential backoff
- Zombie connection cleanup runs before each retry attempt
- Successful depot creation when IAM propagation is slow (tested live)
- Clean failure message with diagnostic checklist on timeout
- depot_destroy still works (verify — creation flow restructured)
- LRO failure mode documented (what error shape triggers retry)

**[260303-1446] rough**

Replace the impersonation readiness gate in depot_create with Pattern B:
connection-creation-as-probe with retry/backoff.

## Background: Two Cloud Build SAs

- **Default build SA**: `{PN}@cloudbuild.gserviceaccount.com` — executes builds
- **Cloud Build Service Agent**: `service-{PN}@gcp-sa-cloudbuild.iam.gserviceaccount.com` — manages CB v2 connections, reads secrets for connection config

The secret accessor grants (lines ~897-955) correctly target the Service Agent
(`service-` prefix). The connection creation LRO exercises the same SA reading
the same secrets — making it a direct propagation test.

## What to remove

Delete from rbgp_Payor.sh (rbgp_depot_create function):
- The `Impersonation readiness gate` buc_step block and everything in it:
  - CB SA email URL-encoding
  - Step C: generateAccessToken polling loop
  - Step D: accessSecretVersion polling loop
  - All z_gat_* and z_asv_* local variables
- Identify the block by the buc_step label, NOT by line numbers (they shift)

**DO NOT touch:**
- Line ~812: `rbgi_add_sa_iam_role ... roles/iam.serviceAccountTokenCreator`
  on Mason — this is build-time impersonation (CB impersonates Mason during
  builds), NOT the readiness gate. Audited separately in ₢AiABA.
- Secret accessor grants on the 3 secrets — these stay (they're what the
  connection creation will exercise)
- Connection admin grant — stays

## What to modify

Wrap the existing connection creation + poll in a retry loop:

### Pre-work: extract zombie cleanup
The existing zombie connection cleanup (find by `Check for zombie CB v2
connection` log message) currently runs once before the first create attempt.
Extract it into a local function or clearly-delimited block so it can be
called between retry attempts.

### Retry loop structure
1. Run zombie cleanup (delete any existing connection with same name)
2. Attempt connection creation (POST connections.create → LRO)
3. Poll LRO to completion (existing `rbgu_http_json_lro_ok` call)
4. On LRO success: poll installationState until COMPLETE (existing code)
5. On LRO failure (secret-access-related or other):
   - Log diagnostic: which step failed, HTTP code, error message
   - Backoff sleep (exponential: 3s initial, 2x multiplier, 20s cap)
   - Increment elapsed time, check against 420s deadline
   - Loop back to step 1
6. On deadline exceeded: die with diagnostic checklist

### Risk: LRO failure mode is unverified
We assume the LRO fails cleanly when the service agent can't read secrets.
This has NOT been observed directly. During implementation:
- On the FIRST attempt (when IAM hasn't propagated), observe and record
  the actual LRO error shape (done:true with error? stuck in pending?)
- If the failure mode is NOT clean (e.g., LRO hangs indefinitely instead
  of failing), we may need a timeout on the LRO poll itself as the trigger
  for retry. Document what we find.

- The `Impersonation readiness gate` buc_step block is fully deleted

**[260303-1442] rough**

Replace the impersonation readiness gate in depot_create with Pattern B:
connection-creation-as-probe with retry/backoff.

## What to remove

Delete from rbgp_Payor.sh (depot_create):
- Step C: generateAccessToken polling loop (lines ~968-1012)
- Step D: accessSecretVersion polling loop (lines ~1014-1050)
- The entire "Impersonation readiness gate" buc_step block
- The tokenCreator grant on the CB service agent (line ~812:
  rbgi_add_sa_iam_role for roles/iam.serviceAccountTokenCreator on Mason)
  NOTE: verify this grant's actual purpose — it grants tokenCreator on
  Mason TO the CB service agent, which may serve a different purpose
  (build-time impersonation). Only remove if it's solely for the gate.

## What to add

Wrap the existing connection creation + poll in a retry loop:
1. Attempt connection creation (POST connections.create LRO)
2. Poll LRO to completion
3. If LRO fails with secret-access-related error:
   - Log diagnostic (which secret, what error)
   - Delete zombie connection (existing cleanup code at lines ~1058-1076)
   - Backoff sleep (exponential, capped at 20s, deadline 420s)
   - Retry from step 1
4. If LRO succeeds, poll installationState until COMPLETE (existing code)
5. If deadline exceeded, die with diagnostic

## Key design points

- Reuse existing zombie connection cleanup logic
- Reuse existing backoff pattern from the old gate
- Connection creation LRO tests the ACTUAL operation (service agent
  reading secrets), not a proxy
- No new API calls, no new IAM grants needed

- Tools/rbw/rbgp_Payor.sh — primary changes
- Possibly Tools/rbw/rbgu_Utility.sh if shared retry helpers are useful

## Acceptance criteria

- No generateAccessToken or accessSecretVersion calls in depot_create
- Connection creation retries on secret-access failure with backoff
- Zombie connection cleanup between retries
- Successful depot creation when IAM propagation is slow
- Clean failure message on timeout

### fix-impersonation-gate-per-rbscip (₢AiAA9) [complete]

**[260303-1417] complete**

Fix impersonation readiness gate to match RBSCIP research.

## Problem

The ₢AiAA0 implementation added two steps not in the RBSCIP trade study:
- Step A: Get Payor email via userinfo (requires openid scope the token lacks)
- Step B: Grant Payor serviceAccountTokenCreator on CB service agent (requires the email)

These break depot_create with HTTP 401 on the userinfo endpoint.

## RBSCIP says

"The gate mints a short-lived token as the CB service agent via generateAccessToken,
then calls accessSecretVersion with that impersonated token, retrying on 403 until
the grant propagates."

No mention of Payor email. No mention of granting tokenCreator to the Payor.

## Hypothesis

The Payor is the project owner (just created the project in step 5). Project owners
have iam.serviceAccounts.getAccessToken permission, which allows calling
generateAccessToken without an explicit serviceAccountTokenCreator grant.

## Required research

Verify whether project owner can call generateAccessToken on Google-managed service
agents (service-{PN}@gcp-sa-cloudbuild.iam.gserviceaccount.com). If yes, delete
Steps A+B entirely. If no, find the correct approach that doesn't require scopes
the Payor token lacks.

## Target files

- `Tools/rbw/rbgp_Payor.sh` — impersonation gate section (~lines 961-1060)
- `lenses/RBSDC-depot_create.adoc` — may need spec update if gate steps change
- `lenses/RBSCIP-IamPropagation.adoc` — update if research findings change

## Acceptance criteria

- depot_create completes through CB v2 connection creation without 401
- Impersonation gate verifies CB SA can access secrets per RBSCIP
- No dependency on userinfo endpoint or openid/email scopes

- Uppercase final char = lasting effect (create, destroy, reset, install, refresh)
- Lowercase final char = read-only or guide (list, guide, retrieve)

### rename-tabtargets-role-prefix (₢AiAA2) [complete]

**[260302-1905] complete**

Rename rbw tabtargets to consistent rbw-<Role><Verb><Object> epithet pattern.

## Role Prefixes

- `D` — Director (write ops: build, inscribe, delete, abjure, beseech, conjure, summon)
- `G` — Governor (SA lifecycle: create director, create retriever, delete SA, list SAs)
- `P` — Payor (depot/billing: create depot, destroy depot, list depots, reset governor, establish, refresh)
- `R` — Retriever (read ops: retrieve image, list images)

## Renames

| Current | New | Zipper const |
|---------|-----|-------------|
| `rbw-Dr.DirectorRetrievesImage.sh` | `rbw-Rri.RetrieverRetrievesImage.sh` | RBZ_RETRIEVE_IMAGE |
| `rbw-Dl.DirectorListsImages.sh` | `rbw-Rli.RetrieverListsImages.sh` | RBZ_LIST_IMAGES |
| `rbw-ld.ListDepots.sh` | `rbw-Pld.PayorListsDepots.sh` | RBZ_LIST_DEPOT |
| `rbw-gpe.PayorEstablishment.sh` | `rbw-Pes.PayorEstablishes.sh` | RBZ_PAYOR_ESTABLISH |
| `rbw-gpr.PayorRefresh.sh` | `rbw-Pre.PayorRefreshes.sh` | RBZ_PAYOR_REFRESH |
| `rbw-gps.ShowPayorEstablishment.sh` | `rbw-Pse.PayorShowsEstablishment.sh` | RBZ_SHOW_PAYOR_ESTABLISH |
| `rbw-pCD.PayorCreatesDepot.sh` | `rbw-Pcd.PayorCreatesDepot.sh` | RBZ_CREATE_DEPOT |
| `rbw-pDD.PayorDestroysDepot.sh` | `rbw-Pdd.PayorDestroysDepot.sh` | RBZ_DESTROY_DEPOT |
| `rbw-pRG.PayorResetsGovernor.sh` | `rbw-Prg.PayorResetsGovernor.sh` | RBZ_GOVERNOR_RESET |
| `rbw-pip.PayorInstallProcedure.sh` | `rbw-Pip.PayorInstallsProcedure.sh` | RBZ_PAYOR_INSTALL |

## Logging fix

Remove BURD_NO_LOG=1 from these tabtargets (API calls deserve paper trail):
- `rbw-Dl` → `rbw-Rli` (list images)
- `rbw-ld` → `rbw-Pld` (list depots)

Keep BURD_NO_LOG=1 on guide/display-only tabtargets (`rbw-Pse`, `rbw-Pip`) — no API calls.

## Also fix rbf_list() auth

`rbf_list()` should use Retriever-prefer-Director-fallback pattern (matching `rbf_retrieve()`).

## Files touched per rename

Each rename touches:
1. `tt/rbw-OLD.sh` → `tt/rbw-NEW.sh` (git mv)
2. `Tools/rbw/rbz_zipper.sh` — buz_enroll colophon string
3. Any hardcoded colophon references in code/error messages

## Acceptance Criteria

- All role-actor tabtargets use consistent rbw-<Role> prefix
- Zipper enrollments match new colophons
- rbf_list uses Retriever credentials
- List tabtargets log (no BURD_NO_LOG)
- Tab-completion works with new names
- No broken dispatch paths

### add-burd-now-epoch (₢AiAAg) [complete]

**[260225-1924] complete**

Add BURD_NOW_EPOCH to BUK dispatch infrastructure.

## Motivation

Inscribe needs epoch arithmetic to rate-limit pin refresh (skip if < 1 day old).
BCG prohibits command substitution at point of use. All true time should come from
dispatch for consistency — BURD_NOW_EPOCH provides UTC epoch seconds synchronized
with the existing BURD_NOW_STAMP from a single `date` invocation.

## Single date invocation

Replace the existing `date` call in bud_dispatch.sh:

```bash
# Before:
BURD_NOW_STAMP=$(date +'%Y%m%d-%H%M%S')-$$-$((RANDOM % 1000))

# After:
z_datetime=$(date +'%Y%m%d-%H%M%S %s')
BURD_NOW_STAMP="${z_datetime% *}-$$-$((RANDOM % 1000))"
BURD_NOW_EPOCH="${z_datetime#* }"
```

Bash parameter expansion splits on the space — no subshell, no temp file.
`%s` is always UTC epoch regardless of timezone. The existing local-time
stamp format is preserved.

## Changes

1. bud_dispatch.sh — modify date call, add BURD_NOW_EPOCH
2. bud_dispatch.sh — add BURD_NOW_EPOCH to z_known list (line ~277)
3. bud_dispatch.sh — add `export BURD_NOW_EPOCH` alongside existing exports
4. BUS0-BashUtilitiesSpec.adoc — document BURD_NOW_EPOCH if BURD vars are listed

## Files

- Tools/buk/bud_dispatch.sh
- Tools/buk/vov_veiled/BUS0-BashUtilitiesSpec.adoc (if BURD vars documented)

## Verify

- Run any tabtarget and confirm BURD_NOW_EPOCH is set to a valid epoch
- Confirm BURD_NOW_STAMP format is unchanged

## Single date invocation

Replace the existing `date` call in bud_dispatch.sh:

```bash
# Before:
BURD_NOW_STAMP=$(date +'%Y%m%d-%H%M%S')-$$-$((RANDOM % 1000))

# After:
z_datetime=$(date +'%Y%m%d-%H%M%S %s')
BURD_NOW_STAMP="${z_datetime% *}-$$-$((RANDOM % 1000))"
BURD_NOW_EPOCH="${z_datetime#* }"
```

Bash parameter expansion splits on the space — no subshell, no temp file.
`%s` is always UTC epoch regardless of timezone. The existing local-time
stamp format is preserved.

## Changes

1. bud_dispatch.sh — modify date call, add BURD_NOW_EPOCH
2. bud_dispatch.sh — add BURD_NOW_EPOCH to z_known list (line ~277)
3. bud_dispatch.sh — add `export BURD_NOW_EPOCH` alongside existing exports
4. BUS0-BashUtilitiesSpec.adoc — document BURD_NOW_EPOCH if BURD vars are listed

## Files

- Tools/buk/bud_dispatch.sh
- Tools/buk/vov_veiled/BUS0-BashUtilitiesSpec.adoc (if BURD vars documented)

## Verify

- Run any tabtarget and confirm BURD_NOW_EPOCH is set to a valid epoch
- Confirm BURD_NOW_STAMP format is unchanged

**[260224-1535] complete**

Implement single rubric repo model replacing per-vessel mini-repos.

## Changes

1. **RBRA regime** (`Tools/rbw/rbra_regime.sh`):
   - Drop `RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT` enrollment (line 47) and validation (lines 74-77)
   - Add `RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL` (optional, 0-512 chars, authenticated git URL)
   - Validation: if non-empty, check it starts with `https://`

2. **Utility check routine** (`Tools/rbw/rbgu_Utility.sh`):
   - Replace `rbgu_check_rubric_pat()` (line 684, GitHub API call) with
     `rbgu_check_rubric_repo_url()` using `git ls-remote "${url}" HEAD`
   - Die if non-zero exit (bad URL, bad credentials, repo not found)

3. **Governor preflight** (`Tools/rbw/rbgg_Governor.sh`):
   - `zrbgg_rubric_preflight()` (line 101): replace
     `rbgu_check_rubric_pat "${RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT:-}"` (line 116)
     with `rbgu_check_rubric_repo_url "${RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL:-}"`

4. **depot_initialize guide** (`Tools/rbw/rbgm_ManualProcedures.sh`):
   - Rewrite PAT guidance section (lines 500-520) for rubric repo URL:
     - "Create a repo on your git hosting service"
     - "Create a PAT with Contents:write on that repo"
     - "Construct authenticated URL: https://x-access-token:<PAT>@<host>/<org>/<repo>.git"
     - "Add to Governor RBRA file: RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL=<url>"
   - Change `z_github_pat` variable to `z_rubric_repo_url`
   - Validate with `git ls-remote` instead of GitHub API

5. **Spec** (`lenses/RBS0-SpecTop.adoc`):
   - Rename linked term: `rbra_rubric_github_pat` → `rbra_rubric_repo_url` (lines 297, 722, 2088-2090)
   - Update definition text to describe authenticated git URL
   - Update `rbtoe_check_rubric_pat` definition to `rbtoe_check_rubric_repo_url` if present

- `depot_initialize` runs and validates rubric repo URL via `git ls-remote`
- Preflight gates (create_retriever, create_director) pass with valid authenticated URL
- Preflight gates fail cleanly with missing/invalid URL

### design-courier-credential-regime (₢AiAAB) [abandoned]

**[260222-1522] abandoned**

Design the Courier (rbhk) credential regime:
- Decide: new regime file (rbhk.env) vs RBRR expansion
- Define credential format for GitHub PAT (NOT RBRA — different provider, different trust boundary)
  RBRA is specifically Google SA credentials (CLIENT_EMAIL, PRIVATE_KEY, PROJECT_ID,
  TOKEN_LIFETIME_SEC). GitHub PAT is a single opaque token — fundamentally different.
- Design Secret Manager bridge: GitHub issues PAT, Google stores it for Developer Connect
- Determine validation rules (buv validators for new credential type)
- PAT scope decision: classic PAT with broad `repo` scope vs fine-grained PAT (per-repo).
  Fine-grained is tighter security but more management overhead per vessel repo.
- PAT lifecycle: GitHub PATs expire. Design refresh/rotation ceremony and document
  expected lifetime. The credential regime must account for expiration.
- Document in a new spec lens or memo

- PAT scope decision: classic PAT with broad `repo` scope vs fine-grained PAT (per-repo).

(buv enrollment, scope sentinel). No GitHub account/repo variables needed —
triggers connect to the main repo via Developer Connect, not to separate vessel repos.

Script Developer Connect connection setup:
- Create ONE connection via REST API: POST to developerconnect.googleapis.com
  (this single connection serves all vessel repos — not per-vessel connections)
- Extract authorization URI from response
- Present URI to user for one-time GitHub OAuth consent (manual browser step)
- Poll/verify connection is authorized
- Link the busybox vessel repo to the connection via REST API
  (remaining vessel repos are linked in ₢AiAAM during migration)
- All curl/REST — no gcloud CLI dependency
- BCG compliance for all scripting

Uses RBRR_GDC_CONNECTION_NAME, RBRR_GDC_REGION, RBRR_GDC_SECRET_NAME.
One-time setup for the connection; per-vessel linking is incremental.

### author-cloudbuild-yaml-busybox (₢AiAAD) [complete]

**[260222-1608] complete**

Author cloudbuild.yaml for rbev-busybox (the test mule vessel).

File: rbev-vessels/rbev-busybox/cloudbuild.yaml (ALREADY EXISTS — rewrite in place)

## Design: Maximally Baked

Bake ALL values that are static per-vessel. Only 4 substitutions remain (per-build dynamic):
- _RBGY_TAG_BASE — timestamp tag, generated by Foundry at dispatch time
- _RBGY_GIT_COMMIT — git commit hash
- _RBGY_GIT_BRANCH — git branch name
- _RBGY_GIT_REPO — git repo URL

Everything else is hardcoded directly in the YAML:
- Moniker: rbev-busybox
- Platforms: linux/amd64,linux/arm64,linux/arm/v7
- Dockerfile path: rbev-vessels/rbev-busybox/Dockerfile
- GAR location: from RBRR (read rbrr.env for current values, bake them)
- GAR project: RBRR_DEPOT_PROJECT_ID
- GAR repository: RBRR_GAR_REPOSITORY
- GAR host suffix: -docker.pkg.dev
- Ark suffixes: -image, -about
- Crane URL: RBRR_CRANE_TAR_GZ value
- All 6 pinned image refs: baked from RBRR_GCB_*_IMAGE_REF values in rbrr.env
- Syft image ref: baked inline (no RBRR variable reference at runtime)
- Binfmt image ref: baked inline

## Step structure (9 steps, renumbered sequentially)

Step 01 (derive-tag-base) is ELIMINATED — TAG_BASE comes via _RBGY_TAG_BASE substitution.

1. get-docker-token — gcloud auth print-access-token (gcloud builder)
   Log hygiene: set +x, token to file only
2. docker-login-gar — docker login using token (docker builder)
   Log hygiene: set +x, pipe token via stdin, rm token file
3. qemu-binfmt — register QEMU for cross-platform builds (docker builder)
   Binfmt image ref baked inline
4. build-and-export — multi-arch buildx to OCI tarball (docker builder)
   OCI Layout Bridge Phase 1. Build context is repo root (.).
   Dockerfile at baked path. TAG_BASE from substitution.
5. push-with-crane — push OCI layout to GAR (alpine builder, /bin/sh)
   OCI Layout Bridge Phase 2. Crane URL baked. TAG_BASE from substitution.
6. sbom-and-summary — Syft SBOM generation (docker builder)
   OCI Layout Bridge Phase 3. Syft image ref baked inline.
7. assemble-metadata — build_info.json with jq (alpine builder, /bin/sh)
   Uses TAG_BASE and GIT substitutions. Copies Dockerfile to recipe.txt.
8. build-and-push-metadata — scratch container with metadata (docker builder)
   Uses TAG_BASE substitution for about-tag.

## Dollar escaping rules (Cloud Build YAML)

- $$ in YAML → literal $ after Cloud Build substitution pass
- ${_RBGY_*} → Cloud Build substitutes these (4 dynamic values)
- Shell variables like ${TAG_BASE} or $(cat file) → use $$ escaping:
  TAG_BASE="$${_RBGY_TAG_BASE}" is wrong (that's a substitution)
  Instead: use ${_RBGY_TAG_BASE} directly since TAG_BASE IS a substitution now
- In jq filter bodies: $$varname → becomes $varname for jq's --arg refs

## serviceAccount

NOT in the YAML — set on the trigger resource (₢AiAAH). Cloud Build ignores
serviceAccount in YAML for trigger-invoked builds. Mason SA goes on the trigger.

## Build context

Cloud Build checks out the entire main repo via Developer Connect.
Dockerfile path and build context are relative to repo root.

## References

- rbrr.env — current pinned values to bake
- Tools/rbw/rbgjb/*.sh — original step script bodies
- Tools/rbw/rbf_Foundry.sh lines 136-229 — stitching logic (step order, builders, entrypoints)
- Tools/rbw/rbgc_Constants.sh — RBGC_GAR_HOST_SUFFIX, RBGC_ARK_SUFFIX_*

repo root — the _RBGY_VESSEL_DIR substitution is still needed to locate the Dockerfile
and context within the checked-out repo tree.

The Dockerfile and build context live at the top level of the vessel repo,
not in a subdirectory. The _RBGY_VESSEL_DIR substitution from the shared-repo
design is no longer needed. Adjust Dockerfile and context references accordingly
(e.g., -f Dockerfile . instead of -f {vessel_dir}/Dockerfile {vessel_dir}).

**[260223-0824] complete**

## Acceptance

### introduce-rubric-vocabulary-fix-paddock (₢AiAAP) [complete]

**[260224-0711] complete**

Introduce the Rubric concept and all trigger-migration linked terms into RBS0
and related lenses. Also update the heat paddock to correct the stale
"main repo as trigger source" design decision.

## Paddock correction

Update paddock to reflect the actual architecture:
- Per-vessel mini-repos on GitHub (NOT main repo as trigger source)
- Cloud Build sees only mini-repos via Developer Connect (security boundary)
- Main repo is never exposed to Google Cloud Build
- Inscribe syncs main repo → mini-repo (orchestrated git)

## AXLA additions (AXLA-Lexicon.adoc)

New axig_* motifs:
- axig_developer_connect (Developer Connect service)
- axig_build_trigger (Cloud Build trigger resource)
- axig_repo_link (git repository link within a connection)
- axig_build_config (build configuration file)
- axig_slsa_provenance (build provenance attestation)

## RBS0 mapping section — new rbtgr_* family (RB Term Google Rubric)

- rbtgr_rubric / rbtgr_rubric_s — composite per-vessel build definition (yaml + trigger + mini-repo)
- rbtgr_build_yaml — committed cloudbuild.yaml per vessel
- rbtgr_vessel_trigger — per-vessel Cloud Build trigger
- rbtgr_vessel_repo — per-vessel mini-repo on GitHub (what Cloud Build sees)
- rbtgr_provenance — SLSA v1.0 attestation from trigger builds

## RBS0 mapping section — new rbtgi_* terms (Developer Connect)

- rbtgi_source_connection — Developer Connect connection (one per GitHub org)
- rbtgi_source_link — per-vessel git repository link binding (created by inscribe via Developer Connect)

## RBS0 mapping section — new rbtgo_* operations

- rbtgo_gdc_establish — manual procedure (lens RBSGD already exists)
- rbtgo_rubric_inscribe — generate yaml, verify committed, sync mini-repo, create trigger
- rbtgo_trigger_build — triggers.run dispatch (revised existing term)

Note: no rbtgo_rubric_assay (inscribe handles freshness internally).
Note: no rbtgo_rubric_enshrine (trigger creation is an internal step of inscribe).

## Remaining vocabulary sections unchanged from previous docket

- rbrr_* regime variable terms
- New include files (RBSRI-rubric_inscribe.adoc)
- Subdoc updates using new linked terms
- AXLA voicing annotations throughout

**[260224-0644] rough**

Rewrite RBSTB-trigger_build.adoc for the trigger-based build flow.
Assumes ₢AiAAP (vocabulary) has landed — use new linked terms throughout.

## Remove (old builds.create flow)

- Tarball packaging, GCS upload, stitching, builds.create API references
- rbtgi_build_bucket references (trigger builds fetch from mini-repo, no GCS)

## Rewrite using rubric vocabulary

- {rbtgr_rubric} as the build definition concept
- {rbtgr_build_yaml} for the committed cloudbuild.yaml
- {rbtgr_vessel_trigger} for the Cloud Build trigger resource
- {rbtgr_vessel_repo} for the per-vessel mini-repo
- {rbtgr_provenance} for SLSA v1.0 attestation output
- {rbtgi_source_connection} / {rbtgi_source_link} for Developer Connect

## Document the two operations

- Inscribe ({rbtgo_rubric_inscribe}): pin freshness → generate yaml → verify
  committed → sync mini-repo → create trigger → push
- Dispatch ({rbtgo_trigger_build}): triggers.run with zero custom substitution
  overrides. All _RBGY_* values baked in committed YAML's substitutions block.
  Cloud Build resolves them from the YAML, not from dispatch-time overrides.

## Substitutions architecture

- _RBGY_* values baked into YAML substitutions block at inscribe time
- Step scripts (rbgjb/*.sh) reference _RBGY_* as before — resolved by Cloud Build
- Zero overrides at dispatch — only source.commitSha specified in triggers.run

## Dual-timestamp consecration tag format

- Format: i{date}_{time}-b{date}_{time}
- Example: i20260224_153022-b20260224_160530
- Inscribe timestamp baked as _RBGY_INSCRIBE_TIMESTAMP
- Build timestamp derived at build time by rbgjb01
- TAG_BASE="${_RBGY_INSCRIBE_TIMESTAMP}-b$(date -u +%Y%m%d_%H%M%S)"

## Metadata in -about artifact

- build_info.json includes main repo metadata (commit, branch, repo URL)
  AND rubric repo metadata (mini-repo URL, commit) — all from _RBGY_* substitutions
- {rbtgr_provenance} generated separately by Google as signed attestation on image

## Constraints

- Maintain MCM patterns and AXLA voicing annotations
- This file is included by RBS0 at the {rbtgo_trigger_build} operation section

- Tarball packaging, GCS upload, stitching, builds.create API references

- {rbtgr_rubric} as the build definition concept
- {rbtgr_build_yaml} for the committed cloudbuild.yaml
- {rbtgr_vessel_trigger} for the Cloud Build trigger resource
- {rbtgr_provenance} for SLSA v1.0 attestation output
- {rbtgi_source_connection} / {rbtgi_source_link} where Developer Connect is referenced

- {rbtgo_rubric_assay} — yaml freshness check (committed matches regenerated)
- Clean git state (existing precondition, unchanged)

## Behavior sections
- Prepare: verify {rbtgr_build_yaml} is committed and fresh
- Dispatch: triggers.run with per-invocation substitution overrides via {rbtgr_vessel_trigger}
- Substitution overrides: _RBGY_* variables (dynamic at dispatch time)
- Monitor: poll build status, capture build ID

## Outputs
- Built container image in {rbtgi_repository}
- {rbtgr_provenance} auto-generated by Google for trigger-invoked builds
- Build transcript / about artifact assembled into {rbtga_ark_about}

- Maintain MCM patterns and AXLA voicing annotations
- This file is included by RBS0 at the {rbtgo_trigger_build} operation section
- Do NOT touch RBS0 mapping section or definitions — that's ₢AiAAP's scope

**[260224-0821] complete**

This is the spec-first step before any code changes.

## Session Decisions (record in paddock)

- RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT: optional field in RBRA regime, populated in Director only
- rbgm_gdc_establish() deleted — replaced by automated connection creation in
  depot_create + new rbgm_depot_initialize() human procedure
- Developer Connect connection creation moves to rbgp_depot_create() (automated, PENDING state)
- New rbgm_depot_initialize(): validate GitHub PAT, guide OAuth browser step, poll until COMPLETE
- RBRR_GDC_REPO_LINK and RBRR_GCB_TRIGGER_PATTERN already removed (committed in this pace)

## Spec Updates

1. RBS0 + RBRA subdoc: Add RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT as optional credential field
   - Update RBRA definitions section with new variable
   - Note: only Director role populates this

2. RBS0 + RBSDC: Add developerconnect + secretmanager API enablement and
   Developer Connect connection creation to depot_create procedure
   - Connection created in PENDING state (OAuth not yet done)

3. Author new spec RBSDN-depot_initialize.adoc (or appropriate name):
   - Validate RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT against GitHub API
   - If invalid: guide user through fine-grained PAT creation
   - Retrieve Developer Connect authorization URI from pending connection
   - Human opens browser, authorizes Google Developer Connect app on GitHub org
   - Poll until installationState.stage reaches COMPLETE
   - Final validation: PAT works AND connection is active
   - Idempotent — safe to re-run

4. Update RBSGD-gdc_establish.adoc: reflect that connection creation is automated
   in depot_create, OAuth authorization is guided in depot_initialize.
   The standalone manual guide is being replaced.

## Paddock Update

Record all session decisions from this conversation in the paddock.

- All spec changes committed
- Paddock updated with session decisions
- No code changes in this pace (spec-only)

### code-rbra-pat-and-depot-create (₢AiAAX) [complete]

**[260224-0823] complete**

Implement RBRA GitHub PAT extension and depot_create connection creation.

## RBRA Regime Extension

In Tools/rbw/rbra_regime.sh:
- kindle: add RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT default
- enroll: buv_string_enroll RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT 0 256 "GitHub PAT for rubric repo management"
- enforce: if non-empty, validate format (ghp_ or github_pat_ prefix)

## depot_create Changes

In Tools/rbw/rbgp_Payor.sh rbgp_depot_create():
- Add developerconnect and secretmanager to API enablement list (step "Enable depot project APIs")
- After IAM propagation and resource creation, create Developer Connect connection via REST:
  POST to developerconnect.googleapis.com/v1/projects/{project}/locations/{region}/connections
  with github-config-app=DEVELOPER-CONNECT
  Connection left in PENDING state — OAuth completed later by depot_initialize

## Regime smoke test

Verify regime smoke test passes with optional empty RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT.

### author-depot-initialize (₢AiAAY) [complete]

**[260224-0831] complete**

Author rbgm_depot_initialize() — the human-interactive procedure that validates
GitHub PAT and completes Developer Connect OAuth authorization.

## Function: rbgm_depot_initialize()

In Tools/rbw/rbgm_ManualProcedures.sh, following rbgm_payor_establish() pattern:

1. Source Director RBRA file, check RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT
2. If empty/missing: guide user through fine-grained PAT creation
   - Scopes needed: repo (create, push to mini-repos)
   - Instruct to add RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT=ghp_xxx to director RBRA file
   - Re-source and validate
3. Test PAT: GET https://api.github.com/user with Authorization: token header
4. Retrieve Developer Connect authorization URI:
   GET connection resource, extract installationState.actionUri
5. Display URI — human opens browser, authorizes Google Developer Connect app
6. Poll until installationState.stage == COMPLETE
7. Final summary: PAT valid, connection active, ready for inscribe

Must be idempotent — safe to re-run (skip steps already complete).

## Tabtarget + Wiring

- Create tt/rbw-gdi.DepotInitialize.sh (or appropriate colophon)
- Wire through rbz_zipper.sh
- Delete old rbgm_gdc_establish() and tt/rbw-gge.GdcEstablishment.sh
- Remove RBZ_GDC_ESTABLISH from zipper

## References

- RBSDN spec (authored in prior pace)
- Tools/rbw/rbgm_ManualProcedures.sh
- Tools/rbw/rbz_zipper.sh

**[260224-0757] rough**
