### rubric-infrastructure-checks (₢AiAAa) [complete]

**[260224-1104] complete**

Implement two rubric infrastructure check routines as rbtoe_* orchestration
patterns, callable as buc_die gates from any CLI context.

## Design Decisions

- RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT lives in BOTH Governor and Director RBRA files
  (different people/machines in multi-person orgs, possibly different PATs)
- depot_initialize must source Governor RBRA (not Director — Director doesn't
  exist yet at depot setup time). Fix existing bug on line 491.
- Two atomic check functions in rbgu_Utility.sh (shared by all CLIs)
- No wrapper function — callers compose the two checks as needed
- Governor create_retriever/create_director call both checks
- Inscribe (future) calls only PAT check via Director RBRA

## Spec (RBS0)

Add linked terms:
- :rbtoe_check_rubric_pat: <<rbtoe_check_rubric_pat,Rubric PAT Check>>
- :rbtoe_check_devconnect: <<rbtoe_check_devconnect,Developer Connect Check>>

Add inline definitions in Orchestration Patterns section (same pattern as
rbtoe_rbra_generate, rbtoe_jwt_oauth_exchange, etc.):

rbtoe_check_rubric_pat: validates RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT via
GET https://api.github.com/user, buc_die on non-200.
Takes PAT as argument. No side effects.

rbtoe_check_devconnect: validates Developer Connect connection
installationState.stage == COMPLETE via REST API.
Takes OAuth token, project, region, connection name as arguments. buc_die if
not COMPLETE. No side effects, no polling.

Add prerequisite references in retriever_create and director_create specs:
both must execute rbtoe_check_rubric_pat and rbtoe_check_devconnect before
any work.

## Code

Two functions in rbgu_Utility.sh:

rbgu_check_rubric_pat(pat):
- curl GET https://api.github.com/user with Bearer token
- check HTTP 200 || buc_die with actionable message
- extract and log username for confirmation
- no return value, just succeeds or dies

rbgu_check_devconnect(token, project, region, connection):
- GET Developer Connect connection endpoint
- extract .installationState.stage
- test == COMPLETE || buc_die with actionable message
- no return value, just succeeds or dies

## Wire

rbgg_create_retriever() and rbgg_create_director() in rbgg_Governor.sh:
- After zrbgg_sentinel, before any work
- Source Governor RBRA, kindle, enforce
- Call rbgu_check_rubric_pat with Governor's PAT
- Get Governor OAuth token, call rbgu_check_devconnect

depot_initialize in rbgm_ManualProcedures.sh:
- Fix line 491: source RBRR_GOVERNOR_RBRA_FILE instead of RBRR_DIRECTOR_RBRA_FILE
- Final validation (lines 603-618) already inline — leave as-is or replace
  with calls to the two new functions

## Verify

Attempt retriever creation without valid PAT/DevConnect — should die cleanly
with actionable error message pointing to depot_initialize.

## References

- Tools/rbw/rbgu_Utility.sh — new check functions
- Tools/rbw/rbgg_Governor.sh — rbgg_create_retriever(), rbgg_create_director()
- Tools/rbw/rbgm_ManualProcedures.sh — depot_initialize bug fix (Governor RBRA)
- lenses/RBS0-SpecTop.adoc — Orchestration Patterns section, retriever/director specs
- lenses/RBSRC-retriever_create.adoc, RBSDI-director_create.adoc — prerequisite additions

not COMPLETE. No side effects, no polling.

both must execute rbtoe_check_rubric_pat and rbtoe_check_devconnect before
any work.

## Code

Two functions in rbgu_Utility.sh:

rbgu_check_rubric_pat(pat):
- curl GET https://api.github.com/user with Bearer token
- check HTTP 200 || buc_die with actionable message
- extract and log username for confirmation
- no return value, just succeeds or dies

rbgu_check_devconnect(token, project, region, connection):
- GET Developer Connect connection endpoint
- extract .installationState.stage
- test == COMPLETE || buc_die with actionable message
- no return value, just succeeds or dies

## Wire

rbgg_create_retriever() and rbgg_create_director() in rbgg_Governor.sh:
- After zrbgg_sentinel, before any work
- Source Governor RBRA, kindle, enforce
- Call rbgu_check_rubric_pat with Governor's PAT
- Get Governor OAuth token, call rbgu_check_devconnect

depot_initialize in rbgm_ManualProcedures.sh:
- Fix line 491: source RBRR_GOVERNOR_RBRA_FILE instead of RBRR_DIRECTOR_RBRA_FILE
- Final validation (lines 603-618) already inline — leave as-is or replace
  with calls to the two new functions

## Verify

Attempt retriever creation without valid PAT/DevConnect — should die cleanly
with actionable error message pointing to depot_initialize.

**[260224-1048] rough**

Implement two rubric infrastructure check routines as rbtoe_* orchestration
patterns, callable as buc_die gates from any CLI context.

## Design Decisions

- RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT lives in BOTH Governor and Director RBRA files
  (different people/machines in multi-person orgs, possibly different PATs)
- depot_initialize must source Governor RBRA (not Director — Director doesn't
  exist yet at depot setup time). Fix existing bug on line 491.
- Two atomic check functions in rbgu_Utility.sh (shared by all CLIs)
- No wrapper function — callers compose the two checks as needed
- Governor create_retriever/create_director call both checks
- Inscribe (future) calls only PAT check via Director RBRA

## Spec (RBS0)

Add linked terms:
- :rbtoe_check_rubric_pat: <<rbtoe_check_rubric_pat,Rubric PAT Check>>
- :rbtoe_check_devconnect: <<rbtoe_check_devconnect,Developer Connect Check>>

Add inline definitions in Orchestration Patterns section (same pattern as
rbtoe_rbra_generate, rbtoe_jwt_oauth_exchange, etc.):

rbtoe_check_rubric_pat: validates RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT via
GET https://api.github.com/user, buc_die on non-200.
Takes PAT as argument. No side effects.

rbtoe_check_devconnect: validates Developer Connect connection
installationState.stage == COMPLETE via REST API.
Takes OAuth token, project, region, connection name as arguments. buc_die if
not COMPLETE. No side effects, no polling.

Add prerequisite references in retriever_create and director_create specs:
both must execute rbtoe_check_rubric_pat and rbtoe_check_devconnect before
any work.

## Code

- check HTTP 200 || buc_die with actionable message
- extract and log username for confirmation
- no return value, just succeeds or dies

rbgu_check_devconnect(token, project, region, connection):
- GET Developer Connect connection endpoint
- extract .installationState.stage
- test == COMPLETE || buc_die with actionable message
- no return value, just succeeds or dies

## Spec (RBS0)

Add new section defining {rbtgo_rubric_preflight} operation:
- Linked term: rbtgo_rubric_preflight
- Validates GitHub PAT (RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT) via GET https://api.github.com/user
- Validates Developer Connect connection stage == COMPLETE via REST API
- Returns success or buc_die — no side effects, no browser, no polling
- Called as prerequisite gate, not as standalone user command

Add prerequisite requirement in Governor Operations section:
- {rbtgo_retriever_create} must call {rbtgo_rubric_preflight} before any work
- {rbtgo_director_create} must call {rbtgo_rubric_preflight} before any work

Add final validation call at end of {rbtgo_depot_initialize} sequence.

## Code

Implement function (likely in rbgm_ManualProcedures.sh or Governor):
- Load RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT from director RBRA
- curl GET https://api.github.com/user with Bearer token, check HTTP 200 || buc_die
- Get GCP OAuth token, GET DevConnect connection endpoint, extract .installationState.stage
- test stage == COMPLETE || buc_die
- No user prompts, no browser, no polling — instant pass/die

Wire into rbgg_create_retriever() and rbgg_create_director() as early gate
(after zrbgg_sentinel, before any work).

Wire into rbgm_depot_initialize() as final health confirmation.

### live-depot-initialize (₢AiAAZ) [complete]

**[260224-1654] complete**

Delete and recreate depot, then execute depot_initialize live.

## Sequence

1. Delete existing depot (rbgp_depot_destroy)
2. Recreate depot (rbgp_depot_create) — now includes connection creation
3. Configure RBRA_RUBRIC_GITHUB_PAT in **Governor RBRA file**
   (depot_initialize sources Governor RBRA — Director doesn't exist yet)
4. Run depot_initialize:
   - Validates Governor RBRA PAT via GitHub API
   - Complete GitHub OAuth browser authorization for Developer Connect
   - Verify connection reaches COMPLETE
5. Set RBRR_GDC_CONNECTION_NAME in rbrr.env with real value
6. Verify regime smoke test passes
7. Verify preflight gates work:
   - Run retriever create — should pass preflight (PAT + DevConnect valid)
   - Or intentionally omit PAT to confirm preflight dies cleanly

## Notes

- depot_initialize now sources RBRR_GOVERNOR_RBRA_FILE (not Director)
  per session 3 paddock decision
- PAT will also go in Director RBRA later when Director is created
- Human-interactive — requires browser for OAuth authorization

### adapt-foundry-for-trigger-json (₢AiAAU) [complete]

**[260225-1949] complete**

Adapt existing Foundry internals to produce complete trigger-compatible
cloudbuild.json. The stitch function already emits JSON steps via jq —
this pace extends it to emit the full Build resource structure.

## Extend zrbf_stitch_build_json() for trigger structure

Currently emits `{"steps": [...]}`. Extend to emit complete trigger-compatible
cloudbuild.json matching the Cloud Build Build resource:
- Add `substitutions` object with all _RBGY_* values baked
  (including new: _RBGY_RUBRIC_REPO, _RBGY_RUBRIC_COMMIT, _RBGY_INSCRIBE_TIMESTAMP)
- _RBGY_RUBRIC_REPO and _RBGY_RUBRIC_COMMIT are placeholders in main-repo copy;
  inscribe fills them in the rubric repo copy after push (per RBSRI spec)
- Add `options` object (logging, machineType from RBRR)
- Add `timeout` from RBRR
- All other values deterministic: same inputs produce byte-identical output
- Emit to per-vessel cloudbuild.json path (vessel dir)
- No YAML, no format conversion — pure jq JSON composition (see RBSCJ trade study)

## Add kindle constants

- RBGC_RUBRIC_CLONE_DIR in rbgc_Constants.sh (local clone root, e.g. ".rbk/rubric")
- RBGC_RUBRIC_TRIGGER_PREFIX (demoted from RBRR_GCB_TRIGGER_PATTERN per paddock)
  Trigger name = RBGC_RUBRIC_TRIGGER_PREFIX + vessel sigil
- Derived at kindle: ZRBF_RUBRIC_CLONE_PATH, ZRBF_RUBRIC_TRIGGER_NAME

## Modify rbrr_refresh_gcb_pins

Add RBRR_GCB_PINS_REFRESHED_AT write to rbrr.env at end of successful refresh.
**Stores epoch seconds** (from BURD_NOW_EPOCH, added in ₢AiAAg) — not a formatted
timestamp. This enables simple integer arithmetic for rate-limiting in inscribe:
`(( BURD_NOW_EPOCH - z_stored < 86400 ))`.

Add regime enrollment in rbrr_regime.sh for RBRR_GCB_PINS_REFRESHED_AT.

## Modify rbgjb01 for dual-timestamp tag

Per paddock: TAG_BASE="${_RBGY_INSCRIBE_TIMESTAMP}-b$(date -u +%Y%m%d_%H%M%S)"
Format: i20260224_153022-b20260224_160530

## What was REMOVED from this pace (session 6, 2026-02-25)

- No zrbf_check_pin_freshness() blocking gate function (inscribe refreshes
  automatically when stale, never fails on staleness)

## Dependencies

- ₢AiAAg (add-burd-now-epoch) must land first — provides BURD_NOW_EPOCH

## Files (5)

- Tools/rbw/rbrr_regime.sh — add RBRR_GCB_PINS_REFRESHED_AT enrollment
- Tools/rbw/rbrr_cli.sh — add epoch timestamp write at end of rbrr_refresh_gcb_pins
- Tools/rbw/rbgc_Constants.sh — add RBGC_RUBRIC_* constants
- Tools/rbw/rbf_Foundry.sh — extend stitch, add kindle constants
- Tools/rbw/rbgjb/rbgjb01-derive-tag-base.sh — dual-timestamp construction

## References

- Tools/rbw/rbf_Foundry.sh — zrbf_stitch_build_json() (extend), zrbf_kindle() (add constants)
- Tools/rbw/rbgc_Constants.sh — add RBGC_RUBRIC_* constants
- Tools/rbw/rbgjb/rbgjb01-derive-tag-base.sh — dual-timestamp construction
- lenses/RBSCJ-CloudBuildJson.adoc — trade study justifying JSON format

## Extend zrbf_stitch_build_json() for trigger structure

cloudbuild.json matching the Cloud Build Build resource:
- Add `substitutions` object with all _RBGY_* values baked
  (including new: _RBGY_RUBRIC_REPO, _RBGY_RUBRIC_COMMIT, _RBGY_INSCRIBE_TIMESTAMP)
- _RBGY_RUBRIC_REPO and _RBGY_RUBRIC_COMMIT are placeholders in main-repo copy;
  inscribe fills them in the rubric repo copy after push (per RBSRI spec)
- Add `options` object (logging, machineType from RBRR)
- Add `timeout` from RBRR
- All other values deterministic: same inputs produce byte-identical output
- Emit to per-vessel cloudbuild.json path (vessel dir)
- No YAML, no format conversion — pure jq JSON composition (see RBSCJ trade study)

## Add kindle constants

- RBGC_RUBRIC_CLONE_DIR in rbgc_Constants.sh (local clone root, e.g. ".rbk/rubric")
- RBGC_RUBRIC_TRIGGER_PREFIX (demoted from RBRR_GCB_TRIGGER_PATTERN per paddock)
  Trigger name = RBGC_RUBRIC_TRIGGER_PREFIX + vessel sigil
- Derived at kindle: ZRBF_RUBRIC_CLONE_PATH, ZRBF_RUBRIC_TRIGGER_NAME

## Modify rbrr_refresh_gcb_pins

Add RBRR_GCB_PINS_REFRESHED_AT timestamp write to rbrr.env at end of
successful refresh. Add regime enrollment in rbrr_regime.sh.

## Add zrbf_check_pin_freshness()

Read RBRR_GCB_PINS_REFRESHED_AT, fail if older than ~2 days.
Called by inscribe before generating JSON.

**[260224-0642] rough**

Adapt existing Foundry internals to support trigger-based builds. This is
modification of existing functions, not new implementations.

## Add kindle constants for rubric naming

Add to rbgc_Constants.sh (DRY naming patterns, not per-vessel config):
- RBGC_RUBRIC_REPO_PREFIX — GitHub mini-repo naming pattern (e.g., "rb-rubric-")
- RBGC_RUBRIC_CLONE_DIR — local clone root (".rbk")
- RBGC_RUBRIC_TRIGGER_PREFIX — trigger naming prefix (e.g., "rbw-build-")
  Demoted from RBRR_GCB_TRIGGER_PATTERN — no justification for per-installation config.
  Trigger name = RBGC_RUBRIC_TRIGGER_PREFIX + vessel sigil.

Derived at kindle time from constants + loaded vessel config:
- ZRBF_RUBRIC_REPO_NAME = RBGC_RUBRIC_REPO_PREFIX + RBRV_SIGIL
- ZRBF_RUBRIC_CLONE_PATH = RBGC_RUBRIC_CLONE_DIR + "/" + RBRV_SIGIL
- ZRBF_RUBRIC_TRIGGER_NAME = RBGC_RUBRIC_TRIGGER_PREFIX + RBRV_SIGIL

## Remove RBRR_GCB_TRIGGER_PATTERN from regime

Remove from rbrr.env, rbrr_regime.sh (kindle, enrollment, validation, render).
Naming is now deterministic from RBGC constant + vessel sigil.

## Modify rbrr_refresh_gcb_pins

Add RBRR_GCB_PINS_REFRESHED_AT timestamp to rbrr.env when pins are refreshed.
Single line addition to existing function in rbrr_cli.sh. Add corresponding
regime variable enrollment in rbrr_regime.sh.

## Modify zrbf_stitch_build_json → YAML output

Adapt the existing stitch function to emit cloudbuild.yaml instead of JSON.
Same inputs: step scripts (rbgjb/*.sh) + pins (RBRR_GCB_*_IMAGE_REF) + vessel
config (RBRV_*). Different output format: static YAML with all values baked.

Key design: step scripts stay as flat bash files. Stitch reads each script,
inlines its content into YAML `script:` fields. All _RBGY_* values go into the
YAML `substitutions:` block (baked at inscribe time, not dispatch-time overrides).
Cloud Build resolves _RBGY_* from the committed YAML.

Substitutions block includes:
- All existing _RBGY_* values (GAR coordinates, vessel identity, platforms, etc.)
- _RBGY_INSCRIBE_TIMESTAMP — inscribe timestamp for dual-timestamp consecration tag
- _RBGY_GIT_COMMIT, _RBGY_GIT_BRANCH, _RBGY_GIT_REPO — main repo metadata (as today)
- _RBGY_RUBRIC_REPO, _RBGY_RUBRIC_COMMIT — mini-repo URL and HEAD (new)
  Note: rubric repo facts are populated later by inscribe after mini-repo push;
  stitch generates placeholders, inscribe fills them before committing YAML.

Tag construction in rbgjb01: TAG_BASE="${_RBGY_INSCRIBE_TIMESTAMP}-b$(date -u +%Y%m%d_%H%M%S)"
Format example: i20260224_153022-b20260224_160530

Output YAML structure matching trigger-based builds:
- Bake all builder image pins (digest-pinned refs from RBRR)
- Deterministic: same inputs → byte-identical output
- Use $BUILD_ID only in Cloud Build's own logging, not in tags

## Add zrbf_check_pin_freshness()

Trivial date comparison: read RBRR_GCB_PINS_REFRESHED_AT, fail if older than
~2 days. Called by inscribe before generating yaml.

## References

- Tools/rbw/rbgc_Constants.sh — add RBGC_RUBRIC_* constants
- Tools/rbw/rbf_Foundry.sh — zrbf_stitch_build_json() (modify), zrbf_kindle() (add derived vars)
- Tools/rbw/rbrr_cli.sh — rbrr_refresh_gcb_pins (modify)
- Tools/rbw/rbrr_regime.sh — add pin timestamp enrollment, remove trigger pattern
- rbrr.env — remove RBRR_GCB_TRIGGER_PATTERN, add RBRR_GCB_PINS_REFRESHED_AT
- Tools/rbw/rbgjb/rbgjb01-derive-tag-base.sh — dual-timestamp tag construction
- Tools/rbw/rbgjb/*.sh — step script inputs (unchanged, consumed as templates)

## Add kindle constants for mini-repo naming

- RBGC_RUBRIC_CLONE_DIR — local clone root (".rbk")

These are derived at kindle time from constants + loaded vessel config:
- ZRBF_RUBRIC_REPO_NAME = RBGC_RUBRIC_REPO_PREFIX + RBRV_SIGIL
- ZRBF_RUBRIC_CLONE_PATH = RBGC_RUBRIC_CLONE_DIR + "/" + RBRV_SIGIL

regime variable enrollment in rbrr_regime.sh.

## Modify zrbf_stitch_build_json → yaml output

Adapt the existing stitch function to emit cloudbuild.yaml instead of JSON.
Same inputs: step scripts (rbgjb/*.sh) + pins (RBRR_GCB_*_IMAGE_REF) + vessel
config (RBRV_*). Different output format: static YAML with all values baked.

Key changes:
- Output YAML structure matching rbev-busybox/cloudbuild.yaml reference
- Bake inscribe timestamp into tag template (e.g., i20260223.143022)
- Use $BUILD_ID (Cloud Build built-in) for per-build uniqueness — zero custom substitutions
- Bake all GAR coordinates, vessel identity, platforms, ark suffixes
- Bake all builder image pins (digest-pinned refs from RBRR)
- Deterministic: same inputs → byte-identical output

Trivial date comparison: read RBRR_GCB_PINS_REFRESHED_AT, fail if older than
~2 days. Called by inscribe before generating yaml.

- Overall structure: 5 phases clearly separated, logging adequate, failure modes handled

**[260225-1953] rough**

Implement the inscribe command as a batch-all-vessels operation per RBSRI spec.

No vessel argument — inscribe always processes all conjure vessels.
Non-conjure vessels (no RBRV_CONJURE_DOCKERFILE) are skipped.

Mint colophon per prefix discipline. Wire through rbz_zipper.sh and
rbw_workbench.sh. No imprint (no vessel argument).

## Inscribe flow (per revised RBSRI)

1. rbrr_refresh_gcb_pins() — rate-limited to 1/day (skip if recent)
2. For each conjure vessel in rbev-vessels/:
   a. zrbf_load_vessel() (existing) — load vessel config
   b. Capture main repo metadata: git commit, branch, repo URL
   c. Extended stitch (from AiAAU) — generate cloudbuild.json to vessel dir
      - Bakes _RBGY_INSCRIBE_TIMESTAMP with current UTC timestamp
      - Bakes all _RBGY_* from regime + vessel config
      - Leaves _RBGY_RUBRIC_REPO/_RUBRIC_COMMIT as placeholders
3. Verify ALL committed — compare each generated JSON against committed copy
   - If any differ: STOP, list which vessels are stale, instruct operator
   - All-or-nothing: all must match before proceeding
4. Always-fresh-clone: delete local clone, git clone --depth 1 the
   {rbtgr_rubric_repo} using {rbra_rubric_repo_url}
5. For each conjure vessel: copy cloudbuild.json + Dockerfile + build context
   to per-vessel directory in clone
6. Fill _RBGY_RUBRIC_REPO and _RBGY_RUBRIC_COMMIT in all clone copies
7. ONE commit and push for all vessels
8. For each conjure vessel:
   a. Create {rbtgi_source_link} if needed (Developer Connect REST API)
   b. Create {rbtgr_vessel_trigger} if needed (Cloud Build REST API)
      Trigger name: RBGC_RUBRIC_TRIGGER_PREFIX + vessel sigil

## Vessel mode detection

Skip non-conjure vessels by checking for RBRV_CONJURE_DOCKERFILE in rbrv.env.
Currently only conjure mode is implemented; trbim-macos is a non-conjure vessel.

## Inscribe flow (per revised RBSRI)

1. rbrr_refresh_gcb_pins() — rate-limited to 1/day (skip if recent)

   a. zrbf_load_vessel() (existing) — load vessel config
   b. Capture main repo metadata: git commit, branch, repo URL
   c. Extended stitch (from AiAAU) — generate cloudbuild.json to vessel dir
      - Bakes _RBGY_INSCRIBE_TIMESTAMP with current UTC timestamp
      - Bakes all _RBGY_* from regime + vessel config
      - Leaves _RBGY_RUBRIC_REPO/_RUBRIC_COMMIT as placeholders
3. Verify ALL committed — compare each generated JSON against committed copy
   - If any differ: STOP, list which vessels are stale, instruct operator
   - All-or-nothing: all must match before proceeding
4. Always-fresh-clone: delete local clone, git clone --depth 1 the
   {rbtgr_rubric_repo} using {rbra_rubric_repo_url}
5. For each conjure vessel: copy cloudbuild.json + Dockerfile + build context
   to per-vessel directory in clone
6. Fill _RBGY_RUBRIC_REPO and _RBGY_RUBRIC_COMMIT in all clone copies
7. ONE commit and push for all vessels
8. For each conjure vessel:
   a. Create {rbtgi_source_link} if needed (Developer Connect REST API)
   b. Create {rbtgr_vessel_trigger} if needed (Cloud Build REST API)
      Trigger name: RBGC_RUBRIC_TRIGGER_PREFIX + vessel sigil

**[260224-0643] rough**

Implement the inscribe command as a new tabtarget. This is the single rubric
lifecycle operation — it ensures a vessel's build definition is fully set up
and synced. Reuses existing functions (vessel loading, modified stitch) and
adds genuinely new orchestration (mini-repo management, trigger creation).

## New tabtarget

Mint colophon per prefix discipline. Wire through rbz_zipper.sh and
rbw_workbench.sh. Takes vessel directory as argument.

## Inscribe flow

1. zrbf_check_pin_freshness() — fail if RBRR_GCB_PINS_REFRESHED_AT too old
2. zrbf_load_vessel() (existing) — load vessel config from rbrv.env
3. Capture main repo metadata: git commit, branch, repo URL
4. Modified stitch (from ₢AiAAU) — generate cloudbuild.yaml to vessel dir
   - Bakes _RBGY_INSCRIBE_TIMESTAMP with current UTC timestamp
   - Bakes _RBGY_GIT_COMMIT/BRANCH/REPO from main repo
   - Leaves _RBGY_RUBRIC_REPO/_RUBRIC_COMMIT as placeholders
5. Verify generated yaml matches what is committed and pushed in main repo
   - If different: STOP, tell user to review diff, commit, and push
   - On rerun: deterministic generation produces identical yaml → matches → proceed
6. Clone/pull vessel mini-repo to ZRBF_RUBRIC_CLONE_PATH (.rbk/{vessel}/)
   - Mini-repo name: ZRBF_RUBRIC_REPO_NAME (from kindle constants)
   - If mini-repo doesn't exist on GitHub: create via REST API
7. Sync main repo → mini-repo: copy cloudbuild.yaml + Dockerfile + build context
8. Fill _RBGY_RUBRIC_REPO and _RBGY_RUBRIC_COMMIT in the mini-repo's copy
   of cloudbuild.yaml (sed or equivalent — these are the only non-deterministic values)
9. Git commit + push mini-repo
10. Create Developer Connect repo link for this mini-repo if it doesn't exist
    - Uses RBRR_GDC_CONNECTION_NAME + RBRR_GDC_REGION
    - Repo link binds the connection to this specific mini-repo
11. Create Cloud Build trigger if it doesn't exist
    - Trigger name: ZRBF_RUBRIC_TRIGGER_NAME (RBGC constant prefix + vessel sigil)
    - Trigger references the repo link from step 10
    - Trigger points to cloudbuild.yaml in the mini-repo

## Genuinely new code

- Mini-repo management: create GitHub repo (REST API), clone, sync files, commit, push
- Developer Connect repo link creation: REST API (per-vessel)
- Trigger creation: REST API POST to cloudbuild.googleapis.com
- Pin freshness gate wiring
- Tabtarget + zipper + workbench wiring
- Rubric repo metadata backfill into mini-repo YAML copy

## Reused existing code

- zrbf_load_vessel() — unchanged
- Modified stitch from ₢AiAAU — yaml generation
- Kindle constants from ₢AiAAU — RBGC_RUBRIC_* naming
- rbgo_get_token_capture() — OAuth for GCP/GitHub API calls

## Design notes

- Fresh vessel (no mini-repo, no trigger, no repo link): inscribe creates all three
- Existing vessel (all exist): inscribe updates yaml + syncs
- Same command handles both cases
- .rbk/ is gitignored in main repo (parallels .buk/ pattern)
- Main repo copy of cloudbuild.yaml has placeholder rubric repo values;
  mini-repo copy has real values filled in by inscribe

## References

- Tools/rbw/rbf_Foundry.sh — modified stitch, vessel loading, kindle constants
- Tools/rbw/rbgc_Constants.sh — RBGC_RUBRIC_* naming patterns
- Tools/rbw/rbz_zipper.sh — enrollment wiring
- Tools/rbw/rbw_workbench.sh — command routing
- rbrr.env — GDC connection (RBRR_GDC_CONNECTION_NAME, RBRR_GDC_REGION)

### modify-rbf-build-for-trigger-dispatch (₢AiAAW) [complete]

**[260227-0946] complete**

Modify rbf_build() to dispatch via triggers.run instead of builds.create,
per the rewritten RBSTB spec and paddock session decisions.

## Remove from rbf_build()

Everything in paddock "What Dies": tarball packaging, GCS upload, JSON build
request composition, builds.create submission, git-clean verification.

## Add to rbf_build()

- Always-fresh-clone: delete .rbk/rubric/{vessel}/, git clone --depth 1 the
  {rbtgr_rubric_repo} (same pattern as inscribe — no dependency on inscribe
  having been run locally)
- Read HEAD commit from fresh clone: git rev-parse HEAD
- Derive trigger name from RBGC_RUBRIC_TRIGGER_PREFIX + vessel sigil
- POST triggers.run with source.commitSha — zero substitution overrides
- Parse response for build ID (triggers.run returns Operation)

## Keep in rbf_build()

zrbf_load_vessel(), quota check, zrbf_wait_build_completion(), OAuth, reporting.

## Simplify zrbf_kindle()

Remove tarball/GCS/JSON build request temp variables. Keep API endpoint base
and polling variables.

## References

- Tools/rbw/rbf_Foundry.sh — rbf_build() (modify), zrbf_kindle() (simplify)
- lenses/RBSTB-trigger_build.adoc — authoritative behavior spec
- Cloud Build triggers.run: https://cloud.google.com/build/docs/api/reference/rest/v1/projects.triggers/run

**[260224-0643] rough**

Modify the existing rbf_build() to dispatch via triggers.run instead of
builds.create. This is surgery on an existing function, not a new implementation.

## Remove from rbf_build()

- zrbf_package_context() call and all tarball logic
- zrbf_compose_tarball_name() call
- zrbf_upload_context_to_gcs() call
- zrbf_compose_build_request_json() call
- zrbf_submit_build_json() call
- zrbf_verify_git_clean() call (inscribe already synced mini-repo)
- Build config JSON composition (substitutions block)
- All ZRBF_BUILD_CONTEXT_TAR, ZRBF_BUILD_CONFIG_FILE references

## Add to rbf_build()

- Derive trigger name: ZRBF_RUBRIC_TRIGGER_NAME (RBGC_RUBRIC_TRIGGER_PREFIX + vessel sigil,
  computed at kindle time from constant — no RBRR_GCB_TRIGGER_PATTERN)
- Query cloudbuild.googleapis.com to resolve trigger ID from trigger name
- Read mini-repo HEAD commit from ZRBF_RUBRIC_CLONE_PATH
- POST triggers.run with source.commitSha from mini-repo HEAD
  - Endpoint: cloudbuild.googleapis.com/v1/projects/{project}/locations/{location}/triggers/{id}:run
  - Zero custom substitution overrides — all values baked in committed YAML
  - Only specify which commit to build from
- Parse response to get build ID (triggers.run returns Operation)

## Keep in rbf_build()

- zrbf_load_vessel() — still need vessel config
- Quota check (rbgd_check_gcb_quota) — still valuable
- zrbf_wait_build_completion() — polling logic unchanged
- OAuth token acquisition — still needed for API calls
- Success/failure reporting

## Also simplify zrbf_kindle()

- Remove temp file variables for tarball, build config, build request
- Remove GCS staging bucket references
- Keep kindle constants: ZRBF_RUBRIC_TRIGGER_NAME (from RBGC prefix + vessel sigil)
- Keep: API endpoint base, build status polling variables

## References

- Tools/rbw/rbf_Foundry.sh — rbf_build() (modify), zrbf_kindle() (simplify)
- Tools/rbw/rbgc_Constants.sh — RBGC_RUBRIC_TRIGGER_PREFIX (from ₢AiAAU)
- Cloud Build triggers.run: https://cloud.google.com/build/docs/api/reference/rest/v1/projects.triggers/run

- zrbf_submit_build_json() call

- Trigger lookup: derive trigger name from RBRR_GCB_TRIGGER_PATTERN + vessel sigil,
  query cloudbuild.googleapis.com to resolve trigger ID
- Read mini-repo HEAD commit from ZRBF_RUBRIC_CLONE_PATH (kindle constant + vessel sigil)
- POST triggers.run with source.commitSha from mini-repo HEAD
  - Endpoint: cloudbuild.googleapis.com/v1/projects/{project}/locations/{location}/triggers/{id}:run
  - Zero custom substitution overrides — yaml is fully baked
  - Only specify which commit to build from
- Parse response to get build ID (triggers.run returns Operation)

## Keep in rbf_build()

- zrbf_load_vessel() — still need vessel config
- Quota check (rbgd_check_gcb_quota) — still valuable
- zrbf_wait_build_completion() — polling logic unchanged
- OAuth token acquisition — still needed for API calls
- Success/failure reporting

## Also simplify zrbf_kindle()

- Remove temp file variables for tarball, build config, build request
- Remove GCS staging bucket references
- Add kindle constants: ZRBF_RUBRIC_REPO_NAME, ZRBF_RUBRIC_CLONE_PATH (from ₢AiAAU)
- Keep: API endpoint base, build status polling variables

## References

- Tools/rbw/rbf_Foundry.sh — rbf_build() (modify), zrbf_kindle() (simplify)
- Tools/rbw/rbgc_Constants.sh — RBGC_RUBRIC_* naming patterns (from ₢AiAAU)
- https://cloud.google.com/build/docs/api/reference/rest/v1/projects.triggers/run

**[260223-1823] rough**

builds.create. This is surgery on an existing function, not a new implementation.

### fix-binfmt-policy-for-remote-build (₢AiAAi) [complete]

**[260227-0956] complete**

Fix binfmt policy check in rbf_build() to validate against Cloud Build
runner architecture instead of the local machine.

Current code compares RBRV_CONJURE_PLATFORMS against `uname -m` (the
Mac running the CLI). With trigger dispatch, builds execute on Cloud
Build (linux/amd64), so the local architecture is irrelevant.

## What to change

- In rbf_build(), replace the `uname -s`/`uname -m` binfmt check with
  a check against the Cloud Build runner platform (linux/amd64)
- The RBRV_CONJURE_BINFMT_POLICY="forbid" gate should die if the vessel
  requests platforms beyond linux/amd64 (the Cloud Build default pool arch)
- If private pools land with different architectures, this check will
  need to account for the pool's machine type

## References

- Tools/rbw/rbf_Foundry.sh — rbf_build() binfmt policy block (~line 658)
- rbrv.env RBRV_CONJURE_BINFMT_POLICY, RBRV_CONJURE_PLATFORMS

### implement-prepare-step (₢AiAAI) [abandoned]

**[260223-1820] abandoned**

Implement the prepare step in the Foundry for trigger-based builds.

## Preconditions (fail-fast before expensive operations)

1. Verify {rbtgi_source_connection} health via REST API:
   - GET connection resource, assert installationState.stage == "COMPLETE"
   - GET {rbtgi_source_link} resource, assert cloneUri matches expected repo
   - Fail with clear message: "Developer Connect connection not healthy — run RBSGD procedure"
   - Uses RBRR_GDC_CONNECTION_NAME, RBRR_GDC_REGION, RBRR_GDC_REPO_LINK, RBRR_DEPOT_PROJECT_ID

2. Verify the vessel's {rbtgr_build_yaml} exists in the vessel directory

3. {rbtgo_rubric_assay} — regenerate {rbtgr_build_yaml} to a temp location and diff
   against committed version. If stale: fail with message to inscribe and commit before building.

4. Verify main repo working tree is clean (no uncommitted changes)

## Push to origin

- Push current HEAD to origin (so Cloud Build checks out the right commit from GitHub)
- If HEAD already matches origin: skip push. If diverged: push and report.
- Adapts existing zrbf_verify_git_clean to also verify/ensure origin is current

## Context

This is the key workflow change from builds.create: the old flow uploaded a tarball
directly, so the repo didn't need to be pushed. Now Cloud Build fetches from GitHub
via {rbtgi_source_connection}, so the Foundry must ensure the commit is on origin
before dispatching via {rbtgr_vessel_trigger}.

The {rbtgi_source_connection} health check prevents mysterious trigger failures when
Developer Connect is not configured or has gone stale. Fail early with actionable guidance.

## References

- lenses/RBSGD-gdc_establish.adoc — REST API health check endpoints (step 6)
- Tools/rbw/rbf_Foundry.sh — existing zrbf_verify_git_clean
- rbrr.env — GDC regime variables

**[260222-1503] rough**

Implement the "prepare" step in the Foundry (new phase before dispatch):
- Clone vessel repo to .rbk/ if not already present (git clone over HTTPS with Courier PAT)
- Copy Dockerfile + build context from parent repo (rbev-vessels/{sigil}/) to vessel repo clone
- Generate/update cloudbuild.yaml with current RBRR pin values baked in
  (pins are regime-level, so YAML regeneration reads RBRR and writes updated refs)
- Pin staleness check: balk if pins are older than 1 day
- Commit and push changes via local git operations (git commit + git push over HTTPS)
  Note: this is git protocol, not GitHub REST API — REST API is for repo management only
- BCG compliance for all scripting

This is the "publish ceremony" — changes flow from parent repo to vessel repo.
Dockerfiles live in parent repo (source of truth). Vessel repo is a derived artifact.
The .rbk/ directory is gitignored in parent repo, parallels .buk/ pattern.

Two outputs committed to vessel repo:
1. Dockerfile + build context (copied from parent)
2. cloudbuild.yaml (generated with current pins baked in)

### reconcile-rbscb-roadmap (₢AiAAd) [complete]

**[260227-1043] complete**

Reconcile RBSCB-CloudBuildRoadmap.adoc with implemented reality after all
preceding paces have landed. This is a document-only pace.

## Goals

1. **Eliminate the Decision Log section.** Fold each decision into the relevant
   tier body text as crisp, authoritative statements. The roadmap should read as
   a coherent plan, not a plan plus a changelog.

2. **Align Tier 2 with implementation.** The body should reflect:
   - Single rubric repo with per-vessel directories (not main-repo triggers)
   - Fully-baked cloudbuild.json (not yaml, not dynamic substitution overrides)
   - Inscribe as the lifecycle command (batch all vessels, refresh pins, sync rubric repo)
   - Build context copied to rubric repo (Dockerfile + context per vessel directory)
   - Developer Connect + OAuth (not gcloud)
   - Context scope *narrows* (rubric repo only) — this is better for Tiers 3-5

3. **Fix stale Tier 1 references.** Build log hygiene was folded into Tier 2
   (audit during script inlining). Dockerfile base image digest validation is
   deferred (not SLSA v1.0 required, separate future heat). BuildKit provenance
   flag deferred. Update body text to match.

4. **Verify Tiers 3-5 still hold.** Premises were not broken by implementation
   changes, but descriptions may reference stale details (e.g., "trigger checks
   out the entire repo" — now false, rubric repo narrows scope).

5. **Verify RBSCB include in RBS0.** Session 5 fixed a duplicate include
   (replaced with RBSCJ). Confirm still clean.

## Scope

- Touch: lenses/RBSCB-CloudBuildRoadmap.adoc, include-references in RBS0
- Do NOT touch: paddock, implementation specs (RBSRI, RBSTB, etc.)

## Approach

Re-read RBSCB fresh. Do not apply a mechanical diff list — by the time this
pace runs, earlier paces will have changed other things. Rebuild confidence
in the roadmap by reading it as a newcomer would and fixing what doesn't
match reality.

### private-pool-wire-build-json (₢AiAAf) [complete]

**[260227-1106] complete**

Wire Private Pool into build JSON generation and expand machine type support.

## Stitch function

In zrbf_stitch_build_json(), conditionally add `options.pool.name` when
RBRR_GCB_PRIVATE_POOL_NAME is non-empty. The pool resource name format:
`projects/{project}/locations/{region}/workerPools/{pool}`

When pool is set:
```json
"options": {
  "logging": "CLOUD_LOGGING_ONLY",
  "pool": { "name": "projects/.../workerPools/..." }
}
```

When pool is empty (default pool, current behavior):
```json
"options": {
  "logging": "CLOUD_LOGGING_ONLY",
  "machineType": "..."
}
```

Note: machineType goes in options for default pool but is configured on the
pool resource itself for private pools. The JSON structure differs.

## Machine type expansion

Private pools unlock E2_STANDARD_* types not available on default pool.
Add to rbgc_gcb_machine_vcpus_capture() in rbgc_Constants.sh:
- E2_STANDARD_2 → 2
- E2_STANDARD_4 → 4
- E2_STANDARD_8 → 8
- E2_STANDARD_16 → 16
- E2_STANDARD_32 → 32

## Manual procedures

Update rbgm_ManualProcedures.sh quota guidance to mention private pool
quota metric name when applicable.

## Files

- Tools/rbw/rbf_Foundry.sh — conditional pool in stitch options
- Tools/rbw/rbgc_Constants.sh — E2_STANDARD_* in vCPU mapping
- Tools/rbw/rbgm_ManualProcedures.sh — quota guidance update

## Verify

- bash -n Tools/rbw/rbf_Foundry.sh
- bash -n Tools/rbw/rbgc_Constants.sh
- Inspect generated cloudbuild.json with and without pool name set

### recreate-depot-fresh-devconnect (₢AiAAj) [complete]

**[260227-1532] complete**

Destroy current depot and recreate from scratch to exercise all updated
initialization code paths added during this heat.

## Destroy existing depot

Run depot destroy to tear down the current proto2 depot cleanly.

## Create fresh depot

Run depot create — this now includes Developer Connect connection creation
(automated, leaves connection in PENDING state).

## Run depot_initialize

Complete the Developer Connect OAuth authorization (browser step).
Validate rubric repo URL reachability.
Verify connection reaches COMPLETE state.

## Configure Director RBRA

Ensure RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL is set in Director RBRA (station secrets).
This was a manual step discovered during e2e verification — the Governor
had it but the Director did not.

- Developer Connect connection COMPLETE
- Rubric repo URL reachable from Director RBRA
- GCB pins fresh
- All triggers can be created (inscribe infrastructure phase)

### fix-trigger-create-propagation (₢AiAAn) [complete]

**[260301-0951] complete**

Fix Cloud Build trigger creation in inscribe Phase 5.

## Problem

`rbf_rubric_inscribe()` trigger creation fails with HTTP 403:
"failed to get service account gaia id" when specifying the Mason SA
in the trigger's `serviceAccount` field.

The Mason SA was just created during depot provisioning. Cloud Build's
internal lookup of the SA's gaia ID hasn't propagated yet. The inscribe
code has no propagation check for this — it assumes the Mason SA is
immediately resolvable by Cloud Build.

## Context from this session

- Source link creation now works (roles/developerconnect.admin granted to Director)
- Trigger API parameter fixed (name in body, not triggerId query param)
- Trigger list-and-check for idempotency uses BCG-compliant bash builtins
- All 7 trigger creates fail with the same gaia id error

## Investigation needed

1. Determine if this is a propagation delay or a missing IAM binding
   - The Cloud Build service agent has `roles/iam.serviceAccountTokenCreator`
     on Mason SA (granted in depot_create)
   - The Director SA has `roles/iam.serviceAccountUser` on Mason SA
     (granted in create_director)
   - Check if Cloud Build triggers.create needs a different permission path
2. Research the Cloud Build trigger serviceAccount field requirements
   - Does it need just the email, not the full resource path?
   - Is there a specific propagation pattern for trigger SA resolution?
3. Look at how existing codebase handles SA propagation delays
   (e.g., `zrbgp_*` verification loops, LRO polling patterns)

## Acceptance criteria

- Inscribe creates all 7 triggers successfully on a fresh depot
- Propagation is handled with verification, not sleep-and-pray
- BCG compliant: temp files, stderr capture, buc_step visibility

## Key files

- `Tools/rbw/rbf_Foundry.sh` (inscribe trigger creation, ~line 1252-1310)
- `Tools/rbw/rbgp_Payor.sh` (depot_create Mason SA + CB agent setup, ~line 747-779)
- `Tools/rbw/rbgg_Governor.sh` (create_director SA permissions, ~line 599-625)
- `Tools/rbw/rbgd_DepotConstants.sh` (RBGD_MASON_EMAIL derivation)

### numeric-id-iam-bindings (₢AiAAp) [complete]

**[260301-1036] complete**

Eliminate GAIA propagation race in IAM bindings by using SA numeric ID.

## Problem

When a service account is created via IAM API, cross-service identity resolution
(IAM→Artifact Registry, IAM→Cloud Storage) takes seconds to minutes. Using
`serviceAccount:EMAIL` as the member in setIamPolicy calls on other services
races against GAIA propagation. The `serviceAccount:NUMERIC_ID` form is
immediately resolvable per Google's own documentation.

## Changes

### rbgp_Payor.sh (depot_create)

1. Capture `uniqueId` from Mason SA creation response (in addition to email)
2. Remove the `rbgu_poll_get_until_ok` propagation poll (lines 743-745) — no longer needed
3. Use `serviceAccount:NUMERIC_ID` in all four Mason IAM member bindings:
   - `rbgi_add_repo_iam_role` (AR writer)
   - `rbgi_add_bucket_iam_role` (GCS viewer)
   - `rbgi_add_project_iam_role` × 2 (project viewer, logs writer)
4. Keep email for `rbgi_add_sa_iam_role` target URL (Mason is the resource,
   not the member; IAM→IAM is fast; 4 API calls elapsed by that point)
5. Keep email for display output (line 813)

### rbgg_Governor.sh (create_retriever, create_director)

1. Modify `zrbgg_create_service_account_with_key` (line 174):
   - Capture `uniqueId` from SA creation response
   - Replace email-based GET verify (line 208) with uniqueId-based URL
     (`projects/-/serviceAccounts/${uniqueId}`) — eliminates email
     resolution dependency
   - Remove the 15-second hard sleep (`rbgu_newly_created_delay`, line 205)
   - Echo `uniqueId` to stdout (all logging already goes to stderr per BCG)
2. Callers capture uniqueId: `z_sa_uid=$(zrbgg_create_service_account_with_key ...)`
3. Use `serviceAccount:${z_sa_uid}` in all IAM member bindings for the
   newly-created SA in both `rbgg_create_retriever` and `rbgg_create_director`

### rbgg_Governor.sh (dead code)

Delete `zrbgg_create_service_account_no_key()` (line 284) — defined but never
called anywhere in the codebase.

### rbgi_IAM.sh (dead code elimination)

1. Remove the HTTP 400 "does not exist" retry loop from
   `rbgi_add_bucket_iam_role` (lines 326-350)
2. Also removes 429/500-504 transient retry handling — intentional: this
   matches `rbgi_add_repo_iam_role` which has no transient handling either.
   Transient retries across all four IAM functions is a separate concern.
3. Simplify to single setIamPolicy call matching `rbgi_add_repo_iam_role` pattern

### rbgu_Utility.sh (dead code elimination)

Delete `rbgu_newly_created_delay()` (line 480) — after removing both call sites
in `rbgg_Governor.sh` (lines 205, 312), this function has zero callers.

## Exclusion boundary

Do NOT change IAM bindings where the member is a Google-provisioned service
agent (`z_cb_service_agent`, `z_devconnect_service_agent` in Payor;
`z_cb_service_agent` in Governor). These SAs are managed by Google, not newly
created — they have no propagation race. Only newly-created SAs (Mason,
Retriever, Director) need numeric ID treatment.

## Acceptance criteria

- depot_create uses numeric ID for all Mason member bindings
- Governor create_retriever/create_director use numeric ID for all member bindings
- Google-provisioned service agent bindings unchanged
- No propagation polls or hard sleeps after SA creation
- No retry-on-400 "does not exist" loop in bucket IAM function
- `zrbgg_create_service_account_no_key` deleted
- `rbgu_newly_created_delay` deleted
- Existing tests pass (if any)

## Key files

- Tools/rbw/rbgp_Payor.sh (depot_create, lines 720-813)
- Tools/rbw/rbgg_Governor.sh (lines 174-282, 284-321, 512-643)
- Tools/rbw/rbgi_IAM.sh (rbgi_add_bucket_iam_role, lines 289-353)
- Tools/rbw/rbgu_Utility.sh (rbgu_newly_created_delay, lines 480-494)

- depot_create uses numeric ID for all Mason member bindings
- Governor create_retriever/create_director use numeric ID for all member bindings
- No propagation polls or hard sleeps after SA creation
- No retry-on-400 "does not exist" loop in bucket IAM function
- RBS0 sections for depot_create, create_director, create_retriever are current
- Existing tests pass (if any)

## Key files

- Tools/rbw/rbgp_Payor.sh
- Tools/rbw/rbgg_Governor.sh
- Tools/rbw/rbgi_IAM.sh
- lenses/RBS0-SpecTop.adoc

   Connect OAuth flow

### diagnose-trigger-dispatch-commit-read (₢AiAAt) [complete]

**[260301-1248] complete**

Diagnose and fix: trigger dispatch returns HTTP 400 "Couldn't read commit".

## Symptoms

- Inscribe succeeded: rubric repo pushed (31881d91), source link created
  (bhyslop-rb-rubric), all 7 triggers created on depot 260301-05
- Build dispatch immediately fails with HTTP 400 "Couldn't read commit "
  (note trailing space — commit hash is EMPTY in the error message)
- The commit hash (31881d91) was resolved via git ls-remote seconds earlier
- Trigger name resolved correctly (rbw-trigger-rbev-busybox, HTTP 200 GET)
- NOT a propagation delay — same error after 2+ minutes

## Trigger Resource (from GET)

```json
{
  "id": "833453fa-60c1-4ce4-bec0-32eab8654bfc",
  "name": "rbw-trigger-rbev-busybox",
  "gitFileSource": {
    "path": "rbev-busybox/cloudbuild.json",
    "uri": "projects/rbwg-d-260301-05-260301111023/locations/us-central1/connections/rbw-260301-05-github/gitRepositoryLinks/bhyslop-rb-rubric",
    "repoType": "GITHUB",
    "revision": "refs/heads/main"
  },
  "sourceToBuild": {
    "uri": "projects/rbwg-d-260301-05-260301111023/locations/us-central1/connections/rbw-260301-05-github/gitRepositoryLinks/bhyslop-rb-rubric",
    "ref": "refs/heads/main",
    "repoType": "GITHUB"
  },
  "serviceAccount": "projects/.../serviceAccounts/mason-260301-05@..."
}
```

## Dispatch Request (what we send)

```
POST .../locations/us-central1/triggers/rbw-trigger-rbev-busybox:run
Body: {"source": {"commitSha": "31881d91edef9982f9a911663608efb095bf2b67"}}
```

## Dispatch Response

```json
{"error": {"code": 400, "message": "Couldn't read commit ", "status": "INVALID_ARGUMENT"}}
```

## Root Cause Analysis (in progress)

The `triggers.run` API request body takes a `RepoSource` object. `RepoSource` is a
**1st gen Cloud Source Repositories** concept — its `repoName` field means a CSR repo
name. Our trigger uses **2nd gen Developer Connect** (`sourceToBuild.uri` points to a
`gitRepositoryLinks` resource).

**Hypothesis**: For 2nd gen triggers, the `RepoSource` body format is not applicable.
The API is ignoring the `source.commitSha` field entirely (hence the empty commit in
the error message), because `RepoSource` has no meaning for a Developer Connect trigger.

## Experiment Plan

Try these alternatives for the dispatch body:

1. **Empty body** `{}` — let trigger use its configured `sourceToBuild.ref` (refs/heads/main)
2. **Branch name only**: `{"source": {"branchName": "main"}}` — minimal RepoSource
3. **Full RepoSource**: `{"source": {"branchName": "main", "repoName": "bhyslop-rb-rubric"}}` — long shot, CSR format

If none work, investigate the `projects.locations.builds.create` API with
`ConnectedRepository` source type as an alternative to `triggers.run`.

## Key References

- Code: Tools/rbw/rbf_Foundry.sh lines 454-480 (dispatch logic)
- Transcript: temp-buk/temp-20260301-115222-36588-117/
- Cloud Build triggers.run API: https://docs.cloud.google.com/build/docs/api/reference/rest/v1/projects.locations.triggers/run
- RepoSource: https://docs.cloud.google.com/build/docs/api/reference/rest/v1/RepoSource
- 2nd gen ConnectedRepository issue: https://github.com/googleapis/google-cloud-go/issues/9029
- "Couldn't read commit" forum: https://discuss.google.dev/t/gcp-cloudbuild-failed-to-trigger-build-couldnt-read-commit/100578

## Acceptance Criteria

- Root cause identified and documented
- Fix implemented in rbf_Foundry.sh (not a retry/delay workaround)
- Busybox build succeeds via trigger dispatch

**[260301-1151] rough**

Diagnose and fix: trigger dispatch returns HTTP 400 "Couldn't read commit".

## Symptoms

- Inscribe succeeded: rubric repo pushed (31881d91), source link created
  (bhyslop-rb-rubric), all 7 triggers created
- Build dispatch immediately fails: "Couldn't read commit"
- The commit hash (31881d91) was resolved via git ls-remote seconds earlier
- Trigger name resolved correctly (rbw-trigger-rbev-busybox)

## Investigation Areas

1. **Source link configuration**: Does the source link point to the correct
   rubric repo? Does it reference the right Developer Connect connection?
   Verify via REST API: GET the source link resource and inspect its fields.

2. **Trigger→source link binding**: Does the trigger's sourceToBuild or
   repoSource reference the correct source link and repo? GET the trigger
   resource and inspect.

3. **Developer Connect repo access**: Can Developer Connect actually read the
   rubric repo? The OAuth was just completed for this depot — verify the
   connection's installationState and the repo link's cloneUri.

4. **Commit reference format**: Is the commit hash being passed correctly in
   the triggers.run request? Check the dispatch JSON body in the transcript.

5. **Timing vs configuration**: This should NOT be treated as a propagation
   delay. The error "Couldn't read commit" suggests a configuration or access
   problem, not eventual consistency. Diagnose root cause before retrying.

## Key Files

- Tools/rbw/rbf_Foundry.sh (rbf_build, trigger dispatch logic)
- Transcript from failed build: check temp-buk for dispatch request/response

## Acceptance Criteria

- Root cause identified and documented
- Fix implemented (not a retry/delay workaround)
- Busybox build succeeds via trigger dispatch

### document-triggers-run-research (₢AiAAu) [complete]

**[260301-1503] complete**

Create lenses document RBSCTD-CloudBuildTriggerDispatch.adoc capturing:

## Content

1. **Root cause**: triggers.run REST API only accepts RepoSource (1st gen CSR type) in
   its protobuf schema (RunBuildTriggerRequest.source). Structural limitation, not a bug.
   Confirmed via Go GAPIC proto surface (Dec 2025) and live experiments.

2. **Two resource hierarchies**: Developer Connect gitRepositoryLinks
   (developerconnect.googleapis.com) vs Cloud Build v2 repositories
   (cloudbuild.googleapis.com/v2). Separate APIs, not interchangeable.
   Triggers only work with CB v2 repositories.

3. **Provenance implications**: SLSA v1.0 requires trigger-invoked builds.
   builds.create only produces v0.1. Trigger-based dispatch is mandatory for Tier 2.

4. **Decision**: Replace Developer Connect with Cloud Build v2
   connections/repositories. triggers.run + RepoSource is the supported path
   for CB v2 repository-backed triggers.

5. **Experimental evidence**: 3 triggers.run body formats all HTTP 400
   "Couldn't read commit " (empty commit — API ignores all RepoSource fields);
   builds.create + developerConnectConfig HTTP 200 but only v0.1 provenance.

6. **Web research references** (preserve full URLs with context):
   - Go GAPIC proto showing RunBuildTriggerRequest.source is RepoSource:
     https://pkg.go.dev/cloud.google.com/go/cloudbuild/apiv1/v2/cloudbuildpb#RunBuildTriggerRequest
   - Go GAPIC proto showing Source supports connected_repository and git_source:
     https://pkg.go.dev/cloud.google.com/go/cloudbuild/apiv1/v2/cloudbuildpb#Source
   - googleapis/google-cloud-go#9029 (requesting 2nd gen support for trigger/build requests):
     https://github.com/googleapis/google-cloud-go/issues/9029
   - Google provenance guide (trigger-invoked = v1.0, manual = v0.1 only):
     https://cloud.google.com/build/docs/securing-builds/generate-validate-build-provenance
   - Cloud Build buildType v1 (triggered vs inline provenance structure):
     https://cloud.google.com/build/gcb-buildtypes/google-worker/v1
   - CB v2 repositories API:
     https://cloud.google.com/build/docs/api/reference/rest/v2/projects.locations.connections.repositories
   - CB v2 repositories create:
     https://cloud.google.com/build/docs/api/reference/rest/v2/projects.locations.connections.repositories/create
   - Developer Connect gitRepositoryLinks API:
     https://cloud.google.com/developer-connect/docs/api/reference/rest/v1/projects.locations.connections.gitRepositoryLinks
   - Developer forums "Couldn't read commit" thread:
     https://discuss.google.dev/t/gcp-cloudbuild-failed-to-trigger-build-couldnt-read-commit/100578
   - 1st gen vs 2nd gen repo connections:
     https://cloud.google.com/build/docs/automating-builds/github/connect-repo-github
   - Cloud Build release notes (provenance tied to triggered builds):
     https://cloud.google.com/build/docs/release-notes
   - Artifact Analysis occurrences (provenance verification):
     https://cloud.google.com/artifact-analysis/docs/reference/rest/v1/projects.locations.occurrences

## Acceptance Criteria

- New lenses document authored with proper AsciiDoc structure
- All web research URLs preserved with context
- Experimental results documented
- Decision rationale clear for future readers

### investigate-cbv2-connection-setup (₢AiAAv) [complete]

**[260302-0713] complete**

Research Cloud Build v2 connection infrastructure to plan the Developer Connect replacement.

## Questions to Answer

1. Does a CB v2 connection require a SEPARATE GitHub OAuth authorization from
   Developer Connect, or can the same GitHub App installation be reused?
2. What does the CB v2 connection creation REST API look like?
   (POST cloudbuild.googleapis.com/v2/projects/{p}/locations/{r}/connections)
3. What OAuth flow is needed for CB v2 connections? Browser-based like DC?
4. What IAM permissions/roles are needed? (cloudbuild.connectionAdmin?)
5. What service agents need provisioning? Does CB v2 use the same
   cloudbuild service agent already provisioned, or a separate one?
6. Can we reuse RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL (PAT-in-URL) for git operations
   alongside the CB v2 connection (for trigger source binding)?

## Approach

- Read CB v2 REST API docs via web research
- Compare with existing Developer Connect setup in rbgp_Payor.sh and
  rbgm_ManualProcedures.sh
- Document findings in paddock addendum or pace docket update

## Acceptance Criteria

- All 6 questions answered with citations
- Clear mapping: what replaces what in depot_create and depot_initialize
- Regime variable plan: which RBRR_GDC_* vars to delete/rename

### specs-dc-to-cbv2-rewrite (₢AiAAz) [complete]

**[260302-0738] complete**

Update all specification documents to reflect the DC → CB v2 migration and
the architecture decisions in the 2026-03-02 paddock session.

This pace is standalone — pure documentation, no code changes. Can be executed
in any session with access to the paddock decisions.

## Spec Documents to Update

1. **RBS0-SpecTop.adoc**: Replace Developer Connect vocabulary with CB v2.
   - Linked terms: `rbtgi_source_connection` → CB v2 connection equivalent
   - Linked terms: `rbtgi_source_link` (gitRepositoryLinks) → CB v2 repository
   - Replace `RBRR_GDC_CONNECTION_NAME` → `RBRR_CBV2_CONNECTION_NAME`
   - Remove `RBRR_GDC_REGION` (use `RBGD_GCB_REGION`)
   - Replace `RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL` (PAT-in-URL) → `RBRR_RUBRIC_REPO_URL` (plain)
   - Add new constants: `RBGC_CBV2_PAT_SECRET_NAME`, `RBGC_CBV2_REPOSITORY_ID`
   - Document Secret Manager integration for PAT storage
   - Remove depot_initialize references

2. **RBSDC-depot_create.adoc**: Rewrite depot creation to show:
   - stdin input: PAT + GitHub App installation ID
   - Secret Manager secret creation and PAT storage
   - CB v2 connection creation (referencing secret version + installation ID)
   - CB v2 repository creation (referencing RBRR_RUBRIC_REPO_URL)
   - Inline GitHub guide when credentials not provided
   - Rubric repo URL validation (moved from depot_initialize)
   - Remove Developer Connect connection creation

3. **RBSDN-depot_initialize.adoc**: Retire this document. Add a header noting
   it is superseded — depot_initialize is dead (2026-03-02 paddock decision).
   Do not delete the file; mark it retired with rationale.

4. **RBSRI-rubric_inscribe.adoc**: Update inscribe flow:
   - PAT fetched from Secret Manager at runtime (not from RBRA)
   - Authenticated git URL constructed in memory, discarded after use
   - CB v2 repository check replaces DC gitRepositoryLinks creation
   - Triggers use `repositoryEventConfig.repository` (CB v2 path)

5. **RBSGD-gdc_establish.adoc**: Retire this document. Developer Connect
   establishment guide is obsolete — CB v2 replaces DC entirely.

6. **AXLA-Lexicon.adoc**: Update or replace `axig_developer_connect` motif.
   Add CB v2 terms if needed. Review linked terms for DC vocabulary.

### replace-devconnect-with-cbv2-depot (₢AiAAw) [complete]

**[260302-0835] complete**

Replace Developer Connect with Cloud Build v2 in depot lifecycle code.
Delete depot_initialize entirely.

## depot_create (rbgp_Payor.sh)

### Delete
- Developer Connect API enablement (`developerconnect.googleapis.com`)
- Developer Connect connection creation (POST to DC API)
- Developer Connect service agent provisioning
- All DC-specific URL construction and constants usage
- Output lines referencing `RBRR_GDC_CONNECTION_NAME`, `RBRR_GDC_REGION`

### Add
- `secretmanager.googleapis.com` API enablement
- Read PAT + GitHub App installation ID from stdin
- Inline guide displayed when stdin is empty (GitHub-focused, notes other hosts)
- Validate `RBRR_RUBRIC_REPO_URL` from regime using PAT (git ls-remote)
- Create Secret Manager secret (`RBGC_CBV2_PAT_SECRET_NAME`)
- Store PAT as secret version 1
- Grant Cloud Build service agent `roles/secretmanager.secretAccessor` on secret
- Create CB v2 connection (githubConfig with secret version ref + installation ID)
- Create CB v2 repository (remoteUri = `RBRR_RUBRIC_REPO_URL`)
- Output `RBRR_CBV2_CONNECTION_NAME` for operator to add to rbrr.env

### Update
- Output guidance: remove "Next: depot_initialize", update to reflect new flow

## depot_destroy (rbgp_Payor.sh)

### Add
- Delete CB v2 repository (tolerate 404)
- Delete CB v2 connection (tolerate 404)
- Delete Secret Manager secret (tolerate 404)

### Delete
- Developer Connect connection deletion

## Delete depot_initialize entirely

- Delete `rbgm_depot_initialize()` from rbgm_ManualProcedures.sh
- Delete tabtarget `tt/rbw-gdi.DepotInitialize.sh`
- Remove from rbgm_cli.sh dispatch
- Remove from rbz_zipper.sh enrollment

## Regime changes

- rbrr_regime.sh: replace `RBRR_GDC_CONNECTION_NAME` enrollment with `RBRR_CBV2_CONNECTION_NAME`
- rbrr_regime.sh: remove `RBRR_GDC_REGION` enrollment
- rbrr_regime.sh: add `RBRR_RUBRIC_REPO_URL` enrollment (required, URL format)
- rbra_regime.sh: remove `RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL` enrollment
- rbrr.env: update variable names
- rbgc_Constants.sh: add `RBGC_CBV2_PAT_SECRET_NAME`, `RBGC_CBV2_REPOSITORY_ID`
- rbgc_Constants.sh: remove DC API constants (`RBGC_API_ROOT_DEVELOPERCONNECT`, `RBGC_DEVELOPERCONNECT_V1`)

## Governor changes (rbgg_Governor.sh)

- `rbgg_create_director`: add `roles/secretmanager.secretAccessor` grant on PAT secret
- `zrbgg_rubric_preflight()`: replace DC check with CB v2 connection status check
- Remove DC-specific preflight logic

## Files touched

- Tools/rbw/rbgp_Payor.sh (depot_create, depot_destroy)
- Tools/rbw/rbgm_ManualProcedures.sh (delete depot_initialize)
- Tools/rbw/rbgm_cli.sh (remove dispatch)
- Tools/rbw/rbgg_Governor.sh (director creation, preflight)
- Tools/rbw/rbrr_regime.sh (variable enrollment)
- Tools/rbw/rbra_regime.sh (remove RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL)
- Tools/rbw/rbgc_Constants.sh (add CBV2, remove DC constants)
- Tools/rbw/rbgu_Utility.sh (remove DC utility functions if any)
- .rbk/rbrr.env (variable renames)
- Tools/rbw/rbz_zipper.sh (remove depot_initialize enrollment)
- tt/rbw-gdi.DepotInitialize.sh (delete)

## Acceptance Criteria

- depot_create creates CB v2 connection + repository via REST API
- PAT stored in Secret Manager, never on disk
- depot_destroy cleans up CB v2 + Secret Manager resources
- depot_initialize fully removed (function, tabtarget, dispatch, zipper)
- Regime validation passes with new variables
- No references to Developer Connect remain in code (except retired specs)
## Code Standards

All new bash code must be BCG-compliant (Tools/buk/vov_veiled/BCG-BashConsoleGuide.md).
Enterprise-grade orchestration patterns: buc_step/buc_info/buc_die for user interaction,
z-prefixed locals, proper error handling, no bare echo.

## IMPORTANT: Conditional on ₢AiAAv findings

infrastructure. The scope below is the EXPECTED plan — adjust based on actual findings.

fully removed or must coexist.

## Expected Scope

Based on findings from ₢AiAAv (investigate-cbv2-connection-setup):

1. **depot_create (rbgp_Payor.sh)**:
   - Likely remove: Developer Connect connection creation, DC service agent provisioning,
     DC Secret Manager grant (IF ₢AiAAv confirms CB v2 is fully independent)
   - Add: Cloud Build v2 connection creation (cloudbuild.googleapis.com/v2)
   - Add: any new IAM grants needed for CB v2 connections

2. **depot_initialize (rbgm_ManualProcedures.sh)**:
   - Likely remove: Developer Connect OAuth browser flow (IF CB v2 has its own OAuth)
   - Add: CB v2 connection OAuth browser flow (if different)
   - Keep: rubric repo URL validation (PAT-in-URL, independent of connection type)

3. **Regime variables (.rbk/rbrr.env, rbrr_regime.sh)**:
   - Likely delete: RBRR_GDC_CONNECTION_NAME, RBRR_GDC_REGION (if not needed)
   - Add: replacement variables for CB v2 connection identity (if needed)
   - Update validation in rbrr_regime.sh

4. **Constants (rbgc_Constants.sh)**:
   - Likely remove: RBGC_API_ROOT_DEVELOPERCONNECT, RBGC_DEVELOPERCONNECT_V1
   - Add: CB v2 API root/version constants

- depot_create creates CB v2 connection (with or without DC, per ₢AiAAv findings)
- depot_initialize completes CB v2 OAuth authorization
- Regime validation passes with updated variables
- No broken references to removed constants/variables

### update-inscribe-cbv2-repositories (₢AiAAx) [complete]

**[260302-1841] complete**

Update rubric inscribe to use CB v2 repositories and fetch PAT from Secret Manager.

## inscribe PAT retrieval (rbf_Foundry.sh)

### Delete
- Developer Connect source link (gitRepositoryLinks) GET/CREATE
- All DC API URL construction in inscribe flow
- Any reference to `RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL`

### Add
- Fetch PAT from Secret Manager at inscribe time:
  - GET `projects/{DEPOT}/secrets/{RBGC_CBV2_PAT_SECRET_NAME}/versions/latest`
  - Extract `payload.data` (base64-decoded) → PAT value
  - Uses Director OAuth token (Director SA has secretAccessor grant from create_director)
- Construct authenticated git URL in memory:
  `https://x-access-token:${PAT}@{host}/{path}` from `RBRR_RUBRIC_REPO_URL` + PAT
- Use for git clone/commit/push, discard after use

### Update
- Source link creation → CB v2 repository existence check
  - CB v2 repository was created by depot_create, should already exist
  - GET `projects/{P}/locations/{R}/connections/{C}/repositories/{RBGC_CBV2_REPOSITORY_ID}`
  - If missing, die with guidance to re-run depot_create
- Trigger creation body: use `repositoryEventConfig.repository` with CB v2 resource path
  instead of DC source link reference in `sourceToBuild` and `gitFileSource`
- Replace `RBRR_GDC_REGION` references with `RBGD_GCB_REGION`
- Replace `RBRR_GDC_CONNECTION_NAME` with `RBRR_CBV2_CONNECTION_NAME`

## Constants usage

- `RBGC_CBV2_PAT_SECRET_NAME` — secret name for Secret Manager GET
- `RBGC_CBV2_REPOSITORY_ID` — repository ID for CB v2 resource path construction
- CB v2 API root (cloudbuild.googleapis.com/v2) — add to RBGC if not present

## Files touched

- Tools/rbw/rbf_Foundry.sh (inscribe function — PAT retrieval, source link → CB v2 repo, trigger body)
- Tools/rbw/rbgc_Constants.sh (CB v2 API constants if needed)

## Acceptance Criteria

- Inscribe fetches PAT from Secret Manager (no RBRA dependency)
- Authenticated git URL constructed in memory, never written to disk
- CB v2 repository verified (not created — depot_create handles creation)
- Triggers reference CB v2 repository path in repositoryEventConfig
- No Developer Connect API calls remain in inscribe
- Inscribe completes successfully against depot with CB v2 connection

All new bash code must be BCG-compliant (Tools/buk/vov_veiled/BCG-BashConsoleGuide.md).
Enterprise-grade orchestration patterns: buc_step/buc_info/buc_die for user interaction,
z-prefixed locals, proper error handling, no bare echo.

## inscribe PAT retrieval (rbf_Foundry.sh)

- Developer Connect source link (gitRepositoryLinks) GET/CREATE
- All DC API URL construction in inscribe flow
- Any reference to `RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL`

### Add
- Fetch PAT from Secret Manager at inscribe time:
  - GET `projects/{DEPOT}/secrets/{RBGC_CBV2_PAT_SECRET_NAME}/versions/latest`
  - Extract `payload.data` (base64-decoded) → PAT value
  - Uses Director OAuth token (Director SA has secretAccessor grant from create_director)
- Construct authenticated git URL in memory:
  `https://x-access-token:${PAT}@{host}/{path}` from `RBRR_RUBRIC_REPO_URL` + PAT
- Use for git clone/commit/push, discard after use

### Update

  - CB v2 repository was created by depot_create, should already exist
  - GET `projects/{P}/locations/{R}/connections/{C}/repositories/{RBGC_CBV2_REPOSITORY_ID}`
  - If missing, die with guidance to re-run depot_create
- Trigger creation body: use `repositoryEventConfig.repository` with CB v2 resource path
  instead of DC source link reference in `sourceToBuild` and `gitFileSource`
- Replace `RBRR_GDC_REGION` references with `RBGD_GCB_REGION`
- Replace `RBRR_GDC_CONNECTION_NAME` with `RBRR_CBV2_CONNECTION_NAME`

- `RBGC_CBV2_PAT_SECRET_NAME` — secret name for Secret Manager GET
- `RBGC_CBV2_REPOSITORY_ID` — repository ID for CB v2 resource path construction
- CB v2 API root (cloudbuild.googleapis.com/v2) — add to RBGC if not present

### iam-propagation-resilience (₢AiAA6) [complete]

**[260303-1329] complete**

Author trade study RBSCIP-IamPropagation.adoc and implement retry-on-error
patterns for two GCP IAM eventual consistency failures in depot_create.

## Context

GCP IAM is eventually consistent. Google documents "typically 2 minutes,
up to 7+ minutes" for policy propagation. There is:
- No synchronous guarantee API
- No testIamPermissions probe for other principals (only tests caller)
- No force-propagation mechanism

Two failures surfaced during ₢AiAA0 E2E testing of depot_create:
1. Mason SA creation → setIamPolicy HTTP 400 "does not exist"
2. secretAccessor grant on CB service agent → CB v2 connection LRO fails
   with "could not access secret ... permission_denied"

Temporary placeholders from ₢AiAA0 (to be replaced by this pace):
- `rbgp_Payor.sh`: Mason SA propagation poll (line ~786) — keep as
  fast-path optimization, but it's insufficient alone
- `rbgp_Payor.sh`: `sleep 15` before CB v2 connection creation — remove

## Part 1: Trade Study RBSCIP-IamPropagation.adoc

Author as RBS0 trade study (alongside RBSCJ, RBSCB). Sections:

- Decision: retry-on-error for SA binding; impersonation readiness gate
  for secret access
- Rationale: sleep-and-pray is unreliable; retry tests the actual operation
- Evidence chain from Google docs:
  - IAM propagation: https://docs.cloud.google.com/iam/docs/access-change-propagation
  - SA create wait guidance: https://docs.cloud.google.com/iam/docs/service-accounts-create
  - testIamPermissions is caller-only: https://docs.cloud.google.com/iam/docs/testing-permissions
  - generateAccessToken: https://cloud.google.com/iam/docs/reference/credentials/rest/v1/projects.serviceAccounts/generateAccessToken
  - accessSecretVersion: https://cloud.google.com/secret-manager/docs/reference/rest/v1/projects.secrets.versions/access
- What Dies: fixed sleep delays, standalone propagation polls as gates
- What Survives: SA GET poll (fast-path, not correctness gate)

Include in RBS0: after RBSCJ include line (~line 3270), add:
```
[[rbscip_trade_study]]
=== IAM Propagation Resilience

include::RBSCIP-IamPropagation.adoc[]
```

## Part 2: Retry setIamPolicy on transient "does not exist"

Modify `rbgi_add_project_iam_role()` in Tools/rbw/rbgi_IAM.sh.

Current flow (lines ~82-112):
1. getIamPolicy (POST with requestedPolicyVersion:3)
2. jq to add member+role binding
3. setIamPolicy (POST with updated policy + etag)

New flow — wrap step 1-3 in retry loop:
- On HTTP 400 where response body contains "does not exist", retry
- Re-fetch getIamPolicy on each retry (fresh etag per research)
- Backoff: 3s initial, 2x multiplier, 20s cap, 420s (7min) deadline
- Only retry the specific error — all other 400s die immediately
- Log each retry with attempt count and elapsed time

Exact error to match (from actual failure):
```
Service account mason-demo1005@rbwg-d-demo1005-260303124803.iam.gserviceaccount.com does not exist.
```
Match pattern: HTTP 400 + response contains "does not exist"

BCG compliance:
- Use `while true` loop with `rbgu_http_json` + explicit code check
- Do NOT put rbgu_http_json in an `if` condition (BCG: only _predicate
  functions in conditionals)
- Check HTTP code via `rbgu_http_code_capture`, then branch
- All commands with explicit `|| buc_die`

Also apply the same retry pattern to `rbgi_add_sa_iam_role` and
`rbgi_add_bucket_iam_role` and `rbgi_add_repo_iam_role` if they use
the same get-modify-set pattern.

## Part 3: Impersonation readiness gate for Secret Manager

After granting CB service agent secretAccessor on the 3 secrets in
rbgp_Payor.sh, add a readiness gate before CB v2 connection creation:

Step A: Grant Payor serviceAccountTokenCreator on CB service agent
  - rbgi_add_sa_iam_role (existing function)
  - Payor needs this to impersonate the CB service agent

Step B: Mint token as CB service agent
  POST https://iamcredentials.googleapis.com/v1/projects/-/serviceAccounts/{CB_SA_EMAIL}:generateAccessToken
  Body: {"scope": ["https://www.googleapis.com/auth/cloud-platform"], "lifetime": "300s"}
  Returns: {"accessToken": "...", "expireTime": "..."}

Step C: Poll accessSecretVersion with impersonated token
  GET https://secretmanager.googleapis.com/v1/projects/{PROJECT}/secrets/{NAME}/versions/1:access
  Auth: Bearer {impersonated_token}
  Success = IAM propagated. Retry on 403 with same backoff profile.

Step D: Remove `sleep 15` placeholder, proceed to create connection

Defense-in-depth for CB v2 connection creation:
- On LRO failure, GET connection to check for zombie resource
- DELETE if exists (tolerate 404), then retry
- The existing LRO error checking from ₢AiAA0 catches this

## Files

- lenses/RBSCIP-IamPropagation.adoc (new)
- lenses/RBS0-SpecTop.adoc (add include)
- Tools/rbw/rbgi_IAM.sh (retry on transient 400)
- Tools/rbw/rbgp_Payor.sh (impersonation gate, remove sleep-15,
  CB v2 connection retry with zombie cleanup)
- Tools/rbw/rbgu_Utility.sh (no changes — LRO error checking already done)

## Acceptance Criteria

- Trade study authored with evidence chain
- setIamPolicy retries on "does not exist" with bounded backoff
- Impersonation readiness gate passes before CB v2 connection creation
- No fixed sleep delays in depot_create path
- BCG compliant: no _predicate violations, explicit error handling,
  no commands in conditionals

**[260303-1313] rough**

Author trade study RBSCIP-IamPropagation.adoc and implement retry-on-error
patterns for two GCP IAM eventual consistency failures in depot_create.

## Trade Study: RBSCIP-IamPropagation.adoc

Author and include in RBS0 trade studies section. Document:

- Problem: GCP IAM is eventually consistent (2-7+ min). No synchronous
  guarantee, no testIamPermissions probe, no force-propagation API.
- Failure mode 1: SA creation → setIamPolicy rejects "does not exist"
- Failure mode 2: secretAccessor grant → CB v2 connection can't read secret
- Decision: retry-on-error for SA bindings, impersonation readiness gate
  for Secret Manager access before CB v2 connection creation
- Evidence: Google docs confirm retry with backoff is the only option.
  testIamPermissions tests caller's permissions only, not another SA's.
  Impersonation via generateAccessToken + accessSecretVersion probes the
  exact permission the connection creation needs.

## Implementation 1: Retry setIamPolicy on transient "does not exist"

Modify rbgi_add_project_iam_role (and sibling IAM binding functions in
rbgi_IAM.sh) to retry on HTTP 400 containing "does not exist":
- Re-fetch getIamPolicy on each retry (fresh etag)
- Backoff: 1s initial, 2x multiplier, 20s cap, 10min deadline
- Only retry the specific "does not exist" error — all other 400s die fast
- Remove the Mason SA propagation poll added in ₢AiAA0 (insufficient alone,
  but the SA GET poll before it is harmless — keep as fast-path optimization)

## Implementation 2: Impersonation readiness gate for Secret Manager

After granting CB service agent secretAccessor on the 3 secrets:
1. Grant Payor serviceAccountTokenCreator on CB service agent
2. Use generateAccessToken to mint token as CB service agent
3. Poll accessSecretVersion with that token until success
4. Proceed to create CB v2 connection only after gate passes
- Backoff: same profile as implementation 1
- Remove the sleep-15 placeholder added in ₢AiAA0

Also: on CB v2 connection LRO failure, GET connection to check for zombie
resource, DELETE if exists before retry (defense-in-depth).

## Files

- lenses/RBSCIP-IamPropagation.adoc (new trade study)
- lenses/RBS0-SpecTop.adoc (add include)
- Tools/rbw/rbgi_IAM.sh (retry on transient 400)
- Tools/rbw/rbgp_Payor.sh (impersonation gate, remove sleep-15)

## Acceptance Criteria

- Trade study authored with evidence chain and references
- setIamPolicy retries on "does not exist" with bounded backoff
- CB v2 connection creation preceded by impersonation readiness gate
- No fixed sleep delays in depot_create
- depot_create succeeds on first run against a fresh depot

### bcg-local-readonly-depot-scripts (₢AiAA7) [complete]

**[260303-1411] complete**

Apply BCG `local -r` discipline to all bash scripts in the depot_create call chain.

BCG mandates `local -r` as the default for every local variable assigned once and
never modified. The four exceptions (loop counters, accumulators, two-line capture
patterns, reassigned-before-use) keep `local` without `-r`.

## Target files

- `Tools/rbw/rbgp_Payor.sh` — primary target, largest file, depot_create + depot_destroy + depot_list
- `Tools/rbw/rbgu_Utility.sh` — HTTP helpers, JSON helpers
- `Tools/rbw/rbgi_IAM.sh` — IAM grant functions with propagation retry
- `Tools/rbw/rbgo_OAuth.sh` — OAuth token exchange

`rbgc_Constants.sh` is excluded — it uses `readonly` at kindle scope per BCG, not `local -r`.

## Rules

For each `local z_*` declaration:
- If assigned once and never modified → change to `local -r`
- If loop counter or accumulator → leave as `local`
- If two-line capture pattern (`local z_foo; z_foo=$(cmd) || die`) → leave as `local`
- If reassigned later in function → leave as `local`

## Acceptance criteria

- Every single-assignment local in the four target files uses `local -r`
- No behavioral change — purely declarative
- No test failures (existing tabtargets still work)

### fix-trigger-push-filter-removes-auto-fire (₢AiABC) [complete]

**[260303-1751] complete**

Remove push filter from rubric triggers to prevent inscribe from auto-firing all 7 builds.

## Problem

Triggers are configured with `push: { branch: "^main$" }`. When inscribe pushes to the
rubric repo's main branch, all 7 triggers fire automatically. This is unintended — builds
should only dispatch via explicit `triggers.run` calls from `rbf_build`.

## Changes Required

### Code
- `rbf_Foundry.sh`: Remove the `push` object from the trigger creation jq block in
  `rbf_rubric_inscribe` (near line 1252). The trigger should have
  `repositoryEventConfig.repository` but NO `push` filter — manual-dispatch-only.
- Delete and recreate all 7 existing triggers on demo1015 depot (PATCH to remove a
  nested field is unreliable; delete+recreate is clean and idempotent since inscribe
  already handles "ensure trigger exists").

### Specs
- `lenses/RBSRI-rubric_inscribe.adoc`: Update trigger creation step to document that
  triggers are manual-dispatch-only (no push filter).
- `lenses/RBSTB-trigger_build.adoc`: Confirm dispatch-only semantics are documented.
- Paddock: Add session decision explaining why push triggers were removed (inscribe
  push fires all 7 builds unintentionally; explicit dispatch matches zero-override design).

### Verification
- After fix, inscribe push should NOT trigger any builds
- Manual `rbf_build` dispatch via `triggers.run` should still work
- Delete existing triggers, re-run inscribe to recreate without push filter

## Acceptance Criteria
- Trigger bodies have no `push` filter
- Inscribe push produces zero builds
- `rbf_build` dispatch still succeeds
- Specs updated to reflect manual-dispatch-only design

### fix-sbom-multi-platform-skopeo-split (₢AiABE) [complete]

**[260303-1812] complete**

Fix SBOM generation for multi-platform builds: split OCI archive with skopeo before Syft.

## Problem

Syft cannot scan multi-platform OCI layouts (anchore/syft#1545, still open).
Step 6 (sbom-and-summary) fails with:
  "unexpected media type: application/vnd.oci.image.index.v1+json"
The OCI Layout Bridge produces a multi-platform index; Syft expects a single image.

## Approach: Local skopeo split

Use skopeo to extract a single-platform OCI layout from the multi-platform archive,
then point Syft at the single-platform layout. Fully local, no registry round-trip.

### Pipeline changes (rbgjb step scripts)

**New step script (e.g., rbgjb07b-split-oci-platform.sh):**
- Runs in a pinned skopeo container image
- Official image: quay.io/skopeo/stable — verify it is pullable from Cloud Build
  workers and pinnable by digest before proceeding
- Add RBRR_GCB_SKOPEO_IMAGE_REF to pin regime (rbrr.env + rbrr_regime.sh enrollment)
- Command:
  `skopeo --override-os linux --override-arch amd64 copy oci-archive:/workspace/oci-layout.tar oci:/workspace/oci-amd64`
- Emit subject mapping file (.platform_digests) with platform -> digest entries

**Modified rbgjb08-sbom-and-summary.sh:**
- Point Syft at `oci-dir:/workspace/oci-amd64` instead of `oci-dir:/workspace/oci-layout`
- Label SBOM output with platform: `sbom.linux_amd64.spdx.json`

### Stitch function (zrbf_stitch_build_json)
- Add the new skopeo step to z_step_defs array
- Step numbering will shift — the new step inserts between push-with-crane (07) and
  sbom-and-summary (08). Review all step IDs and cross-step file references.
- The skopeo step needs entrypoint "sh" (alpine-based image, no bash)

### Bake pinned image ref
- The skopeo image ref must be baked into the step script text at stitch time,
  same pattern as RBRR_GCB_SYFT_IMAGE_REF and RBRR_GCB_BINFMT_IMAGE_REF
  (see stitch function lines ~199-200)

### Specs
- Update RBSRI or relevant spec to document SBOM is per-platform (amd64),
  labeled with platform image digest, not the index digest
- Note: per-platform SBOM is honest about scope — doesn't claim to cover
  other platform variants. SLSA provenance requires attestation-to-subject-digest
  correspondence.

### Future work (not this pace)
- Drift detector: periodic check that arm64/armv7 package inventory matches amd64
- BuildKit SBOM attestations (--sbom=true) as architectural alternative
- Per-platform SBOMs if drift is detected

### Regeneration required
- All 7 vessel cloudbuild.json need regeneration after stitch change
- Rubric repo needs re-inscribe

## Acceptance Criteria
- SBOM step succeeds on multi-platform busybox build
- SBOM labeled with platform and platform-specific image digest
- No registry round-trip for SBOM generation
- Skopeo image pinned by digest in RBRR regime
