### fix-iam-policy-declarative-assertions (₢AiABD) [complete]

**[260303-1824] complete**

Fix IAM read-modify-write race: make create_director write complete expected policy.

## Problem

depot_create sets Mason's bindings on GAR repo and secret IAM policies.
create_director later does read-modify-write on the same resources.
If getIamPolicy returns stale data (IAM eventual consistency — 200 but missing
Mason's binding), the setIamPolicy overwrites and destroys Mason's binding.

This is NOT fixable with delays/retries — a 200 with stale data is indistinguishable
from a 200 with fresh data.

## Approach: Complete policy construction

Every setIamPolicy call writes the complete expected binding set. create_director
reads the policy, adds ALL expected bindings (its own AND depot_create's), and writes.
One path, one write, always correct.

## Changes Required

### rbgg_Governor.sh — create_director

**GAR repo IAM** (currently line ~622):
Read the policy. Add both Director repoAdmin AND Mason writer to it.
Mason's email is available via RBGD_MASON_EMAIL (already in scope from rbgd_DepotConstants).
One setIamPolicy with the complete expected policy.

**Secret IAM** (currently line ~592):
Read the policy. Add both Director secretAccessor AND CB service agent secretAccessor.
CB service agent email: `service-{PN}@gcp-sa-cloudbuild.iam.gserviceaccount.com`.
IMPORTANT: create_director currently has RBRR_DEPOT_PROJECT_ID (string) but NOT
the numeric project number needed for the service agent email. Options:
  a) Add RBGD_PROJECT_NUMBER to depot constants (derived from CRM API at depot_create,
     stored alongside RBGD_GCB_PROJECT_ID). Preferred — avoids an extra API call.
  b) Call CRM v3 projects.get to resolve project number at create_director time.
Choose option (a) unless there's a reason the project number shouldn't be stored.

**Implementation detail:**
`rbgu_jq_add_member_to_role_capture` reads from a file and returns JSON on stdout.
To chain two add-member calls, the second call needs the first call's output written
to a file. Simplest approach: write the intermediate result to a temp file, then call
add_member again on that file. Alternatively, extend the jq filter to accept multiple
role+member pairs in one pass — but only if the pattern recurs enough to justify it.

### Specs
- lenses/RBSDI-director_create.adoc: Document that create_director writes the complete
  expected binding set for every IAM policy it touches.
- Paddock: Add session decision on complete-policy-write pattern.

## Acceptance Criteria
- create_director's GAR setIamPolicy includes both Director repoAdmin AND Mason writer
- create_director's secret setIamPolicy includes both Director and CB service agent secretAccessor
- No conditional branches based on what the read returned — one path always
- Specs document the complete-policy-write pattern

**[260303-1719] rough**

Fix IAM read-modify-write race: make create_director assert all expected bindings.

## Problem

`depot_create` sets Mason's bindings on GAR repo and secret IAM policies.
`create_director` later does read-modify-write on the same resources.
If `getIamPolicy` returns stale data (IAM eventual consistency — 200 but missing
Mason's binding), the `setIamPolicy` overwrites and destroys Mason's binding.

This is NOT fixable with delays/retries — a 200 with stale data is indistinguishable
from a 200 with fresh data.

## Approach: Declarative assertion

Every `setIamPolicy` call must assert the complete expected binding set, not just
add its own binding incrementally. When `create_director` modifies a policy, it
positively asserts ALL bindings that should exist on that resource.

## Changes Required

### rbgg_Governor.sh — create_director

**GAR repo IAM** (currently line ~622):
After reading the policy and adding Director `repoAdmin`, also assert Mason `writer`.
Mason's email is available via `RBGD_MASON_EMAIL`. Apply both bindings to the policy
JSON before the single `setIamPolicy` call:
1. `rbgu_jq_add_member_to_role_capture` for Director repoAdmin
2. Run the result through jq again (or a second add_member call) for Mason writer
3. One `setIamPolicy` with the fully-asserted policy

**Secret IAM** (currently line ~592):
After reading the policy and adding Director `secretAccessor`, also assert CB service
agent `secretAccessor`. CB service agent email: `service-{PN}@gcp-sa-cloudbuild.iam.gserviceaccount.com`.
The project number is available from RBGD constants or can be derived.

### Specs
- `lenses/RBSDI-director_create.adoc`: Document that create_director asserts both its
  own bindings AND depot_create's bindings in every IAM policy write. Explain the
  eventual-consistency rationale.
- Paddock: Add session decision on declarative IAM assertion pattern.

### Consider
- Should `rbgu_jq_add_member_to_role_capture` gain a multi-binding variant? Or just
  chain two calls (pipe JSON through jq twice)?
- Should depot_create also assert Mason + CB service agent together in one write?
  (Currently writes them separately — same stale-read risk between the two writes.)

## Acceptance Criteria
- create_director's GAR setIamPolicy includes both Director repoAdmin AND Mason writer
- create_director's secret setIamPolicy includes both Director secretAccessor AND CB service agent secretAccessor
- No IAM binding can be lost to stale reads
- Specs document the declarative assertion pattern

### e2e-verify-cbv2-provenance (₢AiAA0) [abandoned]

**[260303-1814] abandoned**

Guided first-run E2E: depot lifecycle with CB v2 and SLSA v1.0 provenance.

## Prerequisites (must land first)

- ₢AiABC: Remove push filter from triggers (prevents 7-build burst on inscribe)
- ₢AiABD: Declarative IAM policy writes in create_director (prevents binding loss)
- Syft multi-platform resolution: Either fix the SBOM step or disable it for E2E

## Procedure

Full sequential e2e from clean state — destroy existing demo1015 depot and rebuild:

1. Destroy depot demo1015
2. Create depot with CB v2 connection (verifies ₢AiABD fix)
3. Create director + retriever (verifies IAM bindings preserved)
4. Refresh pins
5. Inscribe (verifies ₢AiABC fix — no auto-fired builds)
6. Dispatch busybox build via triggers.run
7. Wait for build success (all steps including SBOM, or SBOM disabled)
8. Query Container Analysis API for SLSA v1.0 provenance on image digest:
   - Confirm inTotoSlsaProvenanceV1 exists
   - Confirm builder.id, source metadata, trigger URI present

GATE: Provenance confirmed → E2E complete.

## Acceptance Criteria

- Busybox build succeeds via triggers.run
- SLSA v1.0 provenance confirmed on produced artifact
- No IAM bindings lost during depot lifecycle
- No auto-fired builds during inscribe
- PAT never appears in logs or transcripts

**[260303-1731] rough**

Guided first-run E2E: depot lifecycle with CB v2 and SLSA v1.0 provenance.

## Prerequisites (must land first)

- ₢AiABC: Remove push filter from triggers (prevents 7-build burst on inscribe)
- ₢AiABD: Declarative IAM policy writes in create_director (prevents binding loss)
- Syft multi-platform resolution: Either fix the SBOM step or disable it for E2E

## Procedure

Full sequential e2e from clean state — destroy existing demo1015 depot and rebuild:

1. Destroy depot demo1015
2. Create depot with CB v2 connection (verifies ₢AiABD fix)
3. Create director + retriever (verifies IAM bindings preserved)
4. Refresh pins
5. Inscribe (verifies ₢AiABC fix — no auto-fired builds)
6. Dispatch busybox build via triggers.run
7. Wait for build success (all steps including SBOM, or SBOM disabled)
8. Query Container Analysis API for SLSA v1.0 provenance on image digest:
   - Confirm inTotoSlsaProvenanceV1 exists
   - Confirm builder.id, source metadata, trigger URI present

GATE: Provenance confirmed → E2E complete.

- SLSA v1.0 provenance confirmed on produced artifact
- No IAM bindings lost during depot lifecycle
- No auto-fired builds during inscribe
- PAT never appears in logs or transcripts

**[260302-1917] rough**

Guided first-run E2E: depot lifecycle with CB v2 and SLSA v1.0 provenance.

This is the FIRST real execution of the CB v2 depot flow. Each phase has
explicit pre-flight checks and operator confirmation gates. Do not batch
steps — complete each phase, verify, then proceed.

## Phase 0: Pre-flight — GitHub prerequisites

Before touching GCP, verify all GitHub-side prerequisites individually:

0a. **GitHub App installed?**
    - Visit https://github.com/apps/google-cloud-build
    - Confirm the Google Cloud Build app is installed on the org
    - Note: this is a DIFFERENT app from Developer Connect
    - Record: org name where app is installed

0b. **Classic PAT exists with correct scopes?**
    - Must be a CLASSIC token (not fine-grained — CB v2 rejects fine-grained)
    - Required scopes: `repo`, `read:user`, `read:org`
    - Test: `curl -s -H "Authorization: token PAT" https://api.github.com/user`
    - Should return your GitHub user JSON (not 401)
    - Record: PAT value (do not log or persist)

0c. **Installation ID known?**
    - GitHub org settings → Installed GitHub Apps → Google Cloud Build → note the numeric ID from the URL
    - Or: `curl -s -H "Authorization: token PAT" https://api.github.com/user/installations`
    - Look for `app_slug: "google-cloud-build"`, record `id` field
    - Record: numeric installation ID

0d. **Rubric repo exists and PAT can access it?**
    - Check `RBRR_RUBRIC_REPO_URL` is set in rbrr.env (plain HTTPS, no credentials)
    - Test: `git ls-remote https://x-access-token:PAT@github.com/org/repo.git HEAD`
    - Should return a commit hash (not 403/404)

0e. **Regime validation passes?**
    - Run: `./tt/rbw-rrv.ValidateRepoRegime.sh`
    - All regime vars required by depot_create must be present

GATE: All 5 checks pass → proceed to Phase 1.

## Phase 1: Create depot with CB v2

Run: `printf '%s\n%s\n' "$PAT" "$INSTALL_ID" | ./tt/rbw-Pcd.PayorCreatesDepot.sh <name>`

Verify each resource individually after creation:
1a. Depot project exists and is ACTIVE
1b. Secret Manager secret exists (contains PAT)
1c. CB v2 connection reaches COMPLETE state
1d. CB v2 repository exists and references RBRR_RUBRIC_REPO_URL
1e. All expected APIs enabled on depot project

If depot_create fails partway: check log, identify which step failed,
decide whether to destroy and retry or fix forward.

GATE: All 5 verifications pass → proceed to Phase 2.

## Phase 2: Governor and Director setup

2a. Run: `./tt/rbw-Prg.PayorResetsGovernor.sh`
2b. Run: `./tt/rbw-GD.GovernorCreatesDirector.sh`
    - Verify: Director SA has `roles/secretmanager.secretAccessor` on PAT secret
2c. Run: `./tt/rbw-GR.GovernorCreatesRetriever.sh`

GATE: Director SA can access secret → proceed to Phase 3.

## Phase 3: Pin refresh + Inscribe

3a. Run: `./tt/rbw-DP.DirectorRefreshesPins.sh`
    - Verify: `RBRR_GCB_PINS_REFRESHED_AT` updated in rbrr.env
3b. Run: `./tt/rbw-DI.DirectorInscribesRubric.sh`
    - Verify: PAT fetched from Secret Manager (check logs — no RBRA reference)
    - Verify: rubric repo has per-vessel directories with cloudbuild.json
    - Verify: triggers created with CB v2 repository references

GATE: Inscribe succeeds, triggers exist → proceed to Phase 4.

## Phase 4: Dispatch and provenance

4a. Dispatch busybox build: appropriate tabtarget or manual triggers.run
4b. Wait for build completion (poll or check Cloud Console)
4c. Query Container Analysis API for SLSA v1.0 provenance on image digest
    - Confirm `inTotoSlsaProvenanceV1` exists
    - Confirm builder.id, source metadata, trigger URI present

GATE: Provenance confirmed → E2E complete.

## Phase 5: Full fleet verification

5a. Verify all 7 vessels inscribed (triggers exist for each)
5b. Optionally dispatch additional vessels beyond busybox

## Acceptance Criteria

- Busybox build succeeds via triggers.run

- Rubric repo exists on GitHub

## Full Sequential E2E

1. **Destroy** existing depot (if any) — `depot_destroy`
2. **Create** depot with CB v2 — `depot_create` with PAT + installation ID via stdin
   - Verify: Secret Manager secret exists, CB v2 connection COMPLETE, CB v2 repository exists
3. **Update** rbrr.env with output values (`RBRR_CBV2_CONNECTION_NAME`)
4. **Create** Governor and Director — `governor_reset`, `create_director`
   - Verify: Director SA has `secretAccessor` on PAT secret
5. **Refresh** pins — verify `RBRR_GCB_PINS_REFRESHED_AT` current

   - PAT fetched from Secret Manager (not from any RBRA file)
   - Rubric repo updated with per-vessel directories
   - All triggers created with CB v2 repository references
7. **Dispatch** busybox build via `triggers.run` + RepoSource
8. **Wait** for build success
9. **Verify SLSA v1.0 provenance** on produced artifact:
   - Query Container Analysis API for occurrences on image digest
   - Confirm `inTotoSlsaProvenanceV1` exists
   - Confirm builder.id, source metadata, trigger URI present
   - Compare with Google provenance guide expectations

The provenance check is the critical gate. If SLSA v1.0 provenance is NOT
generated for the trigger-invoked build, the entire Tier 2 value proposition
fails and we need to escalate.

### migrate-rubric-repo-github-to-gitlab (₢AiAA5) [complete]

**[260303-1250] complete**

Migrate rubric repo infrastructure from GitHub to GitLab.

## Status: Code migration complete, UX remaining

All code and spec changes for the GitHub→GitLab migration are committed
(uncommitted in working tree, ready to notch). What remains is UX:
manual guide, error message improvements, and E2E verification.

### Already done (in working tree)

- **rbgc_Constants.sh**: `RBGC_CBV2_PAT_SECRET_NAME` replaced with 3 GitLab
  secret constants (`RBGC_CBV2_API_TOKEN_SECRET_NAME`, `RBGC_CBV2_READ_TOKEN_SECRET_NAME`,
  `RBGC_CBV2_WEBHOOK_SECRET_NAME`) + `RBGC_CBV2_CONNECTION_SUFFIX="-gitlab"`
- **rbgp_Payor.sh depot_create**: gitlab.com URL gate, single token stdin,
  bash builtin URL construction (no sed), 3 unrolled secret creation + IAM
  (BCG compliant — no loops, no local-in-loop, no word-splitting), gitlabConfig
  connection body, GitLab-specific polling diagnostics, stderr captured to
  temp files (no 2>/dev/null), uuidgen via temp file (no pipeline)
- **rbgp_Payor.sh depot_destroy**: 3 unrolled secret deletions
- **rbf_Foundry.sh inscribe + build**: `RBGC_CBV2_API_TOKEN_SECRET_NAME`,
  `oauth2:TOKEN@` URL (bash builtin), `repositoryType: "GITLAB"`,
  host-agnostic repo path extraction
- **rbgg_Governor.sh**: Director secret reference → api token secret
- **Specs**: RBSDC (full rewrite), RBS0 (rubric repo, CBv2 connection, URL
  example, check function), RBSRI (inscribe precondition + fetch step),
  RBSDI (director secret reference), RBSRR (URL requirement)

### Remaining: Manual guide and UX

#### 1. Create `rbgm_gitlab_setup()` manual guide

New function in rbgm_ManualProcedures.sh using bug_* pattern (always-visible,
colored, clickable links — like rbgm_payor_establish). This guide is the
right place for the full story.

Content:
- Why GitLab, not GitHub (PAT scope problem, Google Issue Tracker #343223837,
  fine-grained PAT rejection by CB v2, machine account overhead)
- Key differences table (from paddock)
- GitLab account creation (if needed)
- GitLab project creation for rubric repo
- Initialize repo (README so it's not empty)
- Set `RBRR_RUBRIC_REPO_URL` in rbrr.env
- Project access token creation walkthrough:
  Project Settings → Access Tokens → Add new token
  - Name: descriptive (e.g. 'rb-depot')
  - Role: Maintainer
  - Scopes: api (includes read_api)
  - Create → copy immediately
- End with `buc_next "rbw-PC"` pointing to depot_create

Two colophons minted:
- `rbw-Pgl` — the guide display function
- `rbw-Pge` — TBD (user specified, needs clarification on purpose)

#### 2. Tabtarget + zipper enrollment

- Create `tt/rbw-Pgl.PayorGitlabSetupGuide.sh` (standard launcher)
- Enroll in rbz_zipper.sh: `buz_enroll RBZ_GITLAB_SETUP "rbw-Pgl" ...`
- Create `tt/rbw-Pge.PayorGitlabEstablish.sh` if needed
- Enroll in rbz_zipper.sh if needed

#### 3. Simplify depot_create inline guide

Remove the verbose inline guide text from depot_create. Replace with terse:
- "Paste GitLab project access token:" / read / validate
- No tutorial text — the guide covers that

#### 4. Improve depot_create error UX

When RBRR_RUBRIC_REPO_URL is missing or not gitlab.com:
```bash
buc_warn "RBRR_RUBRIC_REPO_URL is not set or is not a gitlab.com URL"
buc_info "Set up a GitLab rubric repo first:"
buc_next "rbw-Pgl"
buc_die "Cannot proceed without GitLab rubric repo"
```

The `buc_next` resolves the colophon to the tabtarget filename via ls glob,
so the user sees the exact command to run.

#### 5. Update RBSDC spec

Update depot_create spec to reflect simplified stdin flow (no inline guide)
and the `buc_next` error pattern pointing to the manual guide.

#### 6. E2E verification

- Run guide, verify display
- Run depot_create with GitLab rubric repo, verify end to end
- Run depot_destroy, verify 3 secrets cleaned up

- Manual guide displays correctly with bug_* formatting
- depot_create error shows tabtarget for guide via buc_next

**[260303-1146] rough**

Migrate rubric repo infrastructure from GitHub to GitLab.

## Motivation

GitHub classic PATs (required by CB v2 githubConfig) grant `repo` scope
across ALL repositories the token owner can access. Fine-grained PATs are
not supported by CB v2 (Google Issue Tracker #343223837). A machine account
mitigates but adds 9-step identity management overhead.

GitLab project access tokens are inherently repository-scoped — they cannot
access resources outside the associated project. This eliminates the PAT
scope problem entirely with 3 setup steps.

## CB v2 gitlabConfig REST API shape

```json
POST cloudbuild.googleapis.com/v2/projects/{P}/locations/{R}/connections?connectionId={ID}
{
  "gitlabConfig": {
    "authorizerCredential": {
      "userTokenSecretVersion": "projects/P/secrets/S1/versions/1"
    },
    "readAuthorizerCredential": {
      "userTokenSecretVersion": "projects/P/secrets/S2/versions/1"
    },
    "webhookSecretSecretVersion": "projects/P/secrets/S3/versions/1"
  }
}
```

- `hostUri` omitted → defaults to `https://gitlab.com`
- `authorizerCredential`: project access token with `api` scope
- `readAuthorizerCredential`: project access token with `read_api` scope
- `webhookSecretSecretVersion`: random UUID, immutable, auto-generated by depot_create

**Simplification**: A single GitLab project access token with `api` scope
implicitly includes `read_api`. Store same token in both credential secrets.
Webhook secret is auto-generated (random UUID → Secret Manager). Operator
provides ONE value via stdin (the project access token).

## Key differences from GitHub

| Aspect | GitHub (dying) | GitLab (new) |
|---|---|---|
| Tokens from operator | 2 (PAT + installation ID) | 1 (project access token) |
| Secrets in SM | 1 | 3 (api, read_api, webhook) |
| Webhook secret | Not needed | Required, auto-generated UUID |
| App installation | GitHub App required | No app needed |
| Token scope | `repo` (ALL repos) | `api` (one project only) |
| Auth git URL | `https://x-access-token:PAT@github.com/...` | `https://oauth2:TOKEN@gitlab.com/...` |
| Connection name suffix | `-github` | `-gitlab` |

## Scope

### Kill GitHub rubric support
- Remove `githubConfig` connection creation from rbgp_Payor.sh depot_create
- Remove GitHub App installation ID from stdin flow
- Remove github.com URL gate from depot_create
- Remove GitHub-specific variable names and comments

### Implement GitLab rubric support
- CB v2 connection body: `gitlabConfig` with three Secret Manager secrets
  (api token, read_api token using same value, webhook UUID auto-generated)
- Stdin flow: read one value (GitLab project access token)
- URL gate: require gitlab.com in RBRR_RUBRIC_REPO_URL
- Generate webhook secret: `uuidgen | tr -d '\n'` → store in Secret Manager
- Update depot_destroy to clean up GitLab-flavored CB v2 resources (3 secrets)

### Update inline guide in depot_create
- Terse GitLab account setup (create account, create project)
- Detailed project access token creation:
  Project Settings → Access Tokens → Add new token
  - Name: descriptive (e.g. 'rb-depot')
  - Role: Maintainer
  - Scopes: api (includes read_api)
  - Create → copy immediately
- Explanation of why GitHub is not acceptable (PAT scope problem)
- Updated invocation pattern (single token via stdin)

### Update specs
- RBSDC-depot_create.adoc: new stdin parameter (one token), gitlabConfig,
  guide text, webhook secret auto-generation
- RBS0-SpecTop.adoc: rbtgr_rubric_repo definition → GitLab, with rationale
- RBS0-SpecTop.adoc: rbrr_rubric_repo_url example → gitlab.com URL
- RBS0-SpecTop.adoc: introductory material explaining GitLab choice

### Update inscribe (rbf_Foundry.sh)
- Authenticated git URL: `https://oauth2:TOKEN@gitlab.com/org/repo.git`
- PAT fetch from Secret Manager — same pattern, different URL scheme

### Update constants (rbgc_Constants.sh)
- RBGC_CBV2_PAT_SECRET_NAME → split into or rename for GitLab:
  api token secret, read_api token secret, webhook secret
- Connection name suffix: `-gitlab` instead of `-github`

### Update depot_destroy
- Delete 3 secrets (api, read_api, webhook) instead of 1

## Acceptance criteria
- depot_create with GitLab rubric repo succeeds end to end
- No GitHub references remain in rubric repo code path
- Inline guide shows GitLab setup steps with rationale
- RBS0 explains the GitLab choice
- Inscribe fetches token from Secret Manager and pushes to GitLab

## Motivation

across ALL repositories the token owner can access. Fine-grained PATs are

### private-pool-depot-lifecycle (₢AiAAe) [abandoned]

**[260303-1814] abandoned**

Add Private Pool creation and deletion to the depot lifecycle.

## Regime variable

Add `RBRR_GCB_PRIVATE_POOL_NAME` to regime (optional, 0-64 chars).
Empty means default pool (no private pool). When set, depot_create
creates the pool and depot_destroy deletes it.

## Constants

Add `RBGC_API_WORKER_POOLS` endpoint template to rbgc_Constants.sh.
Format: `projects/{project}/locations/{region}/workerPools/{pool}`

## depot_create

After API enablement, if RBRR_GCB_PRIVATE_POOL_NAME is non-empty:
- POST to workerPools API to create the pool
- Use e2 machine config from RBRR_GCB_MACHINE_TYPE
- Pool scales to zero (no idle cost)
- Idempotent: skip if pool already exists (409 CONFLICT = success)

## depot_destroy

Before project deletion, if RBRR_GCB_PRIVATE_POOL_NAME is non-empty:
- DELETE the worker pool
- Tolerate 404 (already gone)

## Quota check

rbgd_DepotConstants.sh currently checks `concurrent_public_pool_build_cpus`.
When private pool is configured, check `concurrent_private_pool_build_cpus`
instead. The metric name changes based on pool type.

## Files

- Tools/rbw/rbrr_regime.sh — add optional enrollment
- Tools/rbw/rbrr.env — add variable with comment
- Tools/rbw/rbgp_Payor.sh — pool create in depot_create, pool delete in depot_destroy
- Tools/rbw/rbgc_Constants.sh — API endpoint constant
- Tools/rbw/rbgd_DepotConstants.sh — conditional quota metric
- lenses/RBSDC-depot_create.adoc — document pool creation step
- lenses/RBSDD-depot_destroy.adoc — document pool deletion step

## References

- Cloud Build workerPools API: https://cloud.google.com/build/docs/api/reference/rest/v1/projects.locations.workerPools
- RBSCB Tier 3 section in lenses/RBSCB-CloudBuildRoadmap.adoc
## Code Standards

All new bash code must be BCG-compliant (Tools/buk/vov_veiled/BCG-BashConsoleGuide.md).
Enterprise-grade orchestration patterns: buc_step/buc_info/buc_die for user interaction,
z-prefixed locals, proper error handling, no bare echo.

Empty means default pool (no private pool). When set, depot_create
creates the pool and depot_destroy deletes it.

Format: `projects/{project}/locations/{region}/workerPools/{pool}`

### fix-depot-create-timestamp-smell (₢AiAAk) [complete]

**[260302-0731] complete**

Depot create generates its project ID timestamp via a second `date` call
(rbgp_Payor.sh line 602-603) instead of using the dispatch-provided
`BURD_NOW_STAMP` or `BURD_NOW_EPOCH`. This causes a 1-second skew between
the tabtarget log filename and the GCP project ID, making it impossible to
reliably derive the project ID from the log timestamp.

## Fix

Replace the independent `date` call in `zrbgp_depot_create()` with the
dispatch timestamp `BURD_NOW_STAMP` (or derive the needed format from
`BURD_NOW_EPOCH`). Verify that `RBGC_GLOBAL_TIMESTAMP_FORMAT` is
compatible with the dispatch timestamp format; adapt if needed.

## Also check

- `zrbgp_governor_reset()` (line 1158-1159) has the same pattern —
  independent `date +%Y%m%d%H%M` for Governor account ID. Consider
  whether this should also use the dispatch timestamp.
- The bucket name at line 673 reuses `z_timestamp` from the same
  independent call, so fixing the project ID also fixes the bucket.

## Acceptance

- Project ID timestamp matches tabtarget log filename timestamp
- No independent `date` calls for resource naming in depot_create
- Governor reset evaluated and fixed if applicable
## Code Standards

All modified bash code must be BCG-compliant (Tools/buk/vov_veiled/BCG-BashConsoleGuide.md).
Enterprise-grade orchestration patterns: z-prefixed locals, proper error handling.

### sanitize-secrets-from-transcripts (₢AiAAl) [complete]

**[260303-1837] complete**

Audit and sanitize secrets from BUK transcripts and logs.

## Reduced Scope (2026-03-02)

The PAT-on-disk problem is largely eliminated by the CB v2 architecture:
- PAT never stored in RBRA files (only in Secret Manager)
- RBRR_RUBRIC_REPO_URL is a plain URL (no credentials)
- PAT fetched at runtime, used in memory, discarded

Remaining concern: **OAuth bearer tokens in HTTP logging.**

## Audit

1. **rbgu_Utility.sh**: Check if `rbgu_http_json` or related functions log
   the Authorization header or bearer token to transcript/log files.

2. **rbf_Foundry.sh**: Check inscribe HTTP calls — does the OAuth token
   appear in buc_log_args output or curl verbose logging?

3. **rbgp_Payor.sh**: Check depot_create HTTP calls — same audit.

4. **rbgg_Governor.sh**: Check governor HTTP calls — same audit.

5. **Secret Manager GET response**: When inscribe fetches the PAT from
   Secret Manager, does the response body (containing the PAT) get logged?

## Fix

If bearer tokens or PAT values appear in logs:
- Redact at the HTTP utility layer (mask Authorization header values)
- Ensure Secret Manager response bodies are not logged
- Option: `buc_log_args` redaction for known secret patterns

## Acceptance Criteria

- No bearer tokens in transcript files after a full inscribe run
- No PAT values in transcript files after Secret Manager fetch
- Validated by grep on transcript after an inscribe + build cycle
## Code Standards

All new or modified bash code must be BCG-compliant (Tools/buk/vov_veiled/BCG-BashConsoleGuide.md).
If adding redaction utilities, follow buc_* function naming and z-prefixed locals.

**[260302-0715] rough**

Audit and sanitize secrets from BUK transcripts and logs.

## Reduced Scope (2026-03-02)

   Secret Manager, does the response body (containing the PAT) get logged?

## Fix

If bearer tokens or PAT values appear in logs:
- Redact at the HTTP utility layer (mask Authorization header values)
- Ensure Secret Manager response bodies are not logged
- Option: `buc_log_args` redaction for known secret patterns

## Acceptance Criteria

- No bearer tokens in transcript files after a full inscribe run
- No PAT values in transcript files after Secret Manager fetch
- Validated by grep on transcript after an inscribe + build cycle

**[260227-1527] rough**

BUK transcripts capture all buc_log_args output verbatim. Commands that
handle RBRA files (depot_initialize, rubric_preflight, inscribe) may log
secret-bearing values like RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL (contains embedded PAT)
or RBRA_PRIVATE_KEY fragments.

## Problem

The transcript at BURD_TRANSCRIPT and the log files at BURD_LOG_HIST
persist after command completion. Any buc_log_args call that includes
a secret value writes it to disk in plaintext.

## Fix

Identify all code paths where secret-bearing RBRA values pass through
logging. Options:

1. **Redaction at log time**: A buc utility that masks known secret
   patterns (PATs, private keys, authenticated URLs) before writing
   to transcript. E.g., `https://x-access-token:ghp_****@github.com/...`

2. **Caller discipline**: Ensure callers never pass raw secret values
   to buc_log_args — log only the non-secret portion (e.g., repo URL
   without the credential).

3. **Transcript cleanup**: Scrub transcripts on command completion.

Evaluate which approach fits BCG patterns best. Option 2 is simplest
but relies on every caller getting it right. Option 1 is more robust.

## Scope

- Audit rbgm_ManualProcedures.sh (depot_initialize)
- Audit rbgu_Utility.sh (rbra_load, http calls with auth tokens)
- Audit rbf_Foundry.sh (inscribe path)
- Check if OAuth bearer tokens appear in HTTP logging

## Acceptance

- No PATs, private keys, or bearer tokens in transcript files
- Validated by grep on transcript after a depot_initialize run

Zero substitution overrides — all values baked in {rbtgr_build_json}.
Verify build completes successfully.

- {rbtgr_provenance} present on built image (SLSA v1.0 attestation)

- Multiple builds of same inscribed JSON produce distinct but related tags

- No custom substitution overrides recorded

### implement-rubric-inscribe (₢AiAAT) [abandoned]

**[260223-1820] abandoned**

Implement {rbtgo_rubric_inscribe} as a reusable Foundry function that generates
cloudbuild.yaml for any vessel from step scripts + regime pins.

## What it does

Reads the rbgjb/*.sh step script bodies, current RBRR_GCB_*_IMAGE_REF pins,
vessel configuration (RBRV_*), and emits a static cloudbuild.yaml for that vessel.
This is the refactored generator from zrbf_stitch_build_json() — same logic,
YAML output instead of JSON build request.

## Inputs
- Vessel directory (contains rbrv.env with vessel config)
- rbgjb/*.sh step scripts (inline into YAML step blocks)
- Current regime pins from rbrr.env (baked into YAML)
- Constants from rbgc_Constants.sh (GAR host suffix, ark suffixes)

## Output
- A valid cloudbuild.yaml written to the vessel directory
- Idempotent: running twice with same inputs produces identical output

## Design constraints
- Must produce byte-identical output for same inputs (deterministic)
- Determinism enables {rbtgo_rubric_assay} (diff committed vs regenerated)
- BCG compliance for all scripting
- No gcloud/gh CLI dependency — pure bash generation

## Why now
- ₢AiAAD authored busybox yaml by hand — this generalizes the pattern
- ₢AiAAQ (pin-refresh integration) needs this to regenerate all vessel yamls
- ₢AiAAM (migrate remaining vessels) needs this to inscribe each vessel's rubric
- Without this, each vessel migration is manual yaml authoring

## References
- Tools/rbw/rbf_Foundry.sh — zrbf_stitch_build_json() (source logic)
- Tools/rbw/rbgjb/*.sh — step script bodies
- rbev-vessels/rbev-busybox/cloudbuild.yaml — reference output (₢AiAAD)

- Pin update and {rbtgr_build_yaml} update become a single atomic commit

the {rbtgr_rubric} stays in sync with regime pins automatically.

### auto-populate-rubric-url-in-rbra (₢AiAAr) [abandoned]

**[260302-0713] abandoned**

Auto-populate RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL during SA creation flows.

## Problem

When Governor creates a Director (or resets itself), the generated RBRA file
contains only SA credentials. The operator must manually append
RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL to both Governor and Director RBRA files. This is
error-prone and caused a block during e2e testing (₢AiAAo).

## Proposed Changes

1. **Director creation** (`rbgg_create_director`): Governor already has the
   rubric URL in its own RBRA. After writing the Director RBRA file, append
   RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL from the Governor's environment.

2. **Governor reset** (`rbgp_governor_reset`): Consider whether the rubric URL
   should be preserved across resets. The Payor doesn't have it, but the
   outgoing Governor RBRA does. May need a "carry forward" or prompt.

3. **Validation**: Add a post-write validation step that sources the new RBRA
   and confirms RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL is present and reachable (git ls-remote)
   before declaring success.

## Design Questions

- Should RBRA files carry installation context beyond SA credentials?
- Should Governor reset preserve rubric URL from the previous Governor RBRA?
- Should depot_initialize auto-append to Governor RBRA instead of requiring
  manual edit?

**[260301-1136] rough**

Auto-populate RBRA_RUBRIC_REPO_URL during SA creation flows.

## Problem

   outgoing Governor RBRA does. May need a "carry forward" or prompt.

- Should depot_initialize auto-append to Governor RBRA instead of requiring
  manual edit?

### partition-zipper-kindle-from-healthcheck (₢AiAA1) [complete]

**[260302-1940] complete**

Partition the zipper kindle sequence so that buz_enroll registrations
(colophon constant definitions) can be sourced without triggering the
full tabtarget health check.

## Problem

The zipper is the single point of definition for colophon strings, but
modules outside the dispatch path (error messages in rbf_Foundry.sh,
rbob_bottle.sh, workbench qualification gates, test cases) cannot easily
source the zipper because kindling pulls in the full tabtarget health
check. This forces them to hardcode colophon strings as literals,
defeating single-point-of-definition.

## Approach

Split zrbz_kindle() into two functions:
- zrbz_kindle() — performs buz_enroll registrations only (lightweight,
  establishes colophon constants). Requires buz_zipper sourced and kindled.
- zrbz_healthcheck() — validates that enrolled tabtarget files exist on
  disk and other integrity checks. Called by the workbench dispatch path.

Modules that need colophon constants add the zipper to their furnish
chain and call zrbz_kindle(). The workbench additionally calls
zrbz_healthcheck() before dispatch.

## Then update consumers

Replace hardcoded colophon string literals with references to the
enrolled constants:
- rbf_Foundry.sh error message referencing rbw-DP
- rbob_bottle.sh error messages referencing rbw-DS
- rbw_workbench.sh qualification gate case pattern

## Acceptance

- Zipper kindle works without tabtarget health check
- Workbench dispatch still runs health check before routing
- No hardcoded colophon strings in rbf_Foundry.sh, rbob_bottle.sh,
  rbw_workbench.sh
- Existing dispatch behavior unchanged

**[260301-1540] rough**

Partition the zipper kindle sequence so that buz_enroll registrations

### replace-hardcoded-colophons-in-cli-consumers (₢AiAA3) [complete]

**[260303-1250] complete**

Replace hardcoded colophon string literals in CLI consumer modules with
zipper-enrolled constants.

## Prerequisite

₢AiAA1 (partition-zipper-kindle-from-healthcheck) must be complete —
buz_enroll no longer validates tabtargets, so CLI modules can kindle
the zipper cheaply.

## Changes

### Add zipper to CLI furnish chains

Both rbf_cli.sh and rbob_cli.sh need to source and kindle the zipper
so their implementation modules can reference colophon constants:

- Source `buz_zipper.sh` and `rbz_zipper.sh`
- Call `zbuz_kindle` and `zrbz_kindle` in furnish (NO healthcheck —
  these are dispatched modules, not the workbench)

### Replace hardcoded strings

**rbf_Foundry.sh** (line ~978):
- `"run ./tt/rbw-DP.DirectorRefreshesPins.sh"` → use `${RBZ_REFRESH_GCB_PINS}`
- The error message tells the operator what tabtarget to run; the colophon
  is sufficient for tab-completion (`./tt/rbw-DP<TAB>`)

**rbob_bottle.sh** (lines ~312, ~316):
- `"tt/rbw-DS.DirectorSummonsArk.sh"` → use `${RBZ_SUMMON_ARK}`
- Same rationale: colophon is sufficient for tab-completion

### Error message format decision

The old messages included full tabtarget paths (colophon + frontispiece).
The colophon constant only provides the colophon portion. Options:
1. Use colophon only: `"run ./tt/${RBZ_REFRESH_GCB_PINS}.<TAB>"`
2. Use colophon in message: `"run tabtarget ${RBZ_REFRESH_GCB_PINS}"`
3. Keep full path but construct from constant (not possible without frontispiece)

Recommend option 2 — cleanest single-point-of-definition.

## Acceptance

- No hardcoded colophon string literals in rbf_Foundry.sh or rbob_bottle.sh
- All existing tests still pass (same 5/11 fixture pass rate)
- Error messages still guide operator to correct tabtarget

**[260302-1937] rough**

Replace hardcoded colophon string literals in CLI consumer modules with

## Prerequisite

### extract-sa-email-magic-strings (₢AiAA8) [complete]

**[260303-1852] complete**

Extract SA domain suffix and email composition magic strings into constants/helper.

## What

Two changes:
1. Add `RBGC_IAM_SA_DOMAIN="iam.gserviceaccount.com"` kindle constant to `rbgc_Constants.sh`
2. Add `rbgu_sa_email_capture()` helper to `rbgu_Utility.sh` that composes `${name}@${project}.${RBGC_IAM_SA_DOMAIN}`

Then replace all inline occurrences of `.iam.gserviceaccount.com` SA email construction across the depot call chain with the helper.

## Target files

- `Tools/rbw/rbgc_Constants.sh` — new kindle constant
- `Tools/rbw/rbgu_Utility.sh` — new helper function
- `Tools/rbw/rbgp_Payor.sh` — consumer
- `Tools/rbw/rbgi_IAM.sh` — consumer
- `Tools/rbw/rbgg_Governor.sh` — consumer (likely)

## Out of scope

- Path segment constants (`/projects/`, `/serviceAccounts/`) — readability tradeoff not justified
- URL builder functions — inline URLs remain more readable

## Acceptance criteria

- Zero inline `.iam.gserviceaccount.com` strings outside the new constant
- All SA email construction uses the helper
- No behavioral change

### audit-mason-tokencreator-grant-purpose (₢AiABA) [complete]

**[260303-1903] complete**

Audit the tokenCreator grant on Mason SA to the CB service agent.

Line ~812 in rbgp_Payor.sh:
  rbgi_add_sa_iam_role "${z_token}" "${z_mason_sa_email}" "${z_cb_service_agent}" "roles/iam.serviceAccountTokenCreator"

This grants tokenCreator on Mason TO the CB service agent, enabling CB to
impersonate Mason during builds. This is separate from the impersonation
readiness gate (which tested Payor→CB SA impersonation).

## Questions to resolve

1. Is this grant actually used at build time? (Does cloudbuild.yaml or
   any build step require CB to call generateAccessToken on Mason?)
2. Or does CB use Mason via actAs (serviceAccountUser) which is granted
   elsewhere?
3. If tokenCreator is not needed for builds, remove it (principle of
   least privilege).
4. If it IS needed, document why in RBSDC.

## Files
- Tools/rbw/rbgp_Payor.sh — the grant
- Tools/rbw/rbgjb/ — build step scripts (do they reference Mason impersonation?)
- lenses/RBSDC-depot_create.adoc — document finding

### align-rbsrc-detail-with-rbsdi (₢AiABB) [complete]

**[260303-1925] complete**

RBSRC-retriever_create.adoc is a high-level summary with no step-by-step
operations, while RBSDI-director_create.adoc has detailed steps including
SA creation, key generation, propagation verification, and role grants.

Both follow the same pattern (Governor creates a role SA with key + RBRA)
and should be specified at the same level of detail.

Options:
1. Flesh out RBSRC to match RBSDI's step-by-step detail
2. Extract shared steps into a common pattern/template and have both
   documents reference it

Also update RBSRC SA verification step to include poll-with-backoff
language matching the RBSDI fix from ₢AiAA0.

- lenses/RBSRC-retriever_create.adoc
- lenses/RBSDI-director_create.adoc (reference for pattern)

- Both specs describe operations at the same level of detail
- SA propagation verification documented with poll/backoff in both
